# The Book of Ezra {.heading_18-0}

## Introduction {#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA151.xhtml_I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3387 .heading_158}

The book of Ezra has 10 chapters, 280 verses, and 7,441 words in the [Authorized Holy Bible]{.class_3429} (1611). It was written somewhere around 450--444 B.C. and begins its narrative about fifty-two years into the seventy-year Babylonian captivity of Judah (Ezra 1:1). Persia has replaced the Babylonian Empire, and the Persian king (Cyrus) is now ["king of Babylon"]{.class_3428} (Ezra 5:13).

The book deals with the partial fulfillment of the promises in Jeremiah 30:10; Deuteronomy 30:1--5; and 1 Kings 8:47--49 about the restoration of Israel, after its captivity. The "catch," of course (which unseats all Catholic theologians, all Moslems, and all postmillennial Protestants) is the fact that Ezra and Nehemiah do not COMPLETELY fulfill Deuteronomy 30 or Jeremiah 30 or 1 Kings 8 because Isaiah 11:11 puts a stumbling block right in front of their efforts to rid themselves of Israel permanently (see Jer. 33:20--26) and replace that nation with 1. 1:1 Now in the first year of Cyrus king of Persia, that the word of the LORD by the mouth of Jeremiah might be fulfilled, the LORD stirred up the spirit of Cyrus king of Persia, that he made a proclamation throughout all his kingdom, and put it also in writing, saying,

2 Thus saith Cyrus king of Persia, The LORD God of heaven hath given me all the kingdoms of the earth; and he hath charged me to build him an house at Jerusalem, which is in Judah.

3 Who is there among you of all his people? his God be with him, and let him go up to Jerusalem, which is in Judah, and build the house of the LORD God of Israel, (he is the God,) which is in Jerusalem.

4 And whosoever remaineth in any place where he sojourneth, let the men of his place help him with silver, and with gold, and with goods, and with beasts, beside the freewill offering for the house of God that is in Jerusalem.

The animal described for Persia is an English "Griffin"---[a winged-lion.]{.class_3429}

According to Proverbs 21:1, this decree originates in a king's heart while he is asleep (Job 4:13), and it is the Lord who "lays it on his heart." This was done to fulfill Isaiah 45:1, which see. All kings' decrees in ancient times were considered to be of divine origin (Jer. 25:11, 29:10; Dan. 9:1--2).

America []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA684.xhtml_page_91}needs children like they raised like it needs Howard Stern and Madonna.

One of the half-men was trying to make Mickey install a different water system which would only cost him about \$20,000. I was not close enough to hear what he said to the jerk, but the jerk laughed and said something insulting back. Mickey said, "I'm tired of you folks. Git off my property." The jerk laughed and ignored him. Mickey said, "You get outta here, or I'm agonna throw you out!" The jerk just grinned, although he did twitch this time. "Don't you smile," yelled Mickey, "You see that ditch right there? If you smile again you are going to be in that ditch in ten seconds up to your neck in mud!"

The smiling stopped. And the kid left with his miniskirted black female.

The next day they returned with a patrolman. He found his patrol car was blocked by another car when he got to the entrance of the camp. Mickey Carter's brother had parked it, and he was there with his cowboy hat on; sittin' and lookin' at em'.

Now, at the time Mickey Carter's brother was the next to the fastest (if not THE fastest) "draw" in the North, South, East, and West. I mean that literally: special made holster, homemade bullets, the whole works. I have seem him split a 38 shell on an axe blade at twenty feet. I have seen him hit a target behind his back (no bigger than a golf ball) using a mirror. I have stood in front of him and tried to clap my hands before he put a pistol muzzle right on my nose, and couldn't do it when he had to draw the pistol from its holster and raise it to my nose. Every time my hands came together they were on either side of the chamber of a Colt 38.

Well, I don't know if Smokey knew the Carter boy had another pistol up in his hat (!), but he did. I saw it after Smokey took his two greenhorns back to town. Smokey was a little "smoked" (the word "Ham" means "burnt with heat"), for he was an Afro-American. Not only was the "fastest draw in the West" a problem, it had been raining, and the whole landscape was soaking wet. This mud road went a quarter of a mile before it got on any gravel. "Smokey" opted to drive back to town with his "load."

To make a long story short, this last encounter produced a "face []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA684.xhtml_page_92}off" in Lake City with the State Attorney, a congressman from Washington, D.C., and a senator from Washington, D.C. Then a large "butchy" looking, bobbed-hair, overweight, middle-aged woman from the HEW entered with her two "sheep" trailing her: the jerk who nearly had taken a mud bath and the black hipster who claimed Carter's camp was guilty of "child abuse."

I went along for the ride.

After twenty minutes of messing around I turned to this non-lady who was trying to act like a lady (she could have whipped any three men in the room) and said, "That girl you sent said that they might be guilty of child abuse. Why did she say that?" The darkie quickly said, "Well, that is, I meant 'child neglect.'" "You didn't say child neglect," I said, "You said child ABUSE. I heard you say it. I heard you say it twice."

"Well," said the female linebacker, "she MEANT child neglect."

I looked her right square in the kisser---you have never met the woman who could intimidate Peter Ruckman, and it has been tried more than twice---and said, "Isn't it about time you people learned to say what YOU MEAN since you are messing with everyone's private affairs?"

Well, that's where the fur hit the fan; that is what "tied the rag on the bush."

About eight people lost their composure, including the congressman, and in the midst of a twentieth-century Babel, the bureaucratic "female" was able to out yell the rest and screamed, "What business is it of yours if you don't even live here and it's not your camp we're discussing! You're just a traveling evangelist!"

It got quiet, and I pulled my chair a little closer to hers to make sure she would get the message and said, "Listen sister. You people are hurting my income. I've got a right to make an honest living. I preach in these Christian camps all summer long and sometimes in the winter. I preach to teenagers in Memphis, Tennessee; Holland, Michigan; Cincinnati, Ohio; Keystone Heights, Florida; Hume Lake, California; San Antonio, Texas; Dayton, Ohio, and here and there\...."

It got so quiet in that room you could hear a twelve-inch electric fan hummin' on the window sill.

So I raised my voice and said, "...and everywhere I go I run into []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA684.xhtml_page_93}you people. I have run into characters like you all over this country trying to shut down Christian camps for young people, and I get my OFFERINGS from these camps! I have five children to support. That's how I make my living, and I wish you would keep your nose out of MY business."

Then all of the thin-skinned compromisers who can't stand competition or loud voices or "name calling," etc. (see p. 161) intervened hastily lest there be bloodshed; that is how ALL of those effeminate, compromising sissies have to behave because of the bad press they might get for "disturbing the peace." ## Chapter 7 {.heading_98-0}

7:1 Now after these things, in the reign of Artaxerxes king of Persia, Ezra the son of Seraiah, the son of Azariah, the son of Hilkiah,

6 This Ezra went up from Babylon; and he was a ready scribe in the law of Moses, which the LORD God of Israel had given: and the king granted him all his request, according to the hand of the LORD his God upon him.

7 And there went up some of the children of Israel, and of the priests, and the Levites, and the singers, and the porters, and the Nethinims, unto Jerusalem, in the seventh year of Artaxerxes the king.

8 And he came to Jerusalem in the fifth month, which was in the seventh year of the king.

10 For Ezra had prepared his heart to seek the law of the LORD, and to do it, and to teach in Israel statutes and judgments.

These first ten verses are a radically condensed and abbreviated "biography" of the author of the book: Ezra. So here we have Ezra spoken of in the [third person ]{.class_3429}(["he," "him,"]{.class_3428} and ["his,"]{.class_3428} vss. 6, 9--10) instead of "me" and "I." Baruch was an excellent ["scribe"]{.class_3428} (see Jer. 36:26, 32).

## Chapter 8 {.heading_98-0}

8:1 These are now the chief of their fathers, and this is the genealogy of them that went up with me from Babylon, in the reign of Artaxerxes the king.

## Chapter 1 {.heading_98-0}

1:1 The words of Nehemiah the son of Hachaliah. And it came to pass in the month Chisleu, in the twentieth year, as I was in Shushan the palace,

2 That Hanani, one of my brethren, came, he and certain men of Judah; and I asked them concerning the Jews that had escaped, which were left of the captivity, and concerning Jerusalem.

3 And they said unto me, The remnant that are left of the captivity there in the province are in great affliction and reproach: the wall of Jerusalem also is broken down, and the gates thereof are burned with fire.

4 And it came to pass, when I heard these words, that I sat down and wept, and mourned certain days, and fasted, and prayed before the God of heaven,

["The month Chisleu\...in Shushan the palace"]{.class_3428} locates the [time]{.class_3429} and [place]{.class_3429} for the action. Chisleu, for a Jew, would be roughly November 25 to December 25th. Shushan is obviously the king's palace which was located in the capitol of ancient Susiana, east of the Tigris River in Persia.

The ["twentieth year"]{.class_3428} has problems. Bullinger dates the final destruction of Jerusalem at 489 B.C. All standard chronologies date it at 587--596 B.C. This makes a difference of nearly [100 years. ]{.class_3429}Here we will stick with the standard chronology and assume that the seventy-year period of captivity is NOT 496--426 B.C. This would make the servitude begin in the fourth year of Jehoiakim (2 Chron. 36:5), but it was [598 B.C. to 528 B.C.]{.class_3429}

When Bullinger gets his act together, he finds he has to make a liar out of the Holy Spirit in the [AV]{.class_3429} text, for, when faced with ["in the twentieth year,"]{.class_3428} he can't find the landing strip. He "flies a holding pattern" for three circles and then fails to land.

First he says the verse means ["forty-two years]{.class_3429} from the beginning of the captivity"; then he says ["thirty-five years]{.class_3429} from Jehoiakins captivity"; and finally, ["twenty-three years]{.class_3429} from the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1300.xhtml_page_163}destruction of Jerusalem." Which, as you can see, doesn't mean anything except that he didn't believe the passage so [he made up three different numbers]{.class_3429} that had nothing to do with the passage. Par for the course in the "scholarly community."

(By now you surely know what to do, don't you? Right on! Ignore him.)

["One of my brethren"]{.class_3428} indicates that Hanani was not only a "Jewish brethren" (see comments under 1 John 2:9, 3:15 in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on General Epistles, ]{.class_3429}Vol. 2[,]{.class_3429} 2003) but a real family "brother" (see ["MY brother"]{.class_3428} in 7:2). Nehemiah's response is fourfold: [he weeps]{.class_3429} (vs. 4), [he mourns]{.class_3429} (vs. 4), [he fasts]{.class_3429} (vs. 4), [and he prays]{.class_3429} (vs. 4).

1:5 And said, I beseech thee, O LORD God of heaven, the great and terrible God, that keepeth covenant and mercy for them that love him and observe his commandments:

6 Let thine ear now be attentive, and thine eyes open, that thou mayest hear the prayer of thy servant, which I pray before thee now, day and night, for the children of Israel thy servants, and confess the sins of the children of Israel, which we have sinned against thee: both I and my father's house have sinned.

7 We have dealt very corruptly against thee, and have not kept the commandments, nor the statutes, nor the judgments, which thou commandedst thy servant Moses.

Now, these walls, in Old Testament times, were very important as you can see by David's concern in 2 Samuel 11:20--24. ["The shooters"]{.class_3428} are on the wall because in any siege they would hold the "high ground." The high ground today in combat is no longer a hill or a rock or a mountain (Judg. 4:14). The Germans were behind it in less than [four days;]{.class_3429} they attacked right [through it.]{.class_3429}

## Chapter 2 {.heading_98-0}

2:1 And it came to pass in the month Nisan, in the twentieth year of Artaxerxes the king, that wine was before him: and I took up the wine, and gave it unto the king. Now I had not been beforetime sad in his presence.

2 Wherefore the king said unto me, Why is thy countenance sad, seeing thou art not sick? this is nothing else but sorrow of heart. Then I was very sore afraid,

3 And said unto the king, Let the king live for ever: why should not my countenance be sad, when the city, the place of my fathers' sepulchres, lieth waste, and the gates thereof are consumed with fire?

4 Then the king said unto me, For what dost thou make request? So I prayed to the God of heaven.

5 And I said unto the king, If it please the king, and if thy servant have found favour in thy sight, that thou wouldest send me unto Judah, unto the city of my fathers' sepulchres, that I may build it.

3:1 Then Eliashib the high priest rose up with his brethren the priests, and they builded the sheep gate; they sanctified it, and set up the doors of it; even unto the tower of Meah they sanctified it, unto the tower of Hananeel.

10 And next unto them repaired Jedaiah the son of Harumaph, even over against his house. And next unto him repaired Hattush the son of Hashabniah.

21 After him repaired Meremoth the son of Urijah the son of Koz another piece, from the door of the house of Eliashib even to the end of the house of Eliashib.

22 And after him repaired the priests, the men of the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1473.xhtml_page_188}plain.

24 After him repaired Binnui the son of Henadad another piece, from the house of Azariah unto the turning of the wall, even unto the corner.

The list of gates do not constitute any particular problem, although Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown assure us that the word ["Meah"]{.class_3428} (vs. 1) has been [mistranslated. ]{.class_3429}Since the word is the Hebrew word for "100," we are to assume the [AV]{.class_3429} is wrong by calling it the name of a [tower. ]{.class_3429}(Typical bungling Alexandrian scholarship.) The word preceding ["Meah"]{.class_3428} (Heb.: He, Mem, Aleph, He) is "[Midgol]{.class_3429}" (Heb.: Mem, Gimmel, Daleth, Lamed)---meaning ["tower."]{.class_3428} Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown insist the passage should read "unto the tower 100."

This would give you "they builded the sheep gate; they sanctified it EVEN UNTO THE TOWER 100 they sanctified it (i.e., ["the sheep gate"]{.class_3428}).

And this is nonsense. Fortunately, Green did not "buy" it, and his [Hebrew Interlinear,]{.class_3429} Vol. II, p. 1265, follows the [King James.]{.class_3429}

["The tower"]{.class_3428} has to be named, for another one in the same passage is named ["the tower of Hananeel"]{.class_3428}---not a "gate."

Notice the interesting insertion of one word in verse 20:[ "EARNESTLY."]{.class_3428} In the midst of all this repairing done by hundreds of men, the word ["repaired"]{.class_3428} occurs thirty-one times, but only once does it mention that a "repairer" repaired ["earnestly"]{.class_3428} (vs. 20). If in the midst of a long, boring list of names---see our remarks on pages 28--31---you wanted to find something devotional and practical, there it is. One worker worked ["earnestly."]{.class_3428} That is, in the New Testament he would have obeyed Colossians 3:17, 23 and Romans 12:11. In the Old Testament, ["Baruch the son of Zabbai"]{.class_3428} would have found a place in Ecclesiastes 9:10.

4:1 But it came to pass, that when Sanballat heard that we builded the wall, he was wroth, and took great indignation, and mocked the Jews.

2 And he spake before his brethren and the army of Samaria, and said, What do these feeble Jews? will they fortify themselves? will they sacrifice? will they make an end in a day? will they revive the stones out of the heaps of the rubbish which are burned?

3 Now Tobiah the Ammonite was by him, and he said, Even that which they build, if a fox go up, he shall even break down their stone wall.

4 Hear, O our God; for we are despised: and turn their reproach upon their own head, and give them for a prey in the land of captivity:

5 And cover not their iniquity, and let not their sin be blotted out from before thee: for they have provoked thee to anger before the builders.

6 So built we the wall; and all the wall was joined together unto the half thereof: for the people had a mind to work.

My bunch (1939--1945) was the bunch where occasionally a G.I. was called upon to dig a six-by-six hole in the ground to [bury a mosquito. ]{.class_3429}The idea was that if you ever [slapped]{.class_3429} any mosquito at Ft. Benning, Georgia, in the summer, while doing a "night problem," you would endanger your life and the life of your patrol (or platoon or whatever). (This was training for the southwest Pacific.) All it takes to get a live grenade rolled into your slit trench or fox hole is some noise that shows an enemy night patrol "wheah you is."[ You never SLAP four to forty mosquitoes who are sucking blood out of your neck, hands, and face. ]{.class_3429}You nicely, quietly (and politely) SMASH them with your fingertips---or dig a "six-by-six" and (sometimes) hold a "mock funeral" for the "deceased."

I understand military training in the regular army is a little "different" now (2004). I am sure it has "progressed"! (Darwin said it [had]{.class_3429} to---automatically.)

Many, many years ago when I was a very young man (age 23), I was about to graduate from OCS at Ft. Benning as an infantry shave-tail (2nd Lt.). On the last day before graduating we "fell out," as usual, on the company street and "dressed right," etc. Then we were given the command to come to "parade rest" and then attention. The "bird dog" (the "Tactical Officer"---Eddie Copeland) yelled "UPTOBERRY OHWARD."

If you never saw a Chinese Fire Drill, you would have seen it []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1546.xhtml_page_205}then. The one hundred candidates---the survivors of the original 200; in those days they washed out the lower half of the candidates no matter how good they were---executed "present arms" (about twenty of them), and some came back to parade rest (about eighty of them). Several took "at ease" (about ten of them), and the rest stood there dumbfounded while about ten came to "right shoulder arms." To or three took two steps forward in ranks.

After things settled down, 1st Looey Copeland said, "Let that be a lesson to you. Always give your commands clearly." When a dozen voices cried out, "What was the command?" He grimly replied: "MONTGOMERY WARD!"

Truman Dollar (later a suicide) preached on the sin of "racism." One "token" black was allowed to preach; he had married a white woman. Wendell Zimmerman (formerly at Kansas City Baptist Temple and then at Jacksonville Baptist Temple in Jacksonville) was assigned "The Bible," and he preached a "holding pattern" for thirty minutes, circling around the airstrip, but he never landed. He didn't dare tell [anyone ]{.class_3429}what the "Scriptures" were, and he never [once ]{.class_3429}confessed that the Book he held in his hand and preached was infallible or even [inerrant]{.class_3429}.

After hours of this artificial, fake "Christianity," ole' Buddy Cargill []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1709.xhtml_page_218}got up, and with Bible under arm, he began to walk up and down in front of the rows where people were seated. When some powdered-up, fluffy, half-male half-female was showing off on the TV screen, Buddy would address various people sitting there and shout "Bless God, brother! (or sister) Doesn't that just make you feel like runnin' the bases!?"

I would make a contribution occasionally by opening my upper shirt pocket with my fingers and then pretend it was a "barf bag" on a plane. After simulating a good "puke" I would "pat" the shirt pocket shut.

Those consecrated, dedicated Christians, sitting near us, often heard "Aw, rats!" or "Oh, my God, what a mess." or "Didya dig that one, Ruck? Is he on pot?" and so forth. Such a response to such a "holy, Baptist" presentation of truth could not go on forever. After two nights of theatrical splendor, lightly flavored with one or two milky messages, a middle-aged woman in front of me suddenly turned around and shouted, "What kind of Christians are you people, anyway?!" I grinned and said, "The kind that enjoys themselves, lady." Immediately her husband turned to glare at me, fists clenched.

My reaction was subconscious and automatic. I kept grinning and looking him straight in the eyes so he would not see what my hands were doing. I lightly crossed them in front of me (on my knees) and bent forward ever so slightly in my chair. He didn't know it, but he was about to take a trip, head over heels, down about three rows, courtesy of a sixty-year-old "red neck." At that moment, Buddy Cargill leaned forward and in a loud voice said, "Don't worry about him, Ruckman. [He'd have to ask his wife for permission 'fore he could hit ya!"]{.class_3429}

That was the spiritual "tone" of a "World Congress."

Sanballat is going to "rat" on Nehemiah (vs. 7:[ "now shall it be reported to the king"]{.class_3428}) like the "canary who couldn't fly" ratted on Albert Anastasia's "Murder Inc." back around 1940--1941. The label "pigeon" (or "canary") came from a "ratter" being described as a "stool pigeon." This droll anachronism was the gangster way of identifying a "bird" who would "sing" when given the "third degree"---a barrage of questions between blows, while seated [on a stool,]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1709.xhtml_page_219} under a 150-watt light, in a dark room at the police station. Another term was "stoolie."

Gravano's "claim to fame" came from this; he "ratted" on John Gotti. The "canary who couldn't [fly]{.class_3429}" was Abe "Kid Twist" Reles (1907--1941) who "took off into the wild blue yonder" out of a window on the sixth floor of the Half Moon Hotel (Coney Island) [without any wings]{.class_3429} (!) and landed [twenty feet]{.class_3429} out from the side of the building.

Verse 14: ["And on the prophetess Noadiah, and the rest of the PROPHETS, that would have put me in fear."]{.class_3428}

At this point, Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown (commentators) decide the [AV]{.class_3429} text is in error [again,]{.class_3429} so they correct it with the A.D. [Septuagint]{.class_3429} which was written 200 years AFTER the New Testament was completed. However, the Hebrew word was [feminine]{.class_3429} (He, Nun, Beth, Yod, Aleph, and He). The Masoretic vowel that ends the word is "[`<bdi dir="rtl">`{=html}אה`</bdi>`{=html}]{.class_3450}": [this is a feminine ending. ]{.class_3429}So the scholars went to the "original Greek" (the LXX was written in Greek) and found this: `<bdi dir="rtl">`{=html}τ`</bdi>`{=html}ω `<bdi dir="rtl">`{=html}π`</bdi>`{=html}ροφητη. This is a [masculine, singular. ]{.class_3429}Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown have translated this contradiction as "Noadiah the PROPHET." But the word "prophet" in the LXX is masculine; the "original" Hebrew was feminine.

"When in doubt . . ." you know what to do! Correct [all]{.class_3442} Hebrew and Greek authorities with the text of the [Holy Bible.]{.class_3442}

6:15 So the wall was finished in the twenty and fifth day of the month Elul, in fifty and two days.

Applying all of this to 1960--2000 is no hard task at all, as any minister in the twentieth or twenty-first century knows if he has ever tried to pastor several hundred people in an independent, Bible-believing, Baptist church (1960--2000).

I will give you just a very brief sampling from one man's past:[ my own. ]{.class_3429}These are the things that often take place in the Body of Christ in its last days (2 Tim. 3:1) since Diotrophes, ["who loveth to have the preeminence,"]{.class_3428} and ["Noadiah the prophetess"]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1709.xhtml_page_223} organize the "ladies auxiliaries" to get rid of a pastor while the deacon board plots (Num. 16) to take over the pulpit, etc.

1\. [Private]{.class_3429} deacon meetings take place behind the pastor's back. 2. Attempts to bring in a young man from Tennessee Temple and work with the pastor as an "associate" with the idea of later putting him in [as pastor. ]{.class_3429}3. Threatening lawsuits against the pastor and finally "taking him to court." 5. Getting all of the anti-pastor men to gang up on the [front row]{.class_3429} of the auditorium to "stare down" the pastor as he taught the [adult Bible class. ]{.class_3429}6. Threatening to burn down the [pastorium. ]{.class_3429}8. Setting up [two separate bank accounts,]{.class_3429} without the church knowing about it, so they could use one of them later [if they had to start another church. ]{.class_3429}9. Getting a teacher to offer the pastor a job teaching in the public schools so he would [resign]{.class_3429} the pastorate. 10. Writing letters to Bob Jones Jr. to get him to convince the pastor that he was not "qualified" to be a "pastor." 11. Bringing an [epileptic]{.class_3429} to church so that if she had a "fit" in the service it could be blamed on the pastor's [preaching. ]{.class_3429}12. Arranging to have one deacon's wife [bump]{.class_3429} another deacon's wife in the aisle in the hopes that a fight would start since the victim's husband was noted for his [quick temper. ]{.class_3429}13. Starting a slander campaign and threatening to blackmail the pastor with "compromising" material if he didn't [quit. ]{.class_3429}14. Threatening to cut off his salary so he would starve to death. 15. Threatening [physical violence]{.class_3429} (a beatin' up). 16. Quit putting any money into the plate in hopes of [bankrupting the church]{.class_3429} by default for failure to pay for a bond program set up by a previous pastor (Dolphus Price, Tennessee Temple).

You say, "What did you do?"

Why, silly, I did just what Nehemiah did.

I pastored the church till seventeen "Palestinian" families left it on the same Sunday. They started a new church within [three miles]{.class_3429} of my pastorate with their "secret bank account" and called in a Tennessee Temple boy---[the son of one of the women they had used!]{.class_3429}

Our offerings tripled after they left.

But I received [light]{.class_3429} treatment. Some of my best friends in the pastorate have encountered ["Sanballat"]{.class_3428} and ["Tobiah"]{.class_3428} and ["Noadiah"]{.class_3428} using these tactics:

1\. A pastor friend of mine in Mississippi had his members [let the air out of tires]{.class_3429} during the service: all four of them.

2\. The deacon of another pastor [shot two of his bird dogs.]{.class_3429}

3\. A pastor in Florida distributed tracts all over his church accusing Beauchamp Vick (Temple Baptist Church, Detroit) of being a [Judas Iscariot]{.class_3429} and a "Ahithopel" in dealing with J. Frank Norris.

4\. In  a Southern Baptist church in Rocky Mount, North Carolina, 80 percent of the people voted to leave the Convention because of [Liberalism]{.class_3429}---attacks against the Bible by the teachers in Baylor, Howard, Judson, Stetson, Wake Forrest, etc. So the deacons, in fellowship with the associational missionary, rallied [twenty people]{.class_3429}---less than 5 percent of the congregation, sued the congregation, took them to court, took the property from them ([about 400 members]{.class_3429}), and drove them off the property: permanently[.]{.class_3429}

5\. During a church split, three kids who were all sons of deacons (fourteen and fifteen year olds) ganged up on the [thirteen-year-old son]{.class_3429} of the pastor when he got out of school and [beat him up.]{.class_3429}

6\. A dear, sweet, "Lottie Moon" lady took three dozen church bulletins and [burned the pastor's picture off them with a cigarette lighter.]{.class_3429}

7\. J. Frank Norris hired a cohort to trail John Rawlings and report on his work in another town so he could get some dirt to print on him in the World Baptist Fellowship newspaper ([The Fundamentalist]{.class_3429}).

8\. Some Christians got together and "set up" Beauchamp Vick's daughter in a staged [blackmail picture.]{.class_3429}

9\. "Anti-Norrisites," in Fort Worth, hired a [gunman]{.class_3429} to shoot down the pastor while he was in his study; they then burned down the First Baptist Church and accused [him]{.class_3429} of doing it to collect the insurance. (See the burning of the Reichstag by "Communists," in 1933, or the "Oklahoma" bomber who planted [four bombs]{.class_3429} in a building [before]{.class_3429} one went off that could no more have been produced by fertilizer than by baking soda.)

10\. I know of [three,]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1709.xhtml_page_225} Bible-believing, soulwinning, Fundamentalist, Baptist pastors who have had Christian businessmen on their finance committees abscond with more than \$20,000 of "collection plate" funds.

11\. Witness Brent Baptist Church, under a Tennessee Temple graduate, running up local bills of over \$100,000 and, then, leaving [without paying a dime of it. ]{.class_3429}At the [same time,]{.class_3429} he evacuated with over \$10,000 worth of "bearer" type bonds that he didn't buy or pay for.

Forty years [later]{.class_3429}, he got another Tennessee Temple boy to set up a "memorial remembrance" service for him; the "old timers" showed up and gave him an [offering]{.class_3429} for preaching! I wasn't invited, [although I was the pastor who paid off the rest of his bond program AND \$100,000 worth of his bad debts!]{.class_3429}

"Blessed be the tie that binds our hearts in Christian love, etc."

I'll show you how the "brethren" are!

I am painting several dozen portraits for the Christian Hall of Fame in Canton, Ohio: Harold Henniger's old church. I have just finished one of J. Frank Norris and have stood it up against the wall to dry; it was done (like most of them were done) in oils. I had finished Knox, Luther, St. Patrick, Tertullian, Polycarp, Ignatius, Whitefield, Wesley, Cartwright, Calvin, Booth, Chrysostom, and several others, and was up now past Sam Jones, Dwight Moody, Charles Finney, and Gypsy Smith. Norris had been "on deck" beside DeHaan, B. H. Carroll, William Riley, and Mel Trotter.

Well, in comes[ Dallas Billington]{.class_3429} (Akron Baptist Temple). He looks down a line of five portraits and sees J. Frank. He grunts and says to Henninger, "You gonna have HIM in here?" Brother Henninger (always a gentleman, and I mean that seriously) says, "Well, Dr. Billington, you know he produced a lot of good preachers in his day and planted a lot of churches!" "Humph!" says Billington, "Some of the brethren aren't going to like that!"

Why did he react like that? Well, before that, back in the late 1940s and early 1950s, the Baptists in Texas had a big split. Up to that time Norris had pastored the two largest Baptist churches in America (simultaneously): one in Fort Worth and one in Detroit. While preaching Sunday morning at the First Baptist Church in Fort []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1709.xhtml_page_226}Worth, Beauchamp Vick, Norris' assistant, would preach in the Temple Baptist Church in Detroit; then Norris would fly up there and preach the evening service.

The dispute that split the fellowship into the Bible Baptist Fellowship (centering around the BBC at Springfield, Missouri) and the World Baptist Fellowship (centering around Arlington and Fort Worth, Texas) was over the Bible Baptist Seminary---"teaching the whole ENGLISH BIBLE"---a subsidiary of the First Baptist Church in Fort Worth. The upshot was many of the pastors wanted to teach there or get "ahold" of the school, and they chose [Beauchamp Vick]{.class_3429} to represent them in an effort to transfer corporation papers, deeds, financial records, etc. to the fellowship (instead of Norris) and dislocate the Seminary so it was on "neutral" ground, owned and operated by PASTORS in several states instead of by one PASTOR in one state.

A typical Baptist "civil war" erupted. I will not bore you with details, but all of Norris' buddies labeled Vick as Judas or at least an "Ahithophel" (2 Sam. 15). All of Vick's buddies accused Norris of "yellow journalism," "dictatorial tactics," misappropriation and mishandling of funds, immorality, and so forth.

At that time, I was an interdenominational, full-time evangelist: I preached in Southern and Northern Baptist churches, Pentecostal churches, the Church of God, Southern and Wesleyan Methodist churches, independent Baptist churches, Nazarene churches, Presbyterian churches, and so forth.

Consequently, I was getting fire from [both sides]{.class_3429} in the split: Rawlings in Cincinnati vs. Goreman in Tampa, Noel Smith in Missouri vs. Gerald Fleming in Dayton, Henninger in Canton vs. Bob Ingle in Jacksonville, Wendell Zimmerman in Kansas City vs. Bonam in San Antonio, und so weiter!

Well, one bright day late in the summer (Aug.), I was ["holding forth the word of life"]{.class_3428} at Camp Chatauqua on the Miami River north of Cincinnati; this was somewhere around 1965. At Chatauqua I preached every summer to the young people from all of the BBF churches in Michigan, Ohio, and Indiana. On that particular night the president of the World Baptist Fellowship (Norris' old group) showed up: [Gerald Fleming]{.class_3429}, a very close friend of mine for many years.

So here, for the first time (and undoubtedly for the last time!), were the [presidents ]{.class_3429}of the two opposing fellowships, plus the [president ]{.class_3429}of BBC, on the same camp grounds, along with an evangelist [all three of them had used several times. ]{.class_3429}In my extreme naivete (I had not been a pastor yet!!), I thought I had a capital idea; it was to get Gerald Fleming, John Rawlings, and Beauchamp Vick engaged (with me!) in a game of shuffleboard. (Frankly, I cared nothing about the game. I always played softball, at Chatauqua, and "Blood Ball," a rather gruesome "body contact" sport where there was no referee and no rules; but the brethren were in no condition to play the latter game.)

I think that Dr. Vick and I played Rawlings and Fleming; I do not exactly remember, but boy! do I ever remember the spiritual "atmosphere" in that thirty minute game.

You talk about being "cool," man! You talk about artificial conversations. Nobody got mad and nobody got rude, but then again, nobody got relaxed and nobody laughed at [anything]{.class_3429}. That game was as neutral and "without incident" as four tennis balls floating in a bathtub.

Later, I was riding home with Mr. and Mrs. Vick to Detroit. I tried to do a little follow-up work. I said, "Dr. Vick, why don't you and your crew get together with Brother Fleming and his crew and bury the hatchet. Put away all the fussing and join the Fellowships! Man, you could take the United States with the churches you have! You could run the Catholics out of the country!"

He shook his head vigorously and said, "Oh, no, no. No, it's too late now. Much too much has been said. There is no way we could get together now."

"But," I insisted, "forgive, man, forgive! Let bygones be bygones, you know."

"You don't know what all they said about me," Vick replied.

"Sure I do," I said. (And I did. Everything, including a plot to blackmail his daughter, and more.) "But good night, Brother Vick, the guy is dead. You're going to have to live forever with him in Heaven and...."

At this point Mrs. Vick, in the front seat, interrupted me and said loudly, "IF HE'S IN HEAVEN!"

I laughed and said, "C'mon, Mrs. Vick, you know he's in Heaven! What are you talking about?"

She told me---gladly---and was very [specific]{.class_3429}. I mean, she dumped a load of garbage on me about Norris that would fill a book, and boy, when she got through I didn't make any more attempts to reconcile any of the "dearly beloved brethren." I haven't since that day, and that has been more than thirty years ago.

## Chapter 7 {.heading_98-0}

7:1 Now it came to pass, when the wall was built, and I had set up the doors, and the porters and the singers and the Levites were appointed,

2 That I gave my brother Hanani, and Hananiah the ruler of the palace, charge over Jerusalem: for he was a faithful man, and feared God above many.

3 And I said unto them, Let not the gates of Jerusalem be opened until the sun be hot; and while they stand by, let them shut the doors, and bar them: and appoint watches of the inhabitants of Jerusalem, every one in his watch, and every one to be over against his house.

4 Now the city was large and great: but the people were few therein, and the houses were not builded.

Verse 1 is self explanatory. In verse 2, Nehemiah steps down slightly from his position and delegates much of his authority to a younger brother, Hanani (as well as ["Hananiah the ruler of the palace"]{.class_3428}). The main reason for this is Nehemiah's plan to take a short "furlough" and go back to Persia to report to his "boss" (see Neh. 13:6--7).

Verse 3: Normally, the gates were opened exactly at [sunrise]{.class_3429} (Judg. 9:3); [here,]{.class_3429} the keepers of the city are told to wait a couple of hours [after]{.class_3429} sunrise before opening: ["until the sun be hot."]{.class_3428} At sundown, when they ["shut the doors"]{.class_3428} and bar them, there are to be "watchers" armed and observing the closing of the gates. This needed to be done because a ragtag army of "ragheads" were still outside the city (Neh. 4:2), and Jerusalem was vastly underpopulated (vs. 4). The "Palestinians" are still lurking behind scenes.

7:5 And my God put into mine heart to gather together the nobles, and the rulers, and the people, that they might be reckoned by genealogy. And I found a register of the genealogy of them which came up at the first, and found []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA1837.xhtml_page_230}written therein,

6 These are the children of the province, that went up out of the captivity, of those that had been carried away, whom Nebuchadnezzar the king of Babylon had carried away, and came again to Jerusalem and to Judah, every one unto his city;

7 Who came with Zerubbabel, Jeshua, Nehemiah, Azariah, Raamiah, Nahamani, Mordecai, Bilshan, Mispereth, Bigvai, Nehum, Baanah. The number, I say, of the men of the people of Israel was this;

The "order of service: is:

Ezra prays and "blesses" God; the congregation answers with a double ["Amen"]{.class_3428} (vs. 6). They lift their hands while doing this, for the stretching out of hands towards heaven (whether standing or kneeling) was the Old Testament posture in prayer (1 Kings 8:22).

At the end of "amening" the pastor, they all bow down their heads and look at the ground. (Cf. the publican in Luke 18 and the expressions in Exod. 23:24; 2 Kings 5:18; Psa. 95:6; Phil. 2:10; etc.) The intimation is that they are [on all fours ]{.class_3429}(on their knees: Dan. 6:10, 10:10; 1 Kings 8:54; Matt. 17:14).

The congregation then [stands up]{.class_3429} (vs. 7), and then thirteen translators, plus Levites, begin to read and translate for the benefit of any Persian, Aramaic, or Babylonian listeners: i.e., Jews raised using these languages (see Acts 2).

The "reading" is done in three stages. First: you [read]{.class_3429} the words as they are found printed in the Book. This must be done slowly and ["distinctly."]{.class_3428} Second: you "give the sense" of the passage so that it ["makes sense."]{.class_3429} (In Hermeneutics this is known as "exegesis.") Third: you cause your congregation to [understand]{.class_3429} the reading. This is more than [exegesis;]{.class_3429} it is [application. ]{.class_3429}You give them an understanding of what the passage means in relation to them: this would involve [illustration and preaching and exhortation. ]{.class_3429}Paul describes it in 2 Timothy 4:1--4 and 1 Timothy 4:13.

The result of this is [conviction]{.class_3429} and [tears]{.class_3429} (vs. 9).

9:32 Now therefore, our God, the great, the mighty, and the terrible God, who keepest covenant and mercy, let not all the trouble seem little before thee, that hath come upon us, on our kings, on our princes, and on our priests, and on our prophets, and on our fathers, and on all thy people, since the time of the kings of Assyria unto this day.

33 Howbeit thou art just in all that is brought upon us; for thou hast done right, but we have done wickedly:

34 Neither have our kings, our princes, our priests, nor our fathers, kept thy law, nor hearkened unto thy commandments and thy testimonies, wherewith thou didst testify against them.

35 For they have not served thee in their kingdom, and in thy great goodness that thou gavest them, and in the large and fat land which thou gavest before them, neither turned they from their wicked works.

36 Behold, we are servants this day, and for the land that thou gavest unto our fathers to eat the fruit thereof and the good thereof, behold, we are servants in it:

38 And because of all this we make a sure covenant, and []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2036.xhtml_page_259}write it; and our princes, Levites, and priests, seal unto it.

## Chapter 10 {.heading_98-0}

10:1 Now those that sealed were, Nehemiah, the Tirshatha, the son of Hachaliah, and Zidkijah,

2 Seraiah, Azariah, Jeremiah,

3 Pashur, Amariah, Malchijah,

4 Hattush, Shebaniah, Malluch,

7 Meshullam, Abijah, Mijamin,

9 And the Levites: both Jeshua the son of Azaniah, Binnui of the sons of Henadad, Kadmiel;

10 And their brethren, Shebaniah, Hodijah, Kelita, Pelaiah, Hanan,

11 Micha, Rehob, Hashabiah,

12 Zaccur, Sherebiah, Shebaniah,

13 Hodijah, Bani, Beninu.

14 The chief of the people; Parosh, Pahathmoab, Elam, Zatthu, Bani,

15 Bunni, Azgad, Bebai,

16 Adonijah, Bigvai, Adin,

17 Ater, Hizkijah, Azzur,

18 Hodijah, Hashum, Bezai,

19 Hariph, Anathoth, Nebai,

20 Magpiash, Meshullam, Hezir,

21 Meshezabeel, Zadok, Jaddua,

22 Pelatiah, Hanan, Anaiah,

23 Hoshea, Hananiah, Hashub,

24 Hallohesh, Pileha, Shobek,

25 Rehum, Hashabnah, Maaseiah,

26 And Ahijah, Hanan, Anan,

27 Malluch, Harim, Baanah.

If any of you ladies want a name for your babies, there is a list from which to choose. You could call your kid ["Meshezabeel." ]{.class_3428}(In Num. 26:33, one of the daughters of Zelophehad is called ["Hoglah." ]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_262}How's that for a girl's name?)

On a more serious note, however, we see once more the phenomenon discussed on page 173. The names of well-known Old Testament characters start popping up: ["Jeremiah" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 2), ["Obadiah" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 5), ["Daniel" ]{.class_3428}and ["Baruch" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 6), ["Benjamin" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 7), ["Adonijah" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 16), and ["Zadok" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 21), just to name a few. The one thing this tells us for sure is that there will be a reoccurrence of Old Testament times: the Law is coming back in and Israel will be completely restored. As far as these Old Testament characters returning, I am not certain, but I have given you the Scriptures that deal with these matters on pages 173--174.

The "sealing" of verse 1, of course, refers to the ["sure covenant" ]{.class_3428}of Nehemiah 9:38. When the Bible speaks of someone [sealing ]{.class_3429}a document, the standard practice was that anyone of any position in a community had a ["signet"]{.class_3428} ring (Jer. 22:24). This ring had a design on it peculiar to the office of that person. When he signed a document, he would drip hot wax on the place for the signature; then he would press his signet ring into the wax. The operation is described briefly in Esther 3:12. So the men whose names are given in this passage are the ones who actually signed the covenant by placing their signet rings to the wax seal. But these signatures [represented ]{.class_3429}the people (vs. 28) through their chiefs (vs. 14).

Now, this covenant was a public document. The Lord believes in public commitment to Him. When Moses comes down from the mount in Exodus 32, he says, ["Who is on the LORD'S side? Let him come unto me" ]{.class_3428}(Exod. 32:26). In the New Testament, Jesus says, ["Whosoever therefore shall confess me before men, him will I confess also before my Father which is in heaven" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 10:32). That's why we give public invitations. The Lord wants you to manifest [publicly ]{.class_3429}that you are His.

Some of you Christians ought to take a blank sheet of paper and write something like this: "I hereby give the Lord Jesus Christ complete control of my life to do anything with it that He sees fit." Then sign and date that little agreement and set it aside where you will it find it every so often. That kind of written agreement between you and God will help you stay on the right track.

10:28 And the rest of the people, the priests, the Levites, the porters, the singers, the Nethinims, and all they that had separated themselves from the people of the lands unto the law of God, their wives, their sons, and their daughters, every one having knowledge, and having understanding;

29 They clave to their brethren, their nobles, and entered into a curse, and into an oath, to walk in God's law, which was given by Moses the servant of God, and to observe and do all the commandments of the LORD our Lord, and his judgments and his statutes;

30 And that we would not give our daughters unto the people of the land, nor take their daughters for our sons:

31 And if the people of the land bring ware or any victuals on the sabbath day to sell, that we would not buy it of them on the sabbath, or on the holy day: and that we would leave the seventh year, and the exaction of every debt.

Notice, first of all, that the Jews who entered into this covenant ["separated themselves"]{.class_3428} (vs. 28). Separation is a Bible doctrine for any believer in any age. Christ Himself was ["separate from sinners"]{.class_3428} (Heb. 7:26). The New Testament Christian is commanded by the Apostle Paul to ["come out from among them"]{.class_3428} (unbelievers, idol worshippers, and infidels---2 Cor. 6:14--16) ["and be ye separate, saith the Lord" ]{.class_3428}(2 Cor. 6:17).

But you have to watch out [how]{.class_3429} you put that separation into practice. There are those who ["separate themselves," ]{.class_3428}but they are characterized as ["sensual, having not the Spirit"]{.class_3428} (Jude 19). The Pharisees and Saducees were so [separated ]{.class_3429}that they would not even enter into a Gentile ["judgment hall, lest they should be defiled" ]{.class_3428}(John 18:28). THEY WERE PLOTTING THE MURDER OF GOD'S SON THE WHOLE TIME!

Somebody sent me, one time, the Constitution of a Baptist church in San Diego, California. That church was so [separated ]{.class_3429}that it not only condemned smoking, drinking, dancing, rock music, drugs, radio, television, and the theater; it also condemned classical music []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_264}(including some of the greatest Christian musicians who ever lived---Bach, Handel, and Mendelssohn), all "contemporary musical instruments," perfume, cologne, beards, moustaches, high heels, tea, coffee, chocolate, public schools, Christian schools, culottes, jewelry, jobs for women, makeup, sports, Christmas, and Easter. In fact, women were not allowed to "handle the word of God in any way, shape, or form." That means that church didn't allow women to [witness]{.class_3429}, teach their children the Scriptures, or [read ]{.class_3429}or [study ]{.class_3429}their Bibles on their own.

A church like that would make a Mennonite or an Amish church look like a hot bed of evangelism. If you want to set up a hellish outfit, that is the way to do it. All you have in a church like that is a bunch of self-righteous, self-centered people who sit around looking at each other, suspicious of what the other fellow is doing. You can't produce [spirituality ]{.class_3429}like that.

Double separation and ultra-separation are the curses of modern Fundamental Christianity. The idea is that the more [separated ]{.class_3429}you are, the more [spiritual ]{.class_3429}you are, and that isn't necessarily so. If that were the case, the most spiritual people in the world are down in the graveyard. [The dead don't smoke, drink, carouse, or go to the movies.]{.class_3429}

I have had better, more spiritual meetings in some [prisons ]{.class_3429}than I have had at some of these [Christian schools. ]{.class_3429}Those kids come into the auditorium all prim and proper. The girls' dresses are below their knees; the boys all have their hair cut just right. But those kids' [hearts ]{.class_3429}were just as cold as a block of ice. They couldn't have cared less about what I was saying.

Brethren, you can get rid of the TV; you can break all the rock albums; you can get the hair cut just right; you can get the dresses to the right length; you can stop running with the wrong crowd; you can drop the cigarettes, drugs, and the booze---AND THE WORLD CAN STILL BE RIGHT THERE IN YOUR HEART.

In the Bible, separation is not only [from]{.class_3429} something, it is [to ]{.class_3429}something. Paul said he was ["separated unto the gospel of God" ]{.class_3428}(Rom. 1:1). In the passage before us, the people ["separated themselves FROM the people of the lands UNTO the law of God." ]{.class_3428}In the Christian life, it is not enough to have a list of things you don't do. The Lord wants you to [do]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_265} something.

Notice, next, that the people ["entered into a curse" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 29). That pretty well sums up the Old Testament. God's covenant with Adam was don't eat of one particular tree or you will die (Gen. 2:17). He did, and he brought a curse upon himself, his wife, and the earth (Gen. 3:17). At the second giving of the Law (Deuteronomy), [twelve curses]{.class_3429} were pronounced by the Levites on sin; that's one curse for each tribe of Israel (Deut. 27:14--26). After those curses were pronounced, half of the tribes were to read the [blessings ]{.class_3429}of Deuteronomy 28:1--14. Then the other six tribes were to read the [cursings ]{.class_3429}of Deuteronomy 28:15--20. But look at the rest of Deuteronomy 28. The rest of the chapter is an exposition of how God will curse Israel for breaking the Law. That's [sixty-seven verses]{.class_3429} on the curses of the Law compared to [fourteen ]{.class_3429}on the blessings of the Law. The very last word in the Old Testament is the word ["curse" ]{.class_3428}(Mal. 4:6).

The New Testament summation of the Old Testament is found in Galatians 3:10. ["For as many as are of the works of the law are under the curse: for it is written, Cursed is every one that continueth not in all things which are written in the book of the law to do them."]{.class_3428} And of course, that is the kind of covenant that the Jews are entering into in Nehemiah 10:28--31. If they break any of the conditions of that covenant, they bring the curse of God upon themselves. That is exactly what happens in Malachi (see Mal. 1:14, 2:2, 3:9).

The New Testament is not that way. The New Testament view is that every one is already under a curse. John 3:18, ["He that believeth not is CONDEMNED ALREADY." ]{.class_3428}John 3:36, ["He that believeth not\...the wrath of God ABIDETH on him." ]{.class_3428}The purpose of the New Testament is to deliver man from the curse.

Romans 11:32, ["For God hath concluded them all in unbelief, that he might have mercy upon all."]{.class_3428}

Galatians 3:22, ["But the scripture hath concluded all under sin, that the promise by faith of Jesus Christ might be given to them that believe."]{.class_3428}

Galatians 3:13,[ "Christ hath redeemed us from the curse of the law, being made a curse for us: for it is written, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_266}Cursed is every one that hangeth on a tree."]{.class_3428}

Just as the last book of the Old Testament [ends ]{.class_3429}with a curse, the last book of the New Testament has [the end]{.class_3429} of the curse (Rev. 22:3).

The people of the Old Testament ["entered into a curse;" ]{.class_3428}the people of the New Testament enter into Jesus Christ.

Given such a sharp contrast, you can count on the Roman Catholic Church (just as sure as you can count on day following night) to completely mutilate the New Testament message. The one great curse of the New Testament is found in 1 Corinthians 16:22. ["If any man love not the Lord Jesus Christ, let him be Anathema Maranatha." ]{.class_3428}That is, "cursed at the coming" of the Lord. So, once more, the Catholics try to drag the Christian back into the Old Testament (with a priesthood, candles, robes, tabernacles, holy water, sprinkling, and continual sacrifices) by pronouncing 125 curses on every Baptist, Lutheran, Presbyterian, Methodist, Episcopalian, Nazarene, Hindu, Moslem, and Buddhist on the face of this earth. Those curses are found in the Council of Trent, which is considered to be the most important council ever held by the Catholic Church. Those curses are based on 1 Corinthians 16:22, and they say that a man is [anathema]{.class_3429} if he doesn't believe what a Roman Catholic is supposed to believe.

That's called [The Tridentine Oath ]{.class_3429}or [The Tridentine Confession. ]{.class_3429}Every Pope who took office since the Council of Trent had to sware by that Confession. The Tridentine Confession says, "I swear by God to uphold [all ]{.class_3429}the teachings of the Catholic Church, [especially ]{.class_3429}the holy Council of Trent."

That just goes to show you that any Catholic, especially the Pope, who talks about getting along with the "separated brethren" or who makes ecumenical overtures to Protestants is a liar. He is either lying about what he believes, or he is lying about getting together with non-Catholics.

The truth of the matter is if you believe in the eternal security of the believer, according to the Council of Trent, [you are cursed. ]{.class_3429}If you don't accept the [Apocrypha ]{.class_3429}as part of the word of God, you are cursed. If you don't believe that Roman Catholic water baptism [regenerates you,]{.class_3429} you are cursed. That's what a Catholic really believes, and anything that contradicts that is either lying or []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_267}ignorance.

In Nehemiah, these people take an oath to obey the Law, and if they don't, they agree to let God "damn" them. Something similar to this takes place in Acts 23:12. ["And when it was day, certain Jews banded together, and bound themselves under a curse, saying that they would neither eat or drink till they had killed Paul." ]{.class_3428}In Acts 23:14, they call it ["a great curse."]{.class_3428} I suppose that God went ahead and damned them since they never did kill Paul.

Now in Matthew and James, there is a strong emphasis against taking oaths. Of course, this has nothing to do with taking an oath[ in court. ]{.class_3442}Christ Himself did that in Matthew 26:63--64. But when it comes to everyday conversation, Christ says, ["Swear not at all...But let your communication be, Yea, yea; Nay, nay" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 5:34, 37). James 5:12 says, ["But above all things, my brethren, swear not, neither by heaven, neither by the earth, neither by any other oath: but let your yea be yea; and your nay, nay; lest ye fall into condemnation."]{.class_3428}

Both of those warnings are found in books written to Hebrews. By now, in this Commentary, you should realize that is hardly a coincidence; the warning goes far beyond personal references such as Jephthah in Judges 11 and Saul in 1 Samuel 14. Those Jews, in the future, are going to be asked to raise their hand in the two-fingered salute of Nimrod the bow man and swear an oath to the Antichrist. When they do, they will fix themselves permanently. I don't exactly know how it will be done, but in my book [The Mark of the Beast, ]{.class_3429}Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1960), I have a family before their three-dimensional, [holographic]{.class_3429}, two-way television set. On the "tube" is the Pope with his hand raised in the [two-fingered papal blessing ]{.class_3429}taking an oath of loyalty from his "viewing audience." After the family has sworn their oath, a mark is projected [through the TV]{.class_3429} onto the right hand or forehead of each viewer. That may have seemed "science fiction" when I first wrote that book back in the 60s, but it's not any more. Government officials, for many years before 1990, could use television sets to spy on people. With modern cable, satellite, and computer technology, the scenario I described is well within being a "real life" situation.

The oath which the Jews take here has three parts to it: 1) racial segregation \[vs. 30\], 2) Sabbath observance \[vs. 31\], and 3) support of the ministry \[vss. 32--39\].

10:32 Also we made ordinances for us, to charge ourselves yearly with the third part of a shekel for the service of the house of our God;

33 For the shewbread, and for the continual meat offering, and for the continual burnt offering, of the sabbaths, of the new moons, for the set feasts, and for the holy things, and for the sin offerings to make an atonement for Israel, and for all the work of the house of our God.

34 And we cast the lots among the priests, the Levites, and the people, for the wood offering, to bring it into the house of our God, after the houses of our fathers, at times appointed year by year, to burn upon the altar of the LORD our God, as it is written in the law:

35 And to bring the firstfruits of our ground, and the firstfruits of all fruit of all trees, year by year, unto the house of the LORD:

36 Also the firstborn of our sons, and of our cattle, as it is written in the law, and the firstlings of our herds and of our flocks, to bring to the house of our God, unto the priests that minister in the house of our God:

37 And that we should bring the firstfruits of our dough, and our offerings, and the fruit of all manner of trees, of wine and of oil, unto the priests, to the chambers of the house of our God; and the tithes of our ground unto the Levites, that the same Levites might have the tithes in all the cities of our tillage.

38 And the priest the son of Aaron shall be with the Levites, when the Levites take tithes: and the Levites shall bring up the tithe of the tithes unto the house of our God, to the chambers, into the treasure house.

39 For the children of Israel and the children of Levi shall bring the offering of the corn, of the new wine, and the oil, unto the chambers, where are the vessels of the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_269}sanctuary, and the priests that minister, and the porters, and the singers: and we will not forsake the house of our God.

This passage deals with the support[ of the Old Testament ministry. ]{.class_3429}Note that the standard temple offering has been reduced from the original as given in Exodus 30:13. In Exodus, the original offering was half a shekel, but the Jews in Nehemiah's time were in extreme poverty (Neh. 9:37). So the yearly offering was reduced to ["the third part of a shekel."]{.class_3428}

The cross-reference to verse 33 is Colossians 2:16--17. The meat and drink offerings, the feast days, the monthly feast of the new moon, and the observance of the sabbath days will all be reinstituted in the Millennium, despite what John Calvin and the Amillennialists teach.

Now, in verse 34, lots are cast to divide up the job of bringing in wood for the burnt offering. Back in the original temple, the Jews had servants to do this for them. In Joshua 9, the Gibeonites had deceived the Israelites and had led them to believe that they were from a far country, when actually they were only a three-day march away. As a result, the elders of Israel had made peace with them and had sworn they would not be destroyed.

["But all the princes said unto all the congregation, We have sworn unto them by the LORD God of Israel: now therefore we may not touch them. This we will do to them; we will even let them live, lest wrath be upon us, because of the oath which we sware unto them. And the princes said unto them, Let them live; but let them be hewers of wood and drawers of water unto all the congregation; as the princes had promised them\....And Joshua made them that day hewers of wood and drawers of water for the congregation, AND FOR THE ALTAR OF THE LORD, even unto this day, IN THE PLACE WHICH HE SHOULD CHOOSE" ]{.class_3428}(Josh. 9:19-21, 27).

When Judah was taken captive, the people lost those servants. Lamentations 5:13 says, ["the children fell under the wood." ]{.class_3428}They had to start cutting and carrying the wood for their fires []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2158.xhtml_page_270}themselves.

Here in Nehemiah 10, the job is divided between ["the priests, the Levites, and the people." ]{.class_3428}So everyone takes a part in a job that is a menial task, but which is important to the operation of the temple. If we make application to the operation of the New Testament church, there is a need in a congregation for "Marthas" as well as "Marys." That is, you need [servers ]{.class_3429}as well as [learners]{.class_3429}. Martha was the sister that took care of preparing and serving the food to the Lord and His disciples; Mary was the sister who sat and learned at the feet of Jesus. A church needs [both]{.class_3429}, preferably members who have a good balance of both qualities. A church can't operate without someone picking up the trash, putting the hymnals back in their racks, cleaning the bathrooms, changing diapers in the nursery, etc. On the other hand, if no one is there to learn the word of God, holding services is rather pointless. A "Mary" shouldn't get so taken up with the revival services that she forgets her turn in the nursery. A "Martha" shouldn't always have to miss the preaching to do some physical job in church. The entire congregation should [take turns]{.class_3429} performing the menial tasks that are needed to operate a church so that all the members can enjoy the preaching and teaching of the word of God in their turn.

When it comes to tithing and giving, I have already discussed this thoroughly in my Commentary on 1 and 2 Corinthians (2 Cor. 8--9).

Before closing Nehemiah 10, I want you to again notice (see pg. 10--13) how the expression ["house of...God" ]{.class_3428}keeps popping up. In this chapter, it has appeared [eight times ]{.class_3429}between verses 32 and 39. It occurs another four times in chapters 11 and 12 and five more times in chapter 13. Not one time in either Testament is it a reference to a church building anywhere on this earth. # The Book of Esther {.heading_18-0}

## Introduction {#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2475.xhtml_I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3414 .heading_98-0}

The book of Esther has 10 chapters, 167 verses, and 5,633 words. It was written somewhere between 485 and 465 B.C. It is the last in a series of three historical books written [after ]{.class_3429}the Jews returned from captivity. As Ezra and Nehemiah tell what happened to the Jews who returned to the Land, Esther tells what happened to the Jews who remained in Babylon and Persia.

In the Jewish Old Testament, the book is included in the section called "The Writings" (called "The Psalms" by Jesus Christ in Luke 24:44). In Hebrew, these books are known as the [Hagiographa]{.class_3429} (the Holy Writings other than the Law and the Prophets) or the [Kethubim]{.class_3429} (simply, the Writings).

Now, the Book of Esther is what I call a "strange" book in the Bible; that is, there are some peculiarities that make this book different from most of the other books in the Scriptures. First, it is one of only two Bible books which bear the name of a woman in the title. The other is, of course, the Book of Ruth. Both books have a marriage that takes place that is important historically as well as [prophetically]{.class_3429}. In Ruth, there is a Moabite woman who marries a Jew and becomes the great grandmother of King David. Prophetically, you have a type of a Gentile bride who marries a type of Christ; [it's a picture of the Church.]{.class_3429}

In Esther, there is a Jewish maiden who marries a Gentile king and becomes responsible for saving the Jews from genocide. In type that is a picture of the Lord restoring Israel as His wife before the Advent.

But the strangest thing of all in the book is that the name of God never appears one time. You won't find "God" anywhere in the book. In fact, you won't find the word ["LORD"]{.class_3429} there either. It is the only book of the Bible that is like that. If "God" has to be in a book for it to be a Bible book, then Esther doesn't qualify.

The omission of [God ]{.class_3429}and [LORD ]{.class_3429}is so glaring that the Septuagint (written almost 200 years after the death of Jesus Christ and the apostles) added passages to Esther so that the words make it in []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2475.xhtml_page_298}there. Jerome gathered these passages together into six chapters that follow chapter 10 in the Latin Vulgate. That is how it stands in a Roman Catholic Bible today, and according to the Council of Trent, you are cursed if you don't accept those six chapters. (Anything to "help God out," you know.)

The great thing in the Book of Esther is what is known as the Providence of God. That means that although the words [God ]{.class_3429}and [LORD]{.class_3429} do not appear in the book, it is obvious to any reader that the Lord is directing the circumstances of life to accomplish His will. When you read Esther, you see the hand of God on every page, but you never see [God]{.class_3429}. [God]{.class_3429} is busy working "behind the scenes." So the book has a great practical application to the New Testament believer, for contrary to Charismatic claptrap, this is not the "day of miracles," expect "your miracle," claim "your miracle," and all of the rest of that sacrilegious nonsense. It is the day when the Holy Spirit speaks through the Scriptures and works through the ordinary everyday events of life.

When you read Esther, you don't read about God parting the Red Sea or causing fire to fall from heaven or healing anybody miraculously. You read about typical instances like a fellow coming into a room at the wrong moment, a woman asking a favor of her husband, someone receiving an invitation to a banquet, a man who can't get to sleep at night. None of those things seem important, but each one determined the destiny of whole lives and nations. God's hand was behind each of those events, working things through.

We have already discussed the dispensational importance of the book (see pp. viii--xi). In the premillennial order of 2 Chronicles through Psalms, Esther falls between the national restoration of Israel in Nehemiah and the persecution of the Jew by Satan in the Tribulation. So Esther deals with events that will occur immediately preceding the Advent. Your modern prophecy boys say that there are no pre-Tribulation, pre-Rapture signs. That's not true. You have a whole book full: Esther, ten chapters. The events of Esther could take place at any time now.

Now, that is an advanced revelation in a King James Bible. You could not get that from a Hebrew Old Testament, for the books are not laid out the same. If you follow the order of books in a [King James Authorized Version, ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2475.xhtml_page_299}you have light that no Hebrew scholar has on the text unless he believes the English Bible; you have an insight on the Second Coming that no Orthodox Jew has, although he has the "verbally inspired originals." Hence, I teach that the [King James Bible]{.class_3429} is superior to the "originals." When I say that, the scholars all have a fit and scream, "Heresy! Blasphemy!" But the Lord is not stuck in some theological or linguistic box. The God of history still has many things to show to those who read and study His Book with a believing heart.

So with believing hearts let us study Esther and let the Holy Spirit who inspired the book and placed it in the canon of Scripture show us the great truths He has preserved for us in the English text.

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml}

## Chapter 1 {.heading_98-0}

1:1 Now it came to pass in the days of Ahasuerus, (this is Ahasuerus which reigned, from India even unto Ethiopia, over an hundred and seven and twenty provinces:)

2 That in those days, when the king Ahasuerus sat on the throne of his kingdom, which was in Shushan the palace,

3 In the third year of his reign, he made a feast unto all his princes and his servants; the power of Persia and Media, the nobles and princes of the provinces, being before him:

Verse 1 opens with the Jews under a Gentile king. Persia is the Gentile kingdom that is in power at this time. Prophetically Persia is a type of England. There have only been two times in history when a king ever made a decree for Israel to return to the Land. The first was under Cyrus of Persia and the other was under George V of England, a Gentile king. When the time came for God to choose a king to return Israel to her homeland, all the monarchies of Europe were gone except one: the English crown. After World War I England was the only world power left with a king.

According to most scholars[, ]{.class_3429}the Ahasuerus of verse 1 was the "Xerxes" of secular history; "Ahasuerus" being a title like Pharaoh or Caesar. While this may be true, notice the emphasis that God puts on the character compared with the view you would get from the History Department at any college or university in America or Europe.

In secular history, Xerxes was best known for his invasion of Greece, which eventually ended in failure. But the Lord completely overlooks this. He ignores Athens, Sparta, the Battle at Thermopylae, and the defeat of the Persian fleet at Salamis. Instead, God spends His time talking about a rebellious wife and an unknown Jewish girl who becomes Xerxes' queen.

When it comes to the Bible and modern education (Christian or secular), ["there is a great gulf fixed" ]{.class_3428}(Luke 16:26). The Lord said, ["My thoughts are not your thoughts"]{.class_3428} (Isa. 55:8), and that's the truth.

When two nations come to hostilities, all the newspapers cover the front page with big headlines that say "WAR!" Up in Heaven the angels yawn and say, "Ho hum. Here we go again." But you let some bum come to Christ at a little run-down Rescue Mission, and up in Glory they are shouting, screaming, and "running the bases." Down here on earth you wouldn't see one news article anywhere on the event. But you see, that's the difference between how the [Lord ]{.class_3429}looks at things and how [man ]{.class_3429}looks at things.

1:4 When he shewed the riches of his glorious kingdom and the honour of his excellent majesty many days, even an hundred and fourscore days.

5 And when these days were expired, the king made a feast unto all the people that were present in Shushan the palace, both unto great and small, seven days, in the court of the garden of the king\'s palace;

6 Where were white, green, and blue, hangings, fastened with cords of fine linen and purple to silver rings and pillars of marble: the beds were of gold and silver, upon a pavement of red, and blue, and white, and black, marble.

Notice in verse 4 that ["an hundred and fourscore days" ]{.class_3428}shows up. That is 180. A hundred and eighty days is half of a year on a Jewish lunar calendar. You say, what is so important about that? Look at verse 3: ["In the third year." ]{.class_3428}Verse 4 is [three and a half years]{.class_3429} into the reign of this Gentile, Persian king. That takes you right into the first half of the Tribulation at the end of the time of the Gentiles. So although Esther may take place historically [before ]{.class_3429}the events in Nehemiah (Neh. 2:6), prophetically the events of Esther are [after ]{.class_3429}the political restoration of Israel.

Verse 5 says that after the three and a half years of verses 3--4 that ["the king made a feast\...in the court of the garden of the king's palace." ]{.class_3428}In the New Testament, there are several words that aren't Greek words at all. The word ["mammon"]{.class_3428} (Luke 16:13) is a Persian word. The ["tree of life" ]{.class_3428}is a Persian term. You take the word ["paradise" ]{.class_3428}(Luke 23:43; 2 Cor. 12:4); [that's]{.class_3429} a Persian word. It literally means "a hunting garden." In Persia, a "paradise" was a huge estate with landscaped gardens that contained wild animals in it that []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_302}you could hunt. It was like the American Indian's idea of Heaven: a "happy hunting ground." So ["the garden of the king's palace"]{.class_3428} is a picture of Heaven.

What you have in verse 5 is a picture of a marriage feast going on [seven days]{.class_3429} up in Heaven, while on the ground, as pictured in the book of Job, Israel is being persecuted by the Devil [seven days]{.class_3429} and seven nights.

So what you have prophesied, [in type,]{.class_3429} is a Gentile kingdom which rules over the Jews and restores the nation politically by royal decree. Then the Rapture takes place, and there is a celebration running up in Heaven for seven years while that Jew is going through seven years of Tribulation.

In verse 6, there is a big layout of money to put on this feast. Ahasuerus is obviously trying to impress ["the nobles and princes" ]{.class_3428}with his wealth and power. In the Bible, Gentile kings held feasts on their birthdays (Gen. 40; Matt.14), at weddings (Esth. 2), or just to show off (Dan. 5). In each case, the feast is held for the benefit of the monarch's political underlings and servants. When a king held a party, the point was not for his servants to bring him presents; at such an occasion the king treated his faithful servants and gave [them ]{.class_3429}gifts and honor. At such a "bash," a king went "all out" so that those men who actually ran the kingdom (the princes, nobles, governors, etc.) would never think that they had more wealth and power than the king. In that way, the king kept his nobles "in line," psychologically. Also, by lavishly awarding faithful service at such events (or by severely punishing unfaithful service), he insured their loyalty.

The New Testament application is this: one day the King is going to hold a feast for his servants (Matt.22; Luke 14; Rev. 19). When He does, He is going to honor those who have served Him well; He will actually serve [them ]{.class_3429}(Luke 12:37). If you want to see a "spread," don't miss the Marriage Supper of the Lamb. You talk about a "feed," man, that will be it.

Notice in verse 6: ["gold and silver" ]{.class_3428}and ["fine linen." ]{.class_3428}Those are elements at the Judgment Seat of Christ (1 Cor. 3:12, Rev. 19:8). You also have ["vessels" ]{.class_3428}showing up in verse 7 (Rom.9:23, 2 Cor. 4:7, 2 Tim. 2:20--21).  

["The beds" ]{.class_3428}of verse 6 aren't beds for [sleeping]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_303}. The Orientals used beds on which to recline when they ate (see Esth.7:7--8). They were [reclining couches.]{.class_3429}

When you see that famous painting of [The Last Supper]{.class_3429}, you are looking at a fouled-up mess. Da Vinci has Christ and the disciples at this Renaissance table with an Italian landscape outside the window. Christ is sitting there with His yellow-blond hair and His blue eyes and His long slender fingers like a woman's at a sewing circle. What a crumby piece of work! But Da Vinci was a Catholic, so he got good press. The truth is that Leonardo Da Vinci couldn't draw flies. (See [Art and Artists, ]{.class_3429}Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1993.)

The Lord and the disciples weren't [sitting ]{.class_3429}on chairs at a table, at the Last Supper, eating with knives, forks, and spoons. They were [reclining ]{.class_3429}on couches. Look at John 13:23. ["Now there was LEANING ON JESUS' BOSOM one of his disciples."]{.class_3428} The Lord is lying on his side with His head resting on His elbow, and John is lying with his head back on the Lord's chest.

From a practical standpoint, reclining is much better for digestion of food than sitting upright. When you sit upright your stomach muscles are all cramped. People back then had more sense than they do today.

1:7 And they gave them drink in vessels of gold, (the vessels being diverse one from another,) and royal wine in abundance, according to the state of the king.

8 And the drinking was according to the law; none did compel: for so the king had appointed to all the officers of his house, that they should do according to every man\'s pleasure.

Back in verse 7: ["and royal wine in abundance."]{.class_3428} There's that wine Christ made in John 2. That wine was [supernatural wine;]{.class_3429} it is the same kind of wine that Christ said, ["I will not drink henceforth of this FRUIT OF THE VINE, until that day when I drink it NEW with you in my Father's KINGDOM"]{.class_3428} (Matt.26:29).

["And the drinking was according to the law; none did compel" ]{.class_3428}(vs.8). Oriental kings usually pledged the guests that []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_304}attended their banquets to drink a certain amount. This practice has survived to a certain degree in modern drinking bouts and drinking contests. The Germans are famous for this at Heidelberg, and the Americans have tried to pick it up from the Germans. At Heidelberg, when someone gives a toast, everyone has to stand and drink the toast. If you don't, then there is something wrong with you [socially;]{.class_3429} you can even insult someone so badly that it can lead to a duel.

So today, in the Hofbraeuhaus they sing: ["Eins, zwei suffa!!"]{.class_3429} [Suffa]{.class_3429} means "pour it down." The idea is that if you don't go along with the crowd that you're not "one of the boys." But here, in verse 8, the king passed a law that they didn't have to drink if they didn't want to. They could "take it or leave it." It was at their discretion.

["For so the king had]{.class_3428}[ ]{.class_3429}[appointed to all the officers of his house, that they should do according to every man's pleasure." ]{.class_3428}Again, this is a picture of the Marriage of the Lamb up in Heaven: you can do what you want to do. When you get to Heaven, you can do whatever you want and [think ]{.class_3429}whatever you want, and you will never have to worry about whether it is [right. ]{.class_3429}Do you realize what a blessing that will be? Haven't you Christians had trouble with some of the thoughts that float through your head at times? If you want to see how depraved and rotten you really are, then think about what you would be like if you yielded to every thought that passed through your brain.
