Christian, there is in you the ability to blaspheme the Holy Spirit and curse God. That kind of stuff is inside us, even as Christians. I thank God that He releases us and gives us moral relief from what we deserve. Most of the time, the Lord gives us so much to keep us occupied that we don't have the time to act on a lot of the evil thoughts we have.

1:9 Also Vashti the queen made a feast for the women in the royal house which belonged to king Ahasuerus.

Notice in verse 9 there is a Gentile queen. In this age here, God is calling out a Gentile bride. So in a sense, Vashti is a picture of a Gentile bride called out to be with the King. In this passage here, she's not in the garden, yet. After the Oriental custom, she is in a separate house from her husband (cf. 1 Kings 7:8), her own house, about to be called. It's a picture of a[ potential ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_305}Gentile queen about to be called up to the Rapture, and she doesn't go. So she is replaced by a Jewish bride.

Now, what you have here is Romans 11. At the [beginning ]{.class_3429}of the Church Age, God showed favor to the Jews because of His promises to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. But when they rejected their Messiah as Saviour in Acts 13, 18, and 28, the Lord gradually [displaced Israel]{.class_3429} and began dealing with the Gentiles. At the end of this age, [God displaces the Gentiles ]{.class_3429}and replaces them with Israel (for a more detailed discussion, see comments on Rom. 11 in that commentary).

At the writing of this Commentary (2003--2004), you are seeing that take place. [God is gradually ceasing his dealings with the Gentile nations as a whole. ]{.class_3429}While the Shemites and the Hamites might be experiencing some last vestiges of real revival, the Gentiles of Genesis 10:5 (America and the European nations that run the world) are experiencing fewer conversions to Jesus Christ than all the rest of the world combined. Very soon the Holy Spirit will move on from Asia and Africa as well and will end up right where He started in Acts 2---[in Jerusalem and the land of Israel. ]{.class_3429}God is in the process of [junking ]{.class_3429}the Gentiles.

The Bible is a remarkable book, don't you think? If 42 authors tried to sit down in collusion and write a book like the Bible, how would they do it? Not knowing the future, they wouldn't be able to "get off the ground." The Bible is the only book that has over 40 different authors, writing over a period of 1600 years, on three different continents, that's dares to prophecy events 2,000 to 3,000 years in the future,[ and gets them right every single time. ]{.class_3429}(See [One in 23,000,000]{.class_3429}, Bible Baptist Bookstore, 2001.) When it comes to prophecy, silly little books like[ The Koran]{.class_3429} are not even on the same race track, much less "in the running."

1:10 On the seventh day, when the heart of the king was merry with wine, he commanded Mehuman, Biztha, Harbona, Bigtha, and Abagtha, Zethar, and Carcas, the seven chamberlains that served in the presence of Ahasuerus the king,

11 To bring Vashti the queen before the king with the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_306}crown royal, to shew the people and the princes her beauty: for she was fair to look on.

12 But the queen Vashti refused to come at the king's commandment by his chamberlains: therefore was the king very wroth, and his anger burned in him.

13 Then the king said to the wise men, which knew the times, (for so was the king's manner toward all that knew law and judgment:

14 And the next unto him was Carshena, Shethar, Admatha, Tarshish, Meres, Marsena, and Memucan, the seven princes of Persia and Media, which saw the king's face, and which sat the first in the kingdom;)

15 What shall we do unto the queen Vashti according to law, because she hath not performed the commandment of the king Ahasuerus by the chamberlains?

16 And Memucan answered before the king and the princes, Vashti the queen hath not done wrong to the king only, but also to all the princes, and to all the people that are in all the provinces of the king Ahasuerus.

17 For this deed of the queen shall come abroad unto all women, so that they shall despise their husbands in their eyes, when it shall be reported, The king Ahasuerus commanded Vashti the queen to be brought in before him, but she came not.

18 Likewise shall the ladies of Persia and Media say this day unto all the king's princes, which have heard of the deed of the queen. Thus shall there arise too much contempt and wrath.

Verse 10 lists ["seven chamberlains that served in the presence of\...the king." ]{.class_3428}Then in verse 14, there are ["seven princes\...which saw the king's face."]{.class_3428} So you have two groups of seven there; the first being servants before the king and the second being royalty that ruled directly under the king. Since those seven chamberlains are [servants]{.class_3442}, the closest New Testament picture you can get is the angels of the seven churches of Revelation (see comments on the ["angels" ]{.class_3428}in that Commentary). The Lord says to the angel of each church, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_307}["I know thy WORKS."]{.class_3428}

Those ["princes" ]{.class_3428}are another story, though. They are not merely ["in the presence of\...the king;" ]{.class_3428}they actually see ["the king's face." ]{.class_3428}Moreover, they are rulers with the king. They are a picture of those ["seven Spirits of God"]{.class_3428} which are ["before the throne"]{.class_3428} (Rev. 4:5) of God.

Those ["princes"]{.class_3428} in Esther 1:14 are listed by name. If you want the "names" of those ["seven Spirits of God," ]{.class_3428}turn over to Isaiah 11:2. There those ["seven Spirits" ]{.class_3428}are:

1.[​]{.class_3436}["the spirit of the LORD."]{.class_3428}

2.[​]{.class_3436}["the spirit of wisdom."]{.class_3428}

3.[​]{.class_3436}["and understanding."]{.class_3428}

4.[​]{.class_3436}["the spirit of counsel."]{.class_3428}

5.[​]{.class_3436}["and might."]{.class_3428}

6.[​]{.class_3436}["the spirit of knowledge."]{.class_3428}

7.[​]{.class_3436}["and of the fear of the LORD."]{.class_3428}

All the commentators handle verse 11 the same. They all say that the king was drunk at this "orgy," and that he wanted to bring in his wife, half-dressed, and have people ogle her (and possibly mock her, as drunken fools will sometimes do). "She, being a modest, wonderful woman of gracious countenance, refused to debase herself to such a lowly estate," and that's why she refused to come. The problem with that is that you can't find it in the Scriptures for "love nor money."

In the narrative of Esther, what takes place is this. The King becomes angry with Vashti for refusing a [direct command ]{.class_3429}of the king. The king calls in his wise men (vs. 13). In the Bible, a heathen king's wise men were associated with magicians (Gen.41:8; Exod.7:11; Dan.2:27, 4:6--7). Hence the term [Magi]{.class_3429} for the ["wise men" ]{.class_3428}of Matthew 2. The Persian ["wise men"]{.class_3428} fare a lot better than the Babylonian wise men of Daniel's time. They analyze the situation correctly and give the king advice that turns out to be [New Testament doctrine]{.class_3429} (see comments on verse 22).

Notice in verse 13: ["the wise men\...knew the times."]{.class_3428} In the context, ["the times"]{.class_3428} are the times in which they lived (as in 1Chron.12:32 and 29:30). But notice in Scripture how often that ["the times" ]{.class_3428}are a prophetic reference to [the end times.]{.class_3429}

Ezekiel 12:27, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_308}["The vision that he seeth is for many days to come, and he prophesieth of THE TIMES that are far off."]{.class_3428}

Daniel 2:21, ["And he changeth THE TIMES and the seasons" ]{.class_3428}(a prophetic reference to God's dealings with the nations of Nebuchadnezzar's image).

Luke 21:24, ["Jerusalem shall be trodden down of the Gentiles, until THE TIMES of the Gentiles be fulfilled."]{.class_3428}

Acts 1:7, ["It is not for you to know THE TIMES or the seasons, which the Father hath put in his own power" ]{.class_3428}(Christ's answer to the disciples' question about the time of the restoration of the kingdom).

In Acts 3:19, you have ["THE TIMES of refreshing" ]{.class_3428}in reference to Israel being forgiven at the Second Advent for her rejection of her Messiah, and in Acts 3:21, you have ["THE TIMES of restitution" ]{.class_3428}in reference to the Millennium.

When Paul talks about ["THE TIMES and the seasons" ]{.class_3428}in 1 Thessalonians 5:1, he is referring to the Rapture of the Church, which he just described back in chapter 4.

So once more you have a prophetic reference in Esther that places the events of the book [in the future. ]{.class_3429}["The times" ]{.class_3428}refer to a period of time immediately preceding the Rapture of the Church all the way to beginning of the Millennium, which (by coincidence, of course, of course) just happens to be the material covered in Esther.

Now, the problem Ahasuerus had was that Vashti had not merely broken one of his commandments. She had set a [bad example ]{.class_3429}for all the women in the kingdom. The Apostle Paul said, ["For none of us liveth to himself, and no man dieth to himself" ]{.class_3428}(Rom. 14:7). Everyone has some kind of influence on someone (see comments in [The Bible Believers' Commentary on Romans).]{.class_3429}

The other women of the kingdom would be tempted to rebel against their husbands. They would say, "If [the queen]{.class_3429} can rebel against the highest authority in the land---the king---then surely we can get away with rebelling against these wimps to whom we're married."

1:19 If it please the king, let there go a royal []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_309}commandment from him, and let it be written among the laws of the Persians and the Medes, that it be not altered, That Vashti come no more before king Ahasuerus; and let the king give her royal estate unto another that is better than she.

20 And when the king's decree which he shall make shall be published throughout all his empire, (for it is great,) all the wives shall give to their husbands honour, both to great and small.

21 And the saying pleased the king and the princes; and the king did according to the word of Memucan:

22 For he sent letters into all the king's provinces, into every province according to the writing thereof, and to every people after their language, that every man should bear rule in his own house, and that it should be published according to the language of every people.

In verse 19, you have the famous ["laws of the Persians and the Medes."]{.class_3428} A verbal command of a Persian king could potentially be reversed, but once that command was committed to writing and sealed with the king's signet, that command became an irreversible, unalterable law. That unalterable character of Persian law will occur over and over again in the book of Esther. When it occurs in the book of Daniel (Dan. 6:8 -- 15), it is a picture of a commandment that came from God, and it has the same typology here.

Notice also in verse 19: ["let the king give her royal estate unto another that is BETTER than she." ]{.class_3428}Just like David replaced Saul, [a Jewish bride will be called out in the Tribulation to replace the Gentiles]{.class_3429} who [now]{.class_3429} have the first privilege of receiving the Gospel. Originally in the book of Acts, [the Jews]{.class_3429} had the first privilege of receiving the Gospel (Rom. 1:16). When the Jews, as a people, rejected the Gospel, the Lord took that privilege away from them and gave it to [the Gentiles. ]{.class_3429}In the Tribulation that privilege [will return to the Jews. ]{.class_3429}

That is how the Lord messes men up. He chooses those Jews as a nation, and that Gentile says, "I don't believe that[ Old Testament;]{.class_3429} it's a bunch of bunk. The Jews aren't God's chosen people." Then the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_310}Lord goes to the Gentiles, and the Jews say, "I don't believe all that stuff about Jesus Christ. He was born illegitimate. I don't believe that [New Testament. ]{.class_3429}The Gentiles are believing a bunch of bunk." The Lord is tricky.

Now look at what He says about that Jew. In Esther 1:19, He calls that Jew ["better" ]{.class_3428}than those Gentiles. How's that for "racial discrimination?" When the Lord finally gets through with that Jew, he is [better ]{.class_3429}than any Arab or "Palestinian." He's [better ]{.class_3429}than any German or Frenchman. He's [better ]{.class_3429}than any Chinese or Japanese. He's [better ]{.class_3429}than any Englishman or American. And he's [better ]{.class_3429}than any African---wherever he lives. But you see, that is Israel restored to that nation's proper place in God's plan. [That is not now.]{.class_3429}

Right [now]{.class_3429}, every Jew is like every Gentile. They are all sinners under the judgment of God for their sin (Rom. 3:9). But when those ["times of refreshing shall come from the presence of the Lord," ]{.class_3428}and Israel has been forgiven for rejecting the Messiah, then things change. When the "fullness of the Jews" comes in (Rom. 11:12), this old world will experience new life and new wealth (Rom. 11:15). That is what the Lord means when He says that Jewish bride will be [better ]{.class_3429}than the Gentiles.

Until then it is nothing but God using one nation to judge another nation for its sins. Israel messes up, so the Lord brings [Babylon ]{.class_3429}in and wipes them out. The kings of Babylon get proud and defile God's property (Dan. 5--6), and the Lord sends the [Medes ]{.class_3429}and the [Persians ]{.class_3429}in to wipe them out. While He's doing that, He is already making plans to use the [Greeks ]{.class_3429}to wipe out the Persians. And when the Greeks do that, the Lord says, "I'm going to let Rome get you." When [Rome ]{.class_3429}finally becomes too corrupt to stand, the Lord sends in the Vandals, the Huns, the Ostrigoths, and the Visigoths and gets rid of them. Then the Lord sends someone else to wipe them out, and so on and on.

You may ask who is the author of war? THE LORD IS! Bob Jones Sr. said, "War is God's judgment on sin here; Hell is God's judgment on sin hereafter." Here is the UN (the United Nuts) trying to get rid of war. You can't possibly get rid of war until you get rid of [sin. ]{.class_3429}The problem is sin, [not war.]{.class_3429}

Modern politicians are like a bunch of men in a kitchen where all []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_311}the faucets in the sinks are running full blast with the sinks plugged up. Water is overflowing all over the kitchen floor. Each of those men has a bucket and mop, and each of them is frantically trying to clean up the mess [without turning off the faucets.]{.class_3429}

The problem with man is not [war ]{.class_3429}and has never been [war]{.class_3429}. War is a symptom that manifests the disease. All of man's efforts at "peace" are like these over-the-counter cold medicines: they offer temporary relief without getting rid of the sickness. If you stop one war, another will follow soon enough. It's just a matter of time because all you have done is [temporarily relieved the symptom.]{.class_3429}

War is God's judgment on [sin]{.class_3429}. The Lord won't let the nations live like they live without killing them. P.S. THE LORD WON'T LET AMERICANS LIVE THE WAY THEY LIVE EITHER WITHOUT KILLING THEM OFF.

The ruling of verse 22 is one of the most controversial passages in this whole book---at least for modern women's libbers. Jamieson, Faucett, and Brown say that this decree led to the universal enslavement of all women. But putting all of the commentators aside, let's see what God has to say about ["the word of Memucan"]{.class_3428} (vs. 21). First Corinthians 11:3, ["the head of every man is Christ; and the head of the woman is THE MAN." ]{.class_3428}Paul also said that bishops and deacons were to [rule well]{.class_3429} in their own houses (1 Tim. 3:4, 12).

A man's house is anyone who lives under his roof over whom he has responsibility. That's his wife, and in America, that's any children under 18. After they are 18, he is not responsible for them any more. They are "on their own," and they are accountable to God and the government. As long as they are in Daddy's house, they are subject to his rule.

He says in Ephesians 5:22--24, ["Wives, submit yourselves unto your own husbands, as unto the Lord. For the husband is the head of the wife, even as Christ is the head of the church\...Therefore as the church is subject unto Christ, so let the wives be to their own husbands in every thing."]{.class_3428}

["The word of Memucan"]{.class_3428} just happened to be an almost verbatim quote of God Almighty. Genesis 3:16, ["Unto the woman he ]{.class_3428}\[God\] []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_312}[said\...thy desire shall be to thy husband, and HE SHALL RULE OVER THEE."]{.class_3428}

The advice that Memucan gave to Ahasuerus is the God-ordained order in the home from Genesis 3 to Revelation 20 (and perhaps beyond). The "rule" of that man in the home is never abrogated or rescinded [anywhere ]{.class_3429}in the entire Scriptures.

Ladies, a man will [rule ]{.class_3429}a home, or he will [wreck ]{.class_3429}it. There are two ways that a man can wreck a home. [The first is if you try to run him. ]{.class_3429}If he doesn't like it, he will tell you to go take a "flying leap," and he'll go find someone else. That way ends up in adultery and divorce, and the whole thing will blow all to pieces.

The [other way]{.class_3429} he can wreck it is if he is weak himself and not right with the Lord. I know in that case that someone has to rule, and the only person who can at that point [is the woman,]{.class_3429} but that home will still be ruined. If the fellow won't take responsibilities and won't be responsible for decisions and won't take the responsibility for making a living and paying the bills, the home will go down the tube [that way.]{.class_3429}

The answer to the situation in the home is for the man to be a real ruler and not a jellyfish. With rule comes [responsibility]{.class_3429}.

In New York harbor stands the Statue of Liberty. Right beside it should be another statue: the Statue of [Responsibility]{.class_3429}. Too many people, these days, want liberty without the [responsibility ]{.class_3429}that goes along with it. If you have liberty without responsibility, you will tear everything to pieces, and that is exactly what has happened to this country since 1964.

Just go to a ballgame and listen to the way the crowd reacts to the National Anthem. You will hear the crowd go crazy when "the land of the free" is sung. They will scream and holler and yell and carry on. "Yeah, we're free!" What they mean is "We can do whatever we d--- please." [That's]{.class_3429} what they mean.

But when it comes to "the home of the brave," all of a sudden the screaming stops. [Modern Americans want to be free without paying the price of freedom.]{.class_3429}

At PBI we give the students liberties here that they would not have at any other Christian school in the world. If you don't believe it, just check out places like PCC, BJU, and Tennessee Temple. But where you have [liberty]{.class_3429}, you have to have [responsibility]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_313}. The students have to be responsible enough to get their own housing, to buy and prepare their own food, to get and keep a job that will pay the bills, to study on their own, to get enough sleep, to pay their own medical expenses. We are not going to tell them when to get up, when to go to work, what job to do, when to go to the dining common to eat, when and where they can study, or when to go to bed. [That's their responsibilities.]{.class_3429}

If a man is going to run his own home, then he should be [responsible ]{.class_3429}for what goes on in that home. If he won't take [responsibility]{.class_3429}, then he can't run the home. One of the characteristics of the men in the Bible, who do what they are supposed to do, is that they rule their own households. The Lord said of Abraham that he would ["COMMAND his children and his household after him" ]{.class_3428}(Gen. 18:19).

Do you know why men like Abraham and Joshua were great? One of the reasons is that neither one of them would consult their wives about [anything ]{.class_3429}when it came to doing right. When God asked Abraham to sacrifice Isaac, he never went to Sarah and asked her what she thought of it; he just obeyed God. I heard Jim Modlish preach a good sermon on that, one time. Modlish said there were three reasons Abraham was able to pass that test. The first was that Abraham got up early in the morning. The second was that he [heard ]{.class_3429}as well as listened. The third reason was that [he didn't talk to Sarah about it.]{.class_3429}

Joshua never asked his wife before he said ["as for me and my house, we will serve the LORD" ]{.class_3428}(Josh. 24:15); [he made the decision for them. ]{.class_3442}If any of them had not liked it, I can assure you that he or she would not have been a part of his ["house" ]{.class_3428}anymore. [They would have gotten "the boot."]{.class_3442}

Some of you who read that last statement are probably thinking right now, "Oh, Ruckman, you are so hard." You think that because you are living like the devil, or at least [thinking ]{.class_3429}like him.

When my son Mike got about 19, we had the argument about the length of his hair. All my kids came up in the public schools, and I had to fight "the Battle of the Hair" about once every six months. At that time, he was telling me that he wasn't going to get it cut. He said, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_314}"Well, you told me that when I got old enough to whip you that I could leave home, and I'm old enough to whip you."

I told him, "All right, leave; I'll help you pack."

Then he said, "I want to stay."

I said, "If you stay, you get it cut."

He said, "OK, but I'm still big enough to whip you."

I told him, "Don't bet on it, boy. You can't stay awake forever."

And he said, "Yeah, you'd do it too; you'd do it."

I said, "You bet your life I'd do it."

I can whup any man alive. All I have to do is let him [go to sleep]{.class_3429} and then get a gas pipe and "let him have it"!

I learned a long time ago that when you're a little guy, you have to do something to get the advantage over the bigger guy. I also learned that you shouldn't be too tough because you have to go to sleep [sometime]{.class_3429}. You had better learn to "get along" with folks.

Now, when it comes to this matter of the home, fellows, if God tells you what to do and shows you what to do and you know what's right to do, YOU DO IT. If your wife comes along, OK, and if she [doesn't,]{.class_3429} OK. If your mother comes along, OK, and if she [doesn't,]{.class_3429} OK. If your children come along, OK, and if they don't, OK---BUT YOU DO WHAT THE LORD TELLS YOU TO DO.

Jesus said, ["If any man come to me, and hate not his father, and mother, and wife, and children, and brethren, and sisters, yea, and his own life also, he cannot be my disciple" ]{.class_3428}(Luke 14:26).

What this modern Christian-celebrity, FM-station, family-oriented, let-your-wife-run-the-home crowd has forgotten is that, in the Bible, it is GOD FIRST,[ and everyone else last. ]{.class_3429}That doesn't mean that a husband shouldn't rule in love. That doesn't mean that a husband runs roughshod over his wife and abuses her physically or verbally. That doesn't mean that a husband ignores his wife's wishes and opinions all together. But it does mean that the husband follows the Lord [regardless of what his wife thinks,]{.class_3429} and the wife is to follow the husband as he follows the Lord. The wife is to help him to do that because [that was the reason for which she was created]{.class_3429} (see 1Cor.11:8--9 and comments in that Commentary).

Some of you ladies who read this might think that is the most []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_315}chauvinistic, "macho" thing that you have ever heard in your lives, and that is very true. But ladies, that chauvinistic, macho Book has given you more privileges, more luxuries, and more opportunities than any women on the face of the earth. If you don't believe that, go to any country where the Bible is [not ]{.class_3429}allowed or is [not ]{.class_3429}believed, practiced, and honored.

If you think that Bible is so bad, go live under Koranic law for a while and see how you fare. If you think Memucan and Paul are too hard on you ladies, get [Islam Unveiled]{.class_3429},[ Women in Islam]{.class_3429}, [Behind the Veil, ]{.class_3429}and the testimony of Aida White from the Bible Baptist Bookstore and see how [Mohammed ]{.class_3429}treats you women.

Go with me over to [India ]{.class_3429}sometime and see the women digging through garbage to find enough food to feed their families or hauling 50 pounds of bricks on their heads to earn enough money to live on. That's how Brahma, Vishnu, and Shiva treat their women in Hinduism.

Before leaving chapter 1, we should note one last thing in the text. Ahasuerus ["sent letters into all the king's provinces, into every province according to the writing thereof, and to every people after their language\...and that it should be published according to the language of every people" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 22).

There are [three ]{.class_3429}universal decrees made in the book of Esther, and they are sent out by post to every province and language in the Persian Empire. The first is here in Esther 1:22, and it is the decree for men to be rulers in their own households. The second is in chapter 3, verses 12--15, and it is the decree to kill the Jews. The third is the decree of Esther 8:9--14 for the Jews to defend themselves. There is a [fourth decree]{.class_3429} in 9:29--30 that is sent by post to all the provinces, but it is sent to the Jews only and not to every language. In each case, though, the decrees are pictures of the word of God going out to all parts of the earth.

[Doctrinally]{.class_3442}, these are pictures of the word of God being preached universally in the Tribulation. In Matthew 24:14, you have the ["the gospel of the kingdom" ]{.class_3428}being ["preached in all the world for a witness unto all nations." ]{.class_3428}In Revelation 14:6, there is an angel ["having the everlasting gospel to preach unto []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2493.xhtml_page_316}them that dwell on the earth, and to every nation, and kindred, and tongue, and people."]{.class_3428}

Those are two gospels that are not ["the gospel of the grace of God"]{.class_3428} (Acts 20:24) which Paul preached. Those gospels are not to be preached in the Church Age at all, and if anyone trusts those gospels [now]{.class_3429}, instead of the Gospel of 1 Corinthians 15:1--4 given to us by the Apostle Paul, that person is headed for Hell. A Christian is [not]{.class_3429} trusting Jesus as King (Matt. 24:14) or Creator (Rev. 14:6) to save him. He is trusting the [Saviour ]{.class_3429}who shed His blood to atone for his sins and who rose from the dead to take him to Heaven. A Bible-believing Christian believes in Christ as both King and Creator, [but that is not what he is trusting for salvation.]{.class_3429}

People in the Tribulation are presented with two messages: 1) the King is coming back to judge you, so you had better believe on Him and live according to His commandments (Rev. 12:17, 14:12); and  2) reject every false god and worship only the God who created the universe.

The first is for sinners at the [beginning ]{.class_3429}of the Tribulation, and the second is for sinners at the end of the Tribulation, [but neither one is a message to a sinner now to receive the New Birth. ]{.class_3429}You had better get those straight; 99 percent of Fundamentalist and Conservative scholars think they are all the same.

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml}

## Chapter 2 {.heading_98-0}

2:1 After these things, when the wrath of king Ahasuerus was appeased, he remembered Vashti, and what she had done, and what was decreed against her.

2 Then said the king's servants that ministered unto him, Let there be fair young virgins sought for the king:

3 And let the king appoint officers in all the provinces of his kingdom, that they may gather together all the fair young virgins unto Shushan the palace, to the house of the women, unto the custody of Hege the king's chamberlain, keeper of the women; and let their things for purification be given them:

4 And let the maiden which pleaseth the king be queen instead of Vashti. And the thing pleased the king; and he did so.

The ["fair young virgins" ]{.class_3428}of verse 2 once more place the text, [prophetically]{.class_3429}, in the Tribulation. Those virgins show up in Matthew 25:1--13 and Revelation 14:1--4. All these things in Esther are types. They may not fit the timetable exactly, but all the typology points toward a Tribulation situation. A Gentile bride has been put aside, and ["virgins" ]{.class_3428}are called out.

Vashti has been put away according to ["the laws of the Persians and the Medes."]{.class_3428} The decree (1:19) is unchangeable. She has no chance of recovery from the divorce: she is put away permanently. Therefore a remarriage, in such a case, is allowed.

What follows is that all of ["the fair young virgins" ]{.class_3428}throughout the Persian Empire are gathered by appointed officers and brought to the king's palace. There they are placed in the care of a eunuch who prepares these women for the king.

That was a royal order that could not be disobeyed. When it comes to freedom and self-determination, American women are spoiled rotten. They have no idea what it is like to be ordered around with absolutely no choice in the matter. The equivalent would be the President of the United States divorcing his wife and ordering the IRS to go around and collect all the pretty young girls in all the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_318}homes, from all 50 states, and have them sent to the White House where he would pick and choose the ones he wanted. Not even Slick Willie could get away with what that king did. Those Oriental kings had absolute power.

2:5 Now in Shushan the palace there was a certain Jew, whose name was Mordecai, the son of Jair, the son of Shimei, the son of Kish, a Benjamite;

6 Who had been carried away from Jerusalem with the captivity which had been carried away with Jeconiah king of Judah, whom Nebuchadnezzar the king of Babylon had carried away.

7 And he brought up Hadassah, that is, Esther, his uncle's daughter: for she had neither father nor mother, and the maid was fair and beautiful; whom Mordecai, when her father and mother were dead, took for his own daughter.

Now, up shows the first Jew mentioned in the book, and with him comes a problem. The problem is not that he was a Benjamite that was called a Jew. (The Jewish Rabbis make a big deal out of this since the term [Jew ]{.class_3429}is obviously associated with the tribe of [Judah. ]{.class_3429}But since Benjamin was a part of the Southern kingdom all along \[see comments on Neh. 2:6\], there was never really any problem to start with.)

The problem is with the ages of Mordecai and Esther. Verse 6 says, ["Who had been carried away from Jerusalem with the captivity which had been carried away with Jeconiah king of Judah, whom Nebuchadnezzar the king of Babylon had carried away." ]{.class_3428}If verse 6 refers to Mordecai (which it seems to do) and the Ahasuerus of Esther was Xerxes, then Mordecai would have been anywhere from 120 to 133 years old, depending upon whose chronology you accept and depending on Mordecai's age when he was taken captive by Nebuchadnezzar.

You must admit that is quite an age to fill the office of a prime minister over an empire. Daniel was only about 85 when he was made the first president over the Persian Empire, and he died before he was 100.

And if Mordecai were that age, how old would Esther be? Supposing that the brother of Mordecai's father (his uncle--vs. 7) was as old as Mordecai (which would make him born the same year as Mordecai), Abihail (Esth. 9:29) would have had to have had Esther when he was 100 or older for her to be one of the ["fair young virgins"]{.class_3428} (vs. 2).

Now, there is no easy solution to the matter. The "original Hebrew" and the "original manuscripts" do nothing to solve the problem at all, so we won't go running to them to get out of this jam.

Moreover, we won't go changing the text of the [Authorized Version]{.class_3429} to accommodate our ignorance of the text, which is exactly what the majority of the commentators do when they run across such a problem in the Scriptures. Instead of dealing with the text as it stands, they change it to meet their own preconceived notions of what the text should "mean." Frankly, we could care less what the text "means." We are more concerned with what it [says. ]{.class_3429}After all, God's reputation as the Author of Scripture is far more important than the reputation of any "scholar" on the face of the earth, be he "Christian" or otherwise, Conservative or Fundamental, or "good and godly."

Accepting and believing the text as it stands in the [King James Bible,]{.class_3429} four solutions present themselves.

The first is that Mordecai and Abihail were indeed that old. This is exactly what the Jewish commentators teach on the matter, and that could very well be. The problem with that view, [Scripturally]{.class_3429}, is that Esther takes place at the end of the Old Testament. We have not seen such extreme old age since Moses died at 120 in Deuteronomy 34:7. When Abraham begat children at 99 and beyond, that was a miracle of God (Rom. 4:19). If Mordecai and Abihail did live to be over 100, it would be very unusual.

Secondly, verse 6 could be referring to someone besides Mordecai. Some commentators think that the ["Shimei"]{.class_3428} of verse 6 was the same Shimei that cursed David (2 Sam. 16) and ["Kish"]{.class_3428} was the father of King Saul (2 Sam. 10). This would make both Shimei and Kish ancestral fathers, which the Bible often does (see Matt. 1 and comments in that commentary). Given the connection between ["Haman"]{.class_3428} and ["Agag"]{.class_3428} (1 Sam. 15), this is quite possible. But if []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_320}Shimei and Kish were the actual grandfather and great grandfather of Mordecai, then one of them could be the one who was carried into Babylon by Nebuchadnezzar. This would certainly bring Mordecai, Abihail, and Esther into more reasonable age brackets.

Then, the [Ahasuerus ]{.class_3429}of Esther could have been a king other than [Xerxes]{.class_3429}. The most ridiculous version of this view is espoused by Bullinger in his [Companion Bible. ]{.class_3429}Bullinger becomes so fouled up in his dating of the exilic and post-exilic periods (see Appendix 1) that he has the book of Esther take place during the [Babylonian ]{.class_3429}captivity. Bullinger equates the Ahasuerus of Daniel 9:1 (the father of Darius the Mede) with the Ahasuerus of Esther. According to Bullinger, the name of this king was Asteiages, and he reigned in the period of time between Daniel 4 and 5. Bullinger even has Esther giving birth to Cyrus (Ezra 1:1).

Of course, all of this flies in the face of what the Scriptures say. First, Cyrus was a [Persian ]{.class_3429}(Dan. 6:28), not a Median-Jew (Dan. 9:1). Second, Esther 1:1 is very clear that it is [Persia]{.class_3429}, not [Babylon]{.class_3429}, which is ruling the entire Middle East at this time. Notice Esther 1:3, ["the power of PERSIA and Media." ]{.class_3428}Esther 1:18, ["the ladies of PERSIA and Media." ]{.class_3428}Esther 1:19, ["the laws of the PERSIANS and the Medes." ]{.class_3428}Whenever the two kingdoms are mentioned together in the book of Esther, Persia always comes before Media. It is never ["the MEDES and Persians" ]{.class_3428}as it is in Daniel. You say, "What's so important about that?" Well as anybody knows who has studied the book of Daniel, the Medes rule the Medo-Persian Empire first; then the Persians become more powerful and take over, and it becomes the Persian Empire. That's not just secular history; that's Bible prophecy (Dan. 8:1--3).

Now, if Ahasuerus is someone else besides Xerxes, the most reasonable candidate would be Darius I of Ezra 5--6. Scofield, using Ussher's chronology, places the dates for Esther at 521 B.C. to 509 B.C. According to Floyd Jones' [The Chronology of the Old Testament: A Return to Basics ]{.class_3429}(see Appendix 1), this is the time of the solo reign of Darius I, the father of Xerxes. This would make Mordecai around 80 years old in Esther. If that were the case, Esther would be seated as the queen-mother in Nehemiah 2:6 (cf. Dan. 5:10).

But probably the best explanation is that most chronologies on the Persian kings are "off." If Floyd Jones is right and Darius I reigned jointly with Xerxes from 505 B.C. to 485 B.C., and if the Artaxerxes of Nehemiah 1:1 was Xerxes (see Appendix 1), then the events of Esther could have taken place during this joint reign. This would end up solving all the problems involved in this passage. Mordecai would have been around 100; Esther could have been born when Abihail was around 80; the queen of Nehemiah 2:6 could have been Esther when she was married to Xerxes; and all of this would explain Artaxerxes' favorable reaction toward Nehemiah. Of course this series of events would take place much earlier than most of the chronologies allow, but it would not be the first time that most of the Scholars' Union was off because they were judging the Bible by secular history (e.g., the identity of the Pharaoh of the Exodus; see the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Exodus]{.class_3429}).

Verse 7 introduces Esther into the narrative. Her Hebrew name is [Hadassah]{.class_3429}; it means "myrtle." [Esther]{.class_3429} is a Persian name which means "star." It is another name for [Ishtar]{.class_3429}. In astrology, it was used as another name for the planet [Venus]{.class_3429}, the morning star.

Mordecai was Esther's older cousin and, apparently, the only surviving member of her family. As earlier noted, her father's name was Abihail (vs. 15), and he and Esther's mother were both dead at this time. Mordecai took and raised Esther as ["his own daughter."]{.class_3428}

2:8 So it came to pass, when the king's commandment and his decree was heard, and when many maidens were gathered together unto Shushan the palace, to the custody of Hegai, that Esther was brought also unto the king's house, to the custody of Hegai, keeper of the women.

9 And the maiden pleased him, and she obtained kindness of him; and he speedily gave her her things for purification, with such things as belonged to her, and seven maidens, which were meet to be given her, out of the king's house: and he preferred her and her maids unto the best place of the house of the women.

What you see in these verses is the hand of God working behind the scenes. There was no reason for ["Hege" ]{.class_3428}(also spelled ["Hegai,"]{.class_3428} []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_322}vss. 8, 15) to favor Esther above the hundreds of other young ladies that were there unless God was moving the heart of the man.

When Daniel and his three friends were taken by Nebuchadnezzar to be wise men, the Bible says that ["God gave them knowledge and skill in all learning and wisdom" ]{.class_3428}(Dan. 1:17) until Nebuchadnezzar found them ["ten times better\...in all matters of wisdom and understanding\...than all the magicians and astrologers that were in all his realm" ]{.class_3428}(Dan. 1:20). When God sent those Jews into captivity, He didn't desert them in His anger. He gave them whatever they needed to [survive]{.class_3429}.

In another chapter, Haman shows up, and he wants to wipe out every Jew on the face of the earth. The Jews are going to need someone in a high position who has the ear of the king himself. So into the harem comes this orphaned Jewish girl. She doesn't have the money to buy any perfume or makeup. She has no one to do her hair or nails. She's just one girl among a thousand (Ecc. 7:28). But when that chief eunuch looks at her, the Lord touches that man's heart. He rushes (["speedily"]{.class_3428}) to get her all the lotions and potions and notions she needs to make her skin soft and her body smelling like a rose garden. He even gets seven "beauticians" (["seven maidens"]{.class_3428}) to spruce her up. Esther winds up getting the top spot in the harem (["the best place of the house of the women"]{.class_3428}). God is positioning that girl to become the queen of every thing from India to Ethiopia just so[ she can save her people.]{.class_3429}

2:10 Esther had not shewed her people nor her kindred: for Mordecai had charged her that she should not shew it.

11 And Mordecai walked every day before the court of the women's house, to know how Esther did, and what should become of her.

Esther hides the fact that she's a Jew at the command of her cousin Mordecai (vs. 20). Hegai doesn't know her race, and the issue is never brought up.

Mordecai obviously has some position of authority in the king's court. Verse 19 says that he ["sat in the king's gate." ]{.class_3428}The [gate ]{.class_3429}of a city in Bible times was where the [city elders]{.class_3429} conducted the business of the city and where the [judges ]{.class_3429}held court (Deut. 16:18; Ruth 4:1--[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_323}2). In the king's palace, his officers sat at the gate and carried out their duties so they could be available if the king called for them (Esth. 6:4--5). Mordecai's position allowed him access to the outer court of the king's harem. No common man from off the streets would be allowed anywhere near it.

2:12 Now when every maid's turn was come to go in to king Ahasuerus, after that she had been twelve months, according to the manner of the women, (for so were the days of their purifications accomplished, to wit, six months with oil of myrrh, and six months with sweet odours, and with other things for the purifying of the women;)

13 Then thus came every maiden unto the king; whatsoever she desired was given her to go with her out of the house of the women unto the king's house.

14 In the evening she went, and on the morrow she returned into the second house of the women, to the custody of Shaashgaz, the king's chamberlain, which kept the concubines: she came in unto the king no more, except the king delighted in her, and that she were called by name.

These young ladies had to be purified a whole year before the king would marry them. That's a long engagement, and it's based on one thing: a woman was unclean before she was married. You must admit, that's not a very high estimation of women if it takes 12 months to get them clean enough to be married.

Verse 14 shows you how an Oriental ruler treated the women in his harem. Each of these young ladies had to spend the night with the king. Each one could take anything with her which she thought could persuade the king to choose her as his chief wife, the queen. But if she wasn't chosen, she wasn't [released ]{.class_3429}to go and lead an ordinary life. She was relegated to the status of a [concubine ]{.class_3429}and kept in the harem until the king decided he wanted to be with her again, which in some cases might be [never]{.class_3429}.

That same situation continues to exist in Islam today. Mohammed married 14 wives (although his followers are only allowed to have [four]{.class_3429}) and had relations with any number of his slave girls that he desired---with Allah's permission, of course ([]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_324}[don't you know!]{.class_3429}). The most infamous of these marriages was to a nine-year-old girl who brought her dollies with her when she came to have her "marriage" consummated.

A Southern Baptist pastor in Jacksonville, Florida (Jerry Vines of First Baptist Church) received a lot of flak from the Moslems for calling Mohammed "a demon-possessed pedophile." THAT'S [EXACTLY]{.class_3429} WHAT HE WAS. Mohammed was a habitual fornicator who foamed at the mouth and snored like a camel when receiving revelations from "Gabriel."

Do you think Ruckman's "just talkin'"? Then get the documented evidence from the Bookstore. It's a comic book called [Mohammed's Believe It or Else!]{.class_3429} It gives the quotations and references in [The Koran]{.class_3429} and [The Hadith,]{.class_3429} Islam's two most "holy scriptures," for everything I said. Whatever you do, don't take my word about anything. [Look it up,]{.class_3429} and don't be as stupid as George W. Bush all of your life.

2:15 Now when the turn of Esther, the daughter of Abihail the uncle of Mordecai, who had taken her for his daughter, was come to go in unto the king, she required nothing but what Hegai the king's chamberlain, the keeper of the women, appointed. And Esther obtained favour in the sight of all them that looked upon her.

16 So Esther was taken unto king Ahasuerus into his house royal in the tenth month, which is the month Tebeth, in the seventh year of his reign.

17 And the king loved Esther above all the women, and she obtained grace and favour in his sight more than all the virgins; so that he set the royal crown upon her head, and made her queen instead of Vashti.

18 Then the king made a great feast unto all his princes and his servants, even Esther's feast; and he made a release to the provinces, and gave gifts, according to the state of the king.

19 And when the virgins were gathered together the second time, then Mordecai sat in the king's gate.

20 Esther had not yet shewed her kindred nor her people; as Mordecai had charged her: for Esther did the commandment of Mordecai, like as when she was brought up with him.

God is working on Esther's behalf. Not only is ["Hegai the king's chamberlain, the keeper of the women" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 15) impressed with her, but ["Esther obtained favour in the sight of all them that looked upon her."]{.class_3428} That is quite a coincidence if God is not taken into account. Here is "love at first sight;" not from merely one man, but from everyone who looks on the girl.

Verse 16 is another one of the important doctrinal verses in Esther. In type there is a post-Tribulation rapture of a Jewish bride that takes place. Notice that it takes place ["in the seventh year of his reign." ]{.class_3428}In type that's the seventh year of the Tribulation. But it takes place ["in the tenth month."]{.class_3428}

Now, on our calendar the tenth month is October. But look at that "Oct" at the beginning of the word. That's not the prefix for [ten]{.class_3429}. That's [eight]{.class_3429}; as in [oct]{.class_3429}opus and [oct]{.class_3429}agon and [oct]{.class_3429}ogenarian. The prefix for ten is [dec]{.class_3429}; as in [dec]{.class_3429}imal and [deci]{.class_3429}meter and [dec]{.class_3429}imate. So December is actually ["the tenth month" ]{.class_3428}according to the meaning of the word.

When Ahasuerus chooses Esther to be his queen, it is ["the tenth month," ]{.class_3428}he makes ["a great feast," ]{.class_3428}he gives every one in the empire a day off (["he made a release to the provinces"]{.class_3428}), and he ["gave gifts, according to the state of the king" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 18). Now, what holiday falls in December and is characterized by feasting, a day off, and gift-giving?

You say, "Dr. Ruckman, what could Christmas possibly have to do with a post-Tribulation rapture?" ["And they that dwell upon the earth shall rejoice over them, and make merry, and shall send gifts one to another; because these two prophets tormented them that dwelt on the earth" ]{.class_3428}(Rev. 11:10).

In that passage, the two witnesses have been slain by the [Antichrist]{.class_3429}. Their bodies lie in the streets of Jerusalem for three and a half days. During that time, the Scriptures say, ["And they that dwell upon the earth shall rejoice over them, and MAKE MERRY, and shall SEND GIFTS one to another."]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_326} And lo and behold, while the [Christmas parties]{.class_3429} are going on and people are singing about Rudolph the Drunken Red-Nosed Reindeer and Santa Claus getting stuck in the chimney and the presents are being unwrapped, there is a [post-Tribulation rapture]{.class_3429} (Rev. 11:11--15 cf. Rev. 14). The Scriptures locate, [within four days,]{.class_3429} the day and month of the post-Tribulation rapture of Jewish saints.

Notice once again the term ["virgins" ]{.class_3428}showing up in the context of a post-Tribulation rapture. In Revelation those ["virgins" ]{.class_3428}are gathered the first time down on earth in chapter 7, and they are gathered ["the second time" ]{.class_3428}in Heaven in chapter 14. In Matthew 25, they are gathered together to wait for the bridegroom to return from the wedding, and then they are gathered together again to enter into the house with the bridegroom and his bride.

Verse 20 is self-explanatory, and we have already discussed it in our comments on verse 10.

2:21 In those days, while Mordecai sat in the king's gate, two of the king\'s chamberlains, Bigthan and Teresh, of those which kept the door, were wroth, and sought to lay hand on the king Ahasuerus.

22 And the thing was known to Mordecai, who told it unto Esther the queen; and Esther certified the king thereof in Mordecai's name.

23 And when inquisition was made of the matter, it was found out; therefore they were both hanged on a tree: and it was written in the book of the chronicles before the king.

Verse 21 describes an assassination plot against Ahasuerus by two of his doorkeepers. Now, you wouldn't think that God would use a murderous conspiracy to accomplish His purpose, but He does. Psalm 76:10 says, ["Surely the wrath of man shall praise thee: the remainder of wrath shalt thou restrain." ]{.class_3428}That's what happens here.

These two chamberlains get mad at the king and decide to kill him. Mordecai just happens to discover the plot. He tells Esther, and Esther tells the king ["in Mordecai's name" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 22). The king investigates the matter. He sends out Dragnet, Columbo, Hawaii 5-0, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_327}and all of those guys and finds out that the thing is so. Teresh and Bigthan are hung for "conspiracy to commit murder."

Those Oriental kings were despots; they were dictators. They were [absolute dictators]{.class_3429}, much more so than Hitler. A real Oriental despot, like those Persian kings, could have you executed at his command. There was no trial or anything else to get you "off the hook." If they wanted you dead, all they had to do was speak the word. Those Oriental despots had power.

Mao Tse-tung holds the world's record for mass murders by an Oriental dictator. During the time he was "Chairman" of China, he had [45 million people]{.class_3429} killed (some estimates go as high as [80 million]{.class_3429}).

The Bible says of Nebuchadnezzar that ["whom he would he slew; and whom he would he kept alive; and whom he would he set up; and whom he would he put down" ]{.class_3428}(Dan. 5:19). That's absolute power.

The greatest Oriental dictator the world has ever seen will show up in the next several years. He will rule over every nation on this earth with ["a rod of iron" ]{.class_3428}(Psa. 2:8--9, Rev. 19:15). Have you ever been hit with a galvanized iron pipe about 3 foot long and an inch thick? It will break your bones!

That's what that [scepter ]{.class_3429}which a king holds represents. It is not merely a symbol of power; it stands for a [club ]{.class_3429}which a king might use to beat down his enemies. That's the kind of king that Jesus Christ will be when He returns. He crushes around two million UN troops under His feet, and then He keeps the nations "in line" with an [iron scepter.]{.class_3429}

Chapter 2 ends with ["it was written in the book of the chronicles before the king" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 23). Nothing is done (at least then) to reward Mordecai for his loyalty to the king. For all practical purposes the incident is buried and forgotten in the national archives of Persia. But there it sits, just waiting for the Lord to bring it to the attention of Ahasuerus at the right time. The Lord[ will]{.class_3429} get praise out of the wrath of ["Bigthan and Teresh," ]{.class_3428}but at the same time He is working quietly, where no one sees Him, on behalf of His people.

Now, there is a great practical lesson here for the New Testament []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2619.xhtml_page_328}believer. Christian, nothing you do for the sake of Jesus Christ is forgotten. It is written down ["in the book\...before the king."]{.class_3428} One of these days, at the Judgment Seat of Christ, the Lord will open the books and honor you for your faithfulness to Him. Christ Himself said, ["Thy Father, which seeth in secret, shall reward thee openly" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 6:18). The Apostle Paul said, ["And let us not be weary in well doing: for in due season we shall reap if we faint not" ]{.class_3428}(Gal. 6:9).

The day will come when the One who made the universe will stand you up before His creation and publicly commend you for a job well done, [but that doesn't happen now down here on earth!]{.class_3429} Right now it's the [cross]{.class_3429}, not the [crown. ]{.class_3429}The problem with modern Christians is that they want their "dessert" without having to eat their spinach, and that's not how the Christian life works. You will get your inheritance in God's time, and if you serve to get the reward [in this]{.class_3429} [life, ]{.class_3429}then you end up with nothing [in Heaven]{.class_3429} (Matt. 6:16).

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml}

## Chapter 3 {.heading_98-0}

3:1 After these things did king Ahasuerus promote Haman the son of Hammedatha the Agagite, and advanced him, and set his seat above all the princes that were with him.

2 And all the king's servants, that were in the king's gate, bowed, and reverenced Haman: for the king had so commanded concerning him. But Mordecai bowed not, nor did him reverence.

3 Then the king's servants, which were in the king's gate, said unto Mordecai, Why transgressest thou the king's commandment?

4 Now it came to pass, when they spake daily unto him, and he hearkened not unto them, that they told Haman, to see whether Mordecai's matters would stand: for he had told them that he was a Jew.

Haman is the "bad guy" in the plot; he's the villain. The Bible contains 33 original plots that are the basis for every novel, movie, and TV program you have ever seen. The most basic plot is the story of a woman who is in danger of losing her love, her money, her property, or her reputation. To help her out is a [hero]{.class_3429}. He is always put out of action three-quarters of the way through the story, but he always makes a [miraculous recovery ]{.class_3429}and shows up at the last minute to defeat the villain. The villain is the one who is out to get the woman. It seems that he is able to knock the hero clean out of commission, but at the end, they have a [one-on-one confrontation]{.class_3429} in which the hero whips the villain.

It doesn't make any difference whether it's Robin Hood and Maid Marion, or the Black Pirate, or Zorro and the Madonna, or Perry Mason trying to win the court case, or Ironsides (in the wheelchair) trying to solve the crime. There will always be that hero and victim (who is usually a [woman]{.class_3429}).They can change the last "face-off" to two horses running or a fight in the engine of a train or a helicopter after a motorcycle or a struggle on the edge of a cliff or a quick-draw in the middle of the street or a shootout in a warehouse. All you are []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_330}doing is watching the same thing over and over and over again. You're just wasting your time and wearing your eyeballs out.

The old-time versions were even closer than that. [The hero always came on a white horse. ]{.class_3429}The horse was called Rex. The next time he's called Trigger. Then he's named Silver. It's the same plot played out over and over. You change the [costumes ]{.class_3429}and the [scenery ]{.class_3429}and the [names ]{.class_3429}to keep the sucker watching the junk.

The same thing can be said of every fiction story in every magazine and book on the shelf. It can be a detective story, a western story, or a romance. It's all the same baloney, cut thin. You'll just burn your eyeballs out reading that stuff.

If you have seen something that wasn't that plot, I bet you that I could find it in a [King James Authorized Version,]{.class_3429} published over 392 years ago. I just bet that you've never seen or heard a story whose basic plot (or plots) I couldn't find in that Book.    

Have you heard the story about the king who disguised himself? [That's in there. ]{.class_3429}How about the fellow who wanted to marry his true love and ended up marrying someone else? [That's in there. ]{.class_3429}How about the brothers who got mad at each other and one of them ended up killing the other? [That's in there. ]{.class_3429}How about the fellow who lost his inheritance? [That's in there too.]{.class_3429}

Don't kid me! All Hollywood and New York and Chicago do is change the scenario. Instead of Cain and Able, it's a couple of business partners on the "outs" with each other, and one partner kills the other. Instead of the prodigal son losing his inheritance ["with riotous living," ]{.class_3428}it's a young man who loses [the ranch]{.class_3429} in a poker game at the saloon. They change the [setting ]{.class_3429}of the story, and they make you think that you have something new. It's nothing new;[ it's all in the Book.]{.class_3429}

Now, you take this story here. Haman is the bad guy; he's out to get those Jews. When the Jews celebrate Purim, the book of Esther is read to the children, and every time the name [Haman]{.class_3429} shows up, the kids all make a bunch of noise and hiss and boo.

That's what we did when I was a boy. We didn't just sit back and watch anything; we [participated]{.class_3429}, brother. When the hero would come on the screen, we would all clap and yell. When the villain appeared, we would all boo and hiss. (Of course, I was a little different; I would always applaud [the villain]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_331}. I always was eccentric. I was one of those kids who liked the [monsters]{.class_3429}.)

The movie would always get going good. The hero would be fencing with someone and swinging from a curtain and jumping over pots; a lot of action, you know. Then some woman would show up and ruin the whole movie. The hero would take the girl in his arms to kiss her, and we would all yell out, "Mush! Mush!" (The only way I could enjoy it was to [pretend he was strangling her.]{.class_3429})

When that villain came on the scene, you never had to [guess ]{.class_3429}who he was. He looked like a bad guy. He usually wore black, and he had a black handlebar mustache. You just knew he was no good the first time you saw him.

The hero would come in clean-cut and shaven. He would [never ]{.class_3429}smoke a cigarette, not him. He would [never ]{.class_3429}drink; it was out of the question. That's how different [our ]{.class_3429}heroes were from this modern bunch. Even the bad guys were classier. If you watch those old gangster movies, the gangsters always wore a suit, tie, and hat. Your modern day [heroes]{.class_3429} look like they fell off the back end of a dumpster.

In the plot of the Book of Esther, [Haman ]{.class_3429}is a type of the Devil. [Esther ]{.class_3429}is a type of the Jewish nation. The [king ]{.class_3429}is a type of God the Father and the Lord Jesus Christ. You have a Tribulation setup. The book of Revelation, then, is the original plot.

In that plot, the [woman ]{.class_3429}(Israel) is running for her life. The [villain ]{.class_3429}(the Devil) is out to get her. The [Hero ]{.class_3429}(Jesus Christ) has been killed and buried. But He comes up from the dead and makes a [miraculous recovery]{.class_3429}. He shows up at the [last minute ]{.class_3429}to face off with the villain, and when He shows up, He comes with [a cavalry]{.class_3429} from "Fort Knox." After He defeats the villain, He marries the woman, and they have a [honeymoon ]{.class_3429}for a thousand years. Then they move into the Father's house, [and they live happily ever after.]{.class_3429}

Now, instead of Mordecai being promoted for saving the king's life, Haman is advanced to the position of the chief prince. Although he is not given the same title, he is in much the same position as Daniel was in Daniel 6. We would call him a "prime minister," today.

Notice that he is called ["the Agagite;" ]{.class_3428}that is, he was descended from [Agag]{.class_3429}. Who was Agag? Turn to 1 Samuel 15:8. Agag was a king over the [Amalekites ]{.class_3429}during the reign of Saul in Israel. God []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_332}commanded Saul to utterly destroy the Amalekites for ambushing Israel in the wilderness in Exodus 17:8--16. Verse 16 of Exodus 17 is where God swears eternal war against the nation of Amalek.

It goes further than that. Look at Numbers 24:20. When the Lord says that ["Amalek was]{.class_3428} [the first of the nations"]{.class_3428} He doesn't mean that they were the first people to become a nation (Gen. 10); [He means that they were the first nation to attack]{.class_3429} Israel when the nation came out of Egypt. As a result God had a special "grudge" against Amalek.

In Numbers 24:7, the Lord says that ["his ]{.class_3428}(Jacob's) [king shall be higher than Agag, and his kingdom shall be exalted."]{.class_3428} So the Lord is going to bless Israel and spread them out and make [that nation's]{.class_3429} king (eventually Jesus Christ) more powerful than the king of the Amalekites. Moreover, He says back in Numbers 24:20, ["his latter end shall be that he perish for ever." ]{.class_3428}Amalek has the same fate as ["all the nations that forget God" ]{.class_3428}(Psa. 9:17).

What does God have against Amalek besides the attack on Israel? Well, the first thing is that the nation is descended from [Esau]{.class_3429}, the rejected son of Isaac (Gen. 36:12--16). He said, ["Jacob have I loved, but Esau have I hated" ]{.class_3428}(Rom. 9:13, Mal.1:2--3). Amalek was also descended from a [Hamitic mother]{.class_3429} (specifically a Canaanite---Gen. 36:2, 12), a woman of a [cursed]{.class_3429} race.

Why is that so "relevant to today's issues"? [Those are the same people Israel is battling right now. ]{.class_3429}The people that are called [Palestinians]{.class_3429} today are nothing more than [the mongrelized remains of the Canaanites, the Amalekites, the Edomites, the Ishmaelites, the Midianites, the Philistines,]{.class_3429} and an assorted mix of various other Hamites of the Arabian area (see comments under Genesis 10 in that Commentary). They have sworn thirteen times, since 1948, that[ their goal is the complete extermination of the State of Israel]{.class_3429} (see [Israel: A Deadly Piece of Dirt]{.class_3429}). So the events that are about to occur in chapter 3 are simply a "dress rehearsal" of what is happening now and in the near future in the land of Israel. The only difference is that when the "Haman" of Revelation 13 gets into power, he will make the "original" look like a Sunday walk in the park. The Antichrist will nearly succeed where Haman and Hitler failed: he will wipe out the entire Jewish race with the exception of a small remnant (see []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_333}comments on Rom.9--11 in that commentary).

Back in 1 Samuel 15, instead of doing what he was told, Saul spared Agag as a kind of trophy of his triumph over the Amalekites. Although ["Samuel hewed Agag in pieces before the LORD in Gilgal" ]{.class_3428}(1 Sam.15:33), evidently at least one of Agag's children must have survived. [Haman is a direct descendant of Agag.]{.class_3429}

Now, what you have in chapter 3 is the beginning of a showdown that should have taken place in 1 Samuel 15, if Saul had obeyed the Lord and had killed all of the Amalekites as he was commanded. [You have a descendant of Agag]{.class_3442} facing a Jew from the tribe of Benjamin. [Saul was from the tribe of Benjamin,]{.class_3442} and he was given direct orders from God to wipe the Amalekites out. There is also a chance that [Mordecai ]{.class_3442}was a direct descendant of the house of Saul (Esth. 2:5 cf. 2 Sam. 16:5, 1 Sam. 9:1--2). So God is about to close the books on the Amalekites as a nation, and[ He is going use a relative of Saul to do it.]{.class_3442}

Brethren, the Lord keeps long accounts. The colored folk say, "De Lawd's ways am tedious, but they am sho'."

One of these Christian financial advisors says that God is not a bookkeeper. He's crazy, man; he doesn't know what in the world he's talking about (Rev. 20:12). I have lived to see God pay me back in kind, in my 60s and 70s, for things I did in my 20s[ ]{.class_3428}and 30s (see [The Full Cup]{.class_3429}, Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1998). Don't you worry; the Lord will settle [all ]{.class_3429}accounts. If He doesn't settle them down here, He will settle them at the Judgment, but He will settle them.

Verse 2: ["And all the king's servants, that were in the king's gate, bowed, and reverenced Haman: for the king had so commanded concerning him. But Mordecai bowed not, nor did him reverence." ]{.class_3428}That's a violation of Romans 13:1--4. Mordecai is disobeying a [direct order]{.class_3429} from the king. The reason he's not bowing is because he's a Jew (vs. 3), and he knows what God said about Amalek. He's in a similar circumstance as Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego were in Daniel 3.

In Daniel 3, the three Hebrew children wouldn't obey a king's commandment to bow to an image. Those who saw them reported their defiance to Nebuchadnezzar, who had them thrown into the fiery furnace. They wouldn't [bow]{.class_3429}, they wouldn't [bend]{.class_3429}, and they wouldn't [burn]{.class_3429}.

Similarly, [Mordecai ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_334}disobeyed a king's command to bow to a man whose race was cursed by God. Those who saw him reported his defiance to Haman, who then planned a campaign of genocide against the entire Jewish race. Mordecai won't [bow]{.class_3429}, he won't [bend]{.class_3429}, and he won't be [killed]{.class_3429}.

Now, those things are foreshadows of the Antichrist and his image in Revelation 13. That Jew was told, when he came out of Egypt, that he was to have [no statues and no images. ]{.class_3429}When he fooled around with images in the book of Judges, he suffered for it. When [Solomon ]{.class_3429}fooled around with images he busted up his kingdom. When [Manasseh ]{.class_3429}gets to messing with them, God draws the line on Judah and sends them into captivity under Zedekiah, when the women were burning incense to ["the queen of heaven" ]{.class_3428}(Jer. 44:19) and the priests were burning incense to images on the walls of the temple chambers (Ezek. 8:10--11). If the Jew learned one thing through those 1,000 years from the exodus to the captivity, he learned DON'T BOW DOWN TO [IMAGES!]{.class_3429}

Then up shows Jesus Christ. He is ["the express image" ]{.class_3428}of God (Heb. 1:3, 2 Cor. 4:4). Thomas bows down to ["the image"]{.class_3428} and says, ["My Lord and my God" ]{.class_3428}(John 20:28). An Orthodox Jew thinks that we Christians are a bunch of idolaters, AND WE ARE! We Bible-believing Christians "idolize" Jesus Christ, and He's God's "image." Of course He is an image made by God Himself (Heb. 10:5, 2:9); He's not a [graven ]{.class_3429}image or a [molten ]{.class_3429}image or an icon or a statue or anything like that. But you can see the Jews' way of looking at things.

That Jew had finally come to the place that never again would he bow down before something that was physical that he could see. The only person to whom he would bow was Jehovah; that Bible says that ["No man hath seen God at any time" ]{.class_3428}(John 1:18). Having rejected the Lord Jesus Christ, the Lord will put them into a position of choosing between the Devil's Christ and bowing down to his image (Rev. 13:15) or choosing the Lord's Christ and being killed (Rev. 12:17, 14:1--12).

In the passage before us, Mordecai is operating according to that lesson the Jews learned: don't bow down or reverence anything you can see. He won't bow before Haman because there is more involved than just a polite bow or a greeting or a normal display of honor. There is [reverence ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_335}involved. The bow here is on the knees with the face on the ground as one would kneel before God (Dan. 6:10, Eph. 3:14).

3:5 And when Haman saw that Mordecai bowed not, nor did him reverence, then was Haman full of wrath.

6 And he thought scorn to lay hands on Mordecai alone; for they had shewed him the people of Mordecai: wherefore Haman sought to destroy all the Jews that were throughout the whole kingdom of Ahasuerus, even the people of Mordecai.

7 In the first month, that is, the month Nisan, in the twelfth year of king Ahasuerus, they cast Pur, that is, the lot, before Haman from day to day, and from month to month, to the twelfth month, that is, the month Adar.

When Haman sees that Mordecai won't bow to him, he "loses it," as the teenagers say: he "blows his stack"; he "flips his lid." With everyone in the whole city of Shushan fawning over him, Haman gets upset because one man ignores him.

"The mountains of worldly honor are always covered with a perpetual snow."

It must be horrible to have such an emotional constitution that if one guy in church doesn't speak to you it ruins your whole day. That would be like living in Hell, man. I can't think of a worse way to live. What a terrible way to live: to have your happiness and contentment dependent on the attention others show you! Don't ever get yourself in a fix like that.

Here is Haman. He's getting all of the adulation that anyone could ever want. But one guy---just one guy---bothers him because he won't bow down.

Verse 6 establishes Haman as a type of the Antichrist. That unreasoning desire to kill every Jew is a Satanic thing (Rev.12). That means that Hitler was a foreshadow of the Antichrist.

I have, in my library, an illustrated book on the life Adolph Hitler by John Toland. One of those pictures shows Hitler's ID card in the Austrian Nazi party before he ever came to Germany. There sits Hitler with 50 Austrian Nazis (all Roman Catholic; there wasn't a []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_336}Protestant in the bunch), holding his ID card. The cards of each member are numbered, and Hitler's number just happens to be 555.

The next world dictator to appear on the world scene is Number 666.

Brethren, the God who set up this universe, the God of Mathematics, has His own computer system. Somewhere on this earth, at some time in human history, there has been a 111 (Caesar), a 222 (Constantine), a 333 (Charlemagne), and a 444 (Napoleon). Number 777 is Jesus Christ coming back, and then the whole thing is over. The computers are so far behind that they don't know what they are doing. Each of those men had a number attached to them, without anyone, intentionally, assigning a number to them.

When the New Heavens and New Earth show up, the Godhead, itself, will be 888. Eight is the number of something new. What number shows up after eight? It's nine, and nine is the number of[ fruitfulness.]{.class_3429}

Do you want to see something "peculiar"? (Stewart Custer would call this one of Ruckman's "peculiar teachings.") Take the title [King James 1611 Holy Bible. ]{.class_3429}Count the number of letters in [King James]{.class_3429}. It's [nine. ]{.class_3429}Count the number of letters in [Holy Bible]{.class_3429}. It's [nine]{.class_3429} too. Now, add up the numbers in [1611]{.class_3429}. What a "coinkidinky;" that just happens to be nine as well.

Brethren, do you know what you hold in your hand when you hold a [King James Bible? ]{.class_3429}You have a Book that is ["for ever\...settled in heaven" ]{.class_3428}(Psa. 119:89). Jesus said, ["Heaven and earth shall pass away, but my words shall not pass away" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 24:35). Peter said, ["The grass withereth, and the flower thereof falleth away: But the word of the Lord endureth for ever"]{.class_3428} (1 Pet. 1:24--25).

The Scriptures are God's 999. They are ["seed" ]{.class_3428}(Luke 8:11) which bears fruit (Matt. 13:23).

In verse 7, Haman is deciding [when]{.class_3429} he will carry out his genocide against the Jews, and he does it by ["lot." ]{.class_3428}A lot is simply a random chance method of choosing a thing. So you reach in the bin and draw the lucky number, you spin the wheel to see where the clicker lands, you draw straws, you cut the cards, you flip the coin, or you cast the dice. That last method is probably what is used here.

Haman has the dice (the Hebrew word being ["Pur"]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_337}) cast to see the day and the month he should kill the Jews. First he finds out the day, which turns out to be the [thirteenth]{.class_3429}, and then he finds out the month, which turns out to be the [twelfth ]{.class_3429}month: ["the month Adar."]{.class_3428}

Notice something about the Jewish calendar in verse 7. The first month has two names. It is called ["Nisan" ]{.class_3428}here. In Exodus 13:4 (cf. Exod. 12:2) it is called ["Abib." ]{.class_3428}[Abib ]{.class_3429}is the Hebrew word for the spring when the corn is young and green. Because the Jewish calendar is a lunar calendar it loses 11 days every year, so the Lord gave the month of the Passover as the first month of spring to keep the calendar on track. To do this, the Jews add a thirteenth month 5 times during a 19 year cycle. Otherwise, eventually, Passover would fall back to winter, then to summer, etc. That is what happens to Moslem holidays which follow a lunar calendar that has no standard to keep it in line with the solar year. [Nisan ]{.class_3429}is the current name for the first month of the Jews religious calendar. It, and all the other names of the Jewish months, were adopted from the Babylonian calendar during the years of exile there.

Now, you take that business about "casting the lot." Those are all games of [chance]{.class_3429}. But Proverbs 16:33 says, ["The lot is cast into the lap; but the whole disposing thereof is of the LORD." ]{.class_3428}That simply means that you can "pay your money and you can takes your chances,"[ ]{.class_3428}but when the time comes for the [pay-off,]{.class_3429} it is [God ]{.class_3429}who determines the outcome. If the dice turn up "snake-eyes," it is the Lord who did it. If you "hit the jackpot," the Lord gave you the winning numbers to test you or destroy you, but it was [God ]{.class_3429}who did it.

That is why games of chance are off[ ]{.class_3428}limits for Christians. If you are a Christian, nothing happens to you by accident or by chance. The promise is ["all things work together for good to them that love God, to them who are the called according to his purpose"]{.class_3428} (Rom. 8:28---see comments in that commentary).

Of course, there are always circumstances of life that you cannot control and the outcome is just as much a gamble as if you "shot craps" in Vegas. Farming is a [gamble]{.class_3429}. There is no way to control the weather or bugs or disease completely. A contractor takes a [gamble ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_338}every time he makes a bid on a contract. He is gambling all he has on the economy being the same, on wages not going up, on his workers finishing the project on schedule, etc. He has to take a chance on all of that, see? But those kinds of things are done to make an honest living [by working]{.class_3429}.

When a Christian risks his money on "games of chance," he is actually tempting God. He is daring God to give him a good hand or to give him the lucky numbers or to let the wheel land on the right spot just so he can get riches [without working for them.]{.class_3429}

Before the Holy Spirit was given in Acts 2, God's people used the "lot," but it was not for purposes of gambling. They were seeking God's will in an area where it wasn't readily revealed by Scripture or prophets. They realized and acknowledged God's providence in the matter, and usually it was a matter of life and death (such as Josh. 7:14--26, 1 Sam.14:38--44, and Jonah 1:5--15). The lot was always a [serious ]{.class_3429}matter (such as Acts 1:21--26).

A Christian's games should be games of [skill ]{.class_3429}and [ability]{.class_3429}. Games like chess and checkers are games that require some knowledge and skill to play and win. There is nothing left to chance. Physical games, like volleyball, football, softball, tennis, and golf, are permissible games. They require skill and ability to play. You have to compensate for the environment and the actions of others. That's not chance. Games of [skill ]{.class_3429}are legitimate games for a Christian; games of [chance ]{.class_3429}are not.

3:8 And Haman said unto king Ahasuerus, There is a certain people scattered abroad and dispersed among the people in all the provinces of thy kingdom; and their laws are diverse from all people; neither keep they the king's laws: therefore it is not for the king's profit to suffer them.

9 If it please the king, let it be written that they may be destroyed: and I will pay ten thousand talents of silver to the hands of those that have the charge of the business, to bring it into the king's treasuries.

10 And the king took his ring from his hand, and gave it unto Haman the son of Hammedatha the Agagite, the Jews' enemy.

11 And the king said unto Haman, The silver is given to thee, the people also, to do with them as it seemeth good to thee.

From the time that the Medes and the Persians took over, in Daniel 6, the Jews are always being accused of disobeying the laws of the kings. Daniel was accused by the other two presidents in Daniel 6:12--13. Accusation is brought against the Jews in Ezra 4:6 and again in Ezra 4:11--16. When Nehemiah begins to build the wall, the charge of rebellion is leveled against the Jews of Jerusalem (Neh. 6:6--7).

[Things haven't changed any. ]{.class_3429}Since the UN's inception in 1945, over half of the resolutions passed (450 out of 700) have been against the State of Israel. The Jews have been accused of genocide against the Palestinians, even though they simply reacted to bombing attacks by the Palestinians incited by Moslem threats to[ annihilate the State of Israel]{.class_3429} (13 of them since 1948). They have been accused of stealing land from the Palestinians, even though the land was taken when six Islamic States [attacked Israel ]{.class_3429}in an unprovoked war.
