They have been accused of creating the Palestinian refugee problem, even though the "refugees" left Israel due to [Moslem death threats]{.class_3429} before the Six Day War and thousands of "Palestinians" who entered Israel after the war had never lived there before the war.

Having said all of that, I am by no means saying that the Jews are guiltless of any wrong-doing. Don't you worry. The Lord knows the faults of His chosen people better than anybody, and He will take care of them in His own good time.

But when you hear a bunch of Gentiles bringing all kinds of accusations against the Jews, mark it down that they [want something those Jews have. ]{.class_3429}It's an envious, covetous spirit that drives a Gentile's animosity towards that Jew. In the case here in Esther, Haman craves Mordecai's [reverence]{.class_3429}, and he's not getting it. So he accuses the Jews falsely and seeks to exterminate them.

When it comes to the New Testament, envy drove those Jews to level the same type of accusations against Jesus Christ and His followers. They said in Acts 17:7, ["These all do contrary to the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_340}decrees of Caesar, saying that there is another king, one Jesus." ]{.class_3428}When the Jews brought Jesus before Pilate, Luke 23:2 says, ["And they began to accuse him, saying, We found this fellow perverting the nation, and forbidding to give tribute to Caesar, saying that he himself is Christ a King." ]{.class_3428}The people who are trying to do something for God in any age will always be accused at some point of breaking the law because[ they are following a different King.]{.class_3429}

The word ["suffer," ]{.class_3428}in verse 8, means "to allow" or "to put up with." The idea , here, is that since these people are law breakers and disobedient to the king, that the king shouldn't put up with their foolishness anymore and, in the context here, should not allow them to live anymore.

Now, Haman's proposition to the king is this: "Pass a law to have these people destroyed, and I will pay for everything" (vs. 9). He's going to borrow the money from the treasury and then pay it back. Haman will "foot the bill" and pay the money to hire the troops to kill the Jews.

The ring of verse 10 is a [signet]{.class_3429} ring; that is, it is a ring with a symbol on it peculiar to the user; it acts as his signature. It was used much as a [brand ]{.class_3429}was used in the Old West. Wax was melted and placed at the bottom of a document. Then the king would press his ring into the soft wax as a signature of his approval. Having thus been sealed, the document became[ law.]{.class_3429}

When Ahasuerus gave Haman his signet ring, he was giving him the full authority of his office. With it, Haman could pass any law, and it would become permanently binding under ["the laws of the Persians and the Medes"]{.class_3428} (see comments under Esth. 1:19).

Verse 11 is a picture of God the Father giving the Devil permission to work someone over. Paul said of the unrepentant saint, living in a state of continually committing gross sin, ["To deliver such an one unto Satan for the destruction of the flesh"]{.class_3428} (1 Cor. 5:5).

If you want to see how that works, turn to Job 1:12. There the Lord tells Satan, ["all that he hath is in thy power; only upon himself put not forth thine hand." ]{.class_3428}The second time He gives Satan permission to work Job over, He says, ["Behold, he is in thine hand; but save his life" ]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_341}(Job 2:6).

It's permissive power from God given to Satan. Satan is called ["the god of this world" ]{.class_3428}(2 Cor. 4:4), and he has been given all the ["power" ]{.class_3428}and ["glory"]{.class_3428} of ["the kingdoms of the world" ]{.class_3428}(Luke 4:5--6). Hebrews 2:14 says that Satan has ["the power of death."]{.class_3428}

In the context here, the Lord is giving the Jews' enemies permission to kill them.

Now, that's what the Jews don't understand. Jewish children have been told all of their lives that [they ]{.class_3429}are God's chosen people and the [Gentiles ]{.class_3429}aren't. So they don't understand why God allows the pogroms in Russia or the Holocaust in Germany. They aren't worshipping idols anymore, so why does God allow things like that to happen? As a result, many Jews today are [atheists]{.class_3429}. Some of the Rabbis are even teaching that God is not all powerful (["omnipotent," ]{.class_3428}Rev. 19:6): He stops what He can, but He can't do [everything.]{.class_3429}

The answer to the problem is found in Deuteronomy 28.Whenever something catastrophic happens to those Jews, God allows it, or even [causes ]{.class_3429}it, because of national sin. Read Deuteronomy 28. Look at verses 32 and 33. That is God turning those Jews over to a bunch of Gentiles to be persecuted. Look at verses 49--52. That is [God ]{.class_3429}raising up a Gentile nation to [kill ]{.class_3429}those Jews. Why? Verse 45: ["because thou hearkenedst not unto the voice of the LORD thy God."]{.class_3428}

The question the Jews should be asking themselves is not "Why is God allowing these things to happen to us?" but "[What have we done]{.class_3429} to cause God to do this to us?" The [answer ]{.class_3429}is found in the New Testament. Jesus Christ said, ["And the Father himself, which hath sent me, hath borne witness of me. Ye have neither heard his voice at any time, nor seen his shape. And ye have not his word abiding in you: FOR WHOM HE HATH SENT, HIM YE BELIEVE NOT" ]{.class_3428}(John 5:37--38).

When the Jews had Christ crucified, they said, ["His blood be on us, and on our children" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 27:25). Mel Gibson may have taken that out of his "Passion" movie to appease the Anti-Defamation League, but that is what they said. God is simply giving them what they asked for. They said, ["We have no king but Caesar" ]{.class_3428}(John 19:15). So God let the [Roman ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_342}general Titus come in A.D. 70 and crucify 500 of them along the road to Jerusalem and then raze the temple to the ground. He gave them [Roman Catholics]{.class_3429} in the Middle Ages to put yellow stars on them, crowd them into ghettos, and burn them in the Inquisition. He gave them Russian Orthodox (Eastern [Catholics]{.class_3429}), ruled over by a Czar (Caesar), to harass them with pogroms. He raised up Hitler and the concentration camp commandants (all of them [Roman Catholics]{.class_3429}) to kill six million of them in the gas chambers.

Why? [Because that's what they said they wanted,]{.class_3429} and because they wouldn't listen to what the Lord told them about [His Son]{.class_3429}. God will continue to let the Gentiles oppress the Jews, with the help and cooperation of the [Roman Catholic Church,]{.class_3429} until they repent of turning His Son over to the [Romans ]{.class_3429}to be crucified (Acts 2) and believe on Him as their Messiah. A remnant does that in Revelation 7, and they wind up in Heaven after the Antichrist kills them. A final remnant does that in Zechariah 12 at the Second Advent, and that's when God destroys the Gentile nations that are after them and cleanses the nation of Israel of its sin of rejecting Christ (Acts 3:19--21).

Given all of that, what should the [Bible-believing]{.class_3429} Christian's attitude be toward the Jews and the nation of Israel?

Well, people like Texe Marrs look at that Jew, and they reason this way: those Jews rejected their Messiah and had Him crucified. They persecuted the early Christians and rejected the Gospel. God is mad with them and scattered them among the nations. Most of them are atheists, today, and don't even believe in Jehovah God any more. The [Antichrist ]{.class_3429}will be a Jew, and Jerusalem is called ["Sodom and Egypt"]{.class_3428} (Rev. 11:8). Moreover, the Lord only promised them the Land if they were obeying Him. After all He drove them out for being disobedient in the first place. How can He let them back in if they are still rejecting Christ? Therefore, the Jews are back in the Land[ against God's will]{.class_3429} (or by the will of Satan---Texe Marrs), or they are not [real Jews ]{.class_3429}(Garner Ted Armstrong), or this is not the return predicted[ in Scripture]{.class_3429} (J. Vernon McGee). Anyway, the Jews have been [replaced ]{.class_3429}as God's people by "spiritual Jews" (Rom. 2), ["the Isarel of God"]{.class_3428} (Gal. 6:16), the true children of Abraham (Gal.3--4)---[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_343}the Church.

The conclusion reached by some of the brethren is that it is perfectly all right for the Palestinian Moslems to suicide bomb the Jews because the Jews "took their homeland" (though no "State" of Palestine has ever existed in the entire 5,000 year history of Canaan and even though it was the Moslems [who originally took the Land away from the Jews]{.class_3429}), "forced them into refugee camps" (even though the Palestinians abandoned their houses and lands due to Moslem death threats), "restricted their economy" (because the Palestinians were using their privilege to freely enter Jewish occupied areas as an opportunity to commit suicide bombings), and "brutalized and killed their fathers and children" (for throwing rocks and bottles and shooting AK-47s at Israeli forces in the Intifada).

Now, all of that stuff about the Jews rejecting Christ and persecuting the church in the book of Acts and rejecting the Gospel is true. The Antichrist [will ]{.class_3429}be a Jew, and Jerusalem [is ]{.class_3429}related to Sodom in this day and age---no matter which Testament you go by (Ezek. 16). But you have to watch your attitude in regard to these things. You can't be anti-Semitic. Whenever you curse that Jew, you place yourself under a curse (Num. 24:9; notice that that verse is about [Israel]{.class_3429}, not [Abraham]{.class_3429}). God may raise up someone to punish His people, [but don't let it be you]{.class_3429} (Matt. 18:7, Luke 17:1). Those Jews will be beaten enough without you adding your hand to it or rejoicing in it.

Concerning the Jew, a Christian is to be a "beloved enemy" (see Rom. 11:28 and comments in that commentary). Christians have [not]{.class_3429} replaced the Jews (Rom.11:1). Any other viewpoint is conceited ignorance (Rom. 11:25).

When it comes to the State of Israel, God only promised a [second]{.class_3429} return (Isa. 11:11), [not a third or fourth. ]{.class_3429}The present nation of Israel, then, is the fulfillment of that prophecy. Besides, if Israel doesn't believe on Christ until the Second Advent and Israel is already in the Land ([which they are]{.class_3429}---Zec. 12:10), common sense would tell you that they didn't return in belief. Why should they? [They didn't return in belief the first time: they were intermarrying with the heathen, and they were breaking the Sabbath]{.class_3429} (Ezra 10, Neh. 13).

The best thing that the United States could do in regards to Israel is to move its embassy from Tel Aviv to Jerusalem ([]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_344}[as the Congress voted to do under the Clinton administration]{.class_3429}) and to sign a military alliance with Israel. We might have the whole world against us, but at least we would have the blessing of God on our nation once more (Num. 24:9).

Verse 11 is self-explanatory. Ahasuerus gives Haman a "blank check" to do what he wants, and the king has no idea about who the people are.

3:12 Then were the king's scribes called on the thirteenth day of the first month, and there was written according to all that Haman had commanded unto the king's lieutenants, and to the governors that were over every province, and to the rulers of every people of every province according to the writing thereof, and to every people after their language; in the name of king Ahasuerus was it written, and sealed with the king's ring.

13 And the letters were sent by posts into all the king's provinces, to destroy, to kill, and to cause to perish, all Jews, both young and old, little children and women, in one day, even upon the thirteenth day of the twelfth month, which is the month Adar, and to take the spoil of them for a prey.

14 The copy of the writing for a commandment to be given in every province was published unto all people, that they should be ready against that day.

15 The posts went out, being hastened by the king's commandment, and the decree was given in Shushan the palace. And the king and Haman sat down to drink; but the city Shushan was perplexed.

["The thirteenth day of the first month" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 12) is the day before Passover. So this law to annihilate the Jews is written the day before the Jewish holiday[ commemorating the nation's deliverance from Egypt. ]{.class_3429}It is rather ironic no matter which way you look at it. From Haman's point of view, he was signing the Jews' execution order the day before the nation's birthday. From the Lord's point of view, Haman is going to end up just like [Pharaoh ]{.class_3429}in Exodus 14, and []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_345}he signs his own death warrant at the Passover season.

Now, in verse[ thirteen]{.class_3429} you have the decree that was written on the [thirteenth]{.class_3429} day, and it is a decree to kill all of the Jews. The number 13 in the Bible nearly always has a bad connotation. There are [thirteen words]{.class_3429} that end in [X]{.class_3429} in a King James Bible (box, Felix, flax, flux, fox, matrix, onyx, ox, Pollux, sardonyx, six, vex, and wax), and of those thirteen words, nine are connected with something bad somewhere in the Scriptures. (The teachers at Bob Jones University may mock us when we say watch out for words that end in [X]{.class_3429}[, ]{.class_3428}but that is because they are conceited---and [stupid ]{.class_3429}I might add. When I say "watch out for words that end in [X]{.class_3429}," I have a [Bible]{.class_3429} reason for saying that.)

I will not go into an in-depth discussion of the number 13 here. If you want to see the reality behind why the world avoids 13s like the plague, get my book on [Bible Numerics]{.class_3429} and a book by Pastor Paul Heaton called [Triskaidekaphobia ]{.class_3429}(both available from the Bible Baptist Bookstore). Between those two books you will get every reference in the Bible, both direct and indirect, to show why [hotels ]{.class_3429}don't have thirteenth floors, why there are no Gate 13s at [airports]{.class_3429}, why Apollo 13 was the only one of the [moon shots]{.class_3429} to fail to land on the moon, and why Friday the 13th is an "unlucky" day. The [King James Bible ]{.class_3429}runs the world whether anyone knows it or not and whether anyone wants it to or not.

Notice the word ["posts" ]{.class_3428}in verse 13. That is where we get [post office ]{.class_3429}and [postman ]{.class_3429}and [parcel post]{.class_3429}. The idea of the word is men on horseback carrying dispatches between fixed stations. In modern horse racing, the expression is "the horses are at the post;" i.e., they are at a stationary house to begin the race. Because the word is so closely connected with horses and riders, you get words like [postillion]{.class_3429}, which is the person who "guides the first pair of horses of a coach or carriage." Another common expression is [posthaste]{.class_3429}. It means to be quick about doing something, but originally it was taken from Henry VIII. He had sent out a rider with a message, and he said,[ "Post, haste]{.class_3429} for thy life." In other words, "Buddy, you had better hurry up and get this message where it's going super quick, or you're a [dead man."]{.class_3429}

Do you see how some English words can have several different meanings? [A post ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_346}isn't just a pole you stick in the ground. The scholars are always complaining about the [King James Bible]{.class_3429} being "archaic." Quite often those "archaic" meanings are still used in today's society. If you want the definitive work on the subject, get Dr. Laurence Vance's book [Archaic Words and the Authorized Version ]{.class_3429}(available from the Bookstore). Bro. Vance demonstrates from contemporary sources that "archaic" King James' words are still used today in the same way they were used in 1611. The problem is not with the[ King James Bible; ]{.class_3429}it is with a bunch of stupid, lazy people who aren't willing to [read ]{.class_3429}or [study]{.class_3429}.

Now, verse 13 and 14 contain some great preaching material. [Death is a universal decree against mankind. ]{.class_3429}"Life is short; death is sure." Romans 5:12, ["Wherefore, as by one man sin entered into the world, and death by sin; and so death passed upon all men, for that all have sinned." ]{.class_3428}Solomon said, ["There is no man that hath power over the spirit to retain the spirit; neither hath he power in the day of death: and there is no discharge in that war" ]{.class_3428}(Eccl. 8:8).

Unless the Rapture takes place, [everyone ]{.class_3429}will die; there is no way to avoid it. Therefore, it behooves every man to ["be ready against that day" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 14). That's a [devotional ]{.class_3429}application of that verse, you understand. It was actually written to the Gentiles getting ready to kill the Jews. But if you know that you are going to die, that's sage advice as well.

"The \$64,000 question" is. "Are you ready to die"? Have you made preparations for [death?]{.class_3429} I'm not talking about life insurance, picking out your coffin, or funeral expenses. After death, you are going to live somewhere forever. Have you prepared for it? The Lord called that rich fellow in Luke 12:20 a ["fool" ]{.class_3428}because he had made preparations for[ life on earth]{.class_3429}, but he had made none for [life after death]{.class_3429}.

There is a famous story used by preachers to illustrate this point. A certain king had a court jester who "played the fool" for him to keep him entertained. The jester played the fool so well that the king gave him a challenge. He gave the jester a fool's "scepter" made of pure gold and sent him to search throughout the kingdom for anyone who was a bigger fool than he was. When he found someone, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_347}he was to give that person the scepter and bring him to the palace to present him to the king. After several years of searching, the jester returned to the palace to find the king on his death bed.

The sickly king was cheered to see the jester and asked, "Did you find a bigger fool than yourself? Were you able to give your 'scepter' to anyone?"

The jester hung his head and replied, "No, sire, I was not. I found no fool bigger than myself."

"Well, no matter," said the king, "for I must leave you now anyway to go on a long journey, and no one will be able to accompany me on that trip to entertain me."

"Where are you going?" asked the jester.

"I do not know." replied the king sadly.

"What preparations have you made for this journey?" enquired the jester.

"None," said the king.

"Then, sire, I must present you with this golden scepter, for [you ]{.class_3429}are the biggest fool I have ever seen."

Verse 15: ["And the king and Haman sat down to drink; but the city Shushan was perplexed." ]{.class_3428}The order to kill all of the Jews goes out, and it sets the whole city to talking and wondering what was going on.

There were those who had no idea of what was going on. No Jew had ever done them any harm, and their philosophy was "live and let live." But they were in no position to say anything. Besides, it wasn't their neck on the chopping block.

I am sure there were some who completely agreed with Haman. A Jew had probably beaten them out of a job or business deal, and they were out for blood.

Then there was a small group who knew what was about to happen was wrong, and they began to make plans to hide the Jews and protect them.

That's the way it was in Germany during the Holocaust. Not every German or Catholic was a Jew-hating Nazi. There were a number of Germans, Dutch, and Polish, such as Corrie Ten Boom and Oskar Schindler, who saved Jews from the concentration camps. The Yad Vashem, the Holocaust organization in Israel, recognizes []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2696.xhtml_page_348}19,700 "righteous Gentiles" responsible for rescuing Jews (figure taken from the organization's website). But most Germans, though they had nothing against any Jew, were scared of doing anything lest they be shipped off to prison camps of their own.

Meanwhile, Haman and Ahasuerus are sitting around drinking and having a good time. Ahasuerus doesn't really know everything that's going on because Haman has hidden the Jews' identity from him, and Haman is gloating on the upcoming genocide of the Jews.

[Doctrinally ]{.class_3429}speaking, this passage points prophetically to the upcoming genocide which Satan and the Antichrist will attempt to carry out against the Jews (Rev. 12). During the Tribulation, the Jewish population of the world will be reduced to a tenth [or less]{.class_3429} of its present number (Isa. 6:10--13). There are approximately 14 million Jews in the world right now (2004). When the Antichrist gets through with them, there will be less than a million and a half. I would be surprised if 100,000 will survive.

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml}

## Chapter 4 {.heading_98-0}

4:1 When Mordecai perceived all that was done, Mordecai rent his clothes, and put on sackcloth with ashes, and went out into the midst of the city, and cried with a loud and a bitter cry;

2 And came even before the king's gate: for none might enter into the king\'s gate clothed with sackcloth.

3 And in every province, whithersoever the king\'s commandment and his decree came, there was great mourning among the Jews, and fasting, and weeping, and wailing; and many lay in sackcloth and ashes.

Verse 1 has three pictures of mourning. First, ["Mordecai rent his clothes." ]{.class_3428}That's a picture of the flesh being torn. In Hebrews 10:20, the veil of the temple is equated with Christ's[ flesh. ]{.class_3429}What's so important about that? God tore that veil in two just like men tore Christ's flesh.

Next, Mordecai ["put on sackcloth with ashes." ]{.class_3428}That sackcloth is a rough cloth like grave clothes. When a person put on sackcloth, it was a picture of being buried. The ["ashes" ]{.class_3428}are usually accompanied with dust, and they are sprinkled on the head (Job 2:12, 30:19, and 42:6). At funerals, when the minister commits the body to the ground, he says, "Ashes to ashes; dust to dust." So it is a symbol of [burial]{.class_3429}. The idea is the thing over which he is mourning is going to bring death to him.

Finally, he ["cried with a loud and bitter cry." ]{.class_3428}If we follow the progression of the pictures to their logical conclusion, then you have a picture of a man being tortured until he dies and ends up in Hell, where there is ["wailing and gnashing of teeth"]{.class_3428} (Matt. 13:50).

That's what happened to many a Jew in the concentration camps in Germany during World War II. They were arrested, imprisoned, and tortured. They were starved, beaten to death with shovels, raped, cut open while with child, buried alive, soaked in gasoline and burned, and slowly strangled to death. They were gassed, cremated, shot execution-style, and heaped into mass graves. And after all of [that]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_350}, they woke up in Hell for rejecting their Messiah.

That is a horrible thing. It's bad enough to go to Hell after living in a nice house, being well clothed, eating decent food, and having good health most of your life; but to go to Hell after living in [poverty ]{.class_3429}all of your life or going [hungry ]{.class_3429}all of your life, like they do in India, or being in pain or handicapped all of your life must be an especially terrible thing. You suffer like the devil all of your days, and you still wind up in the Lake of Fire forever: you get a [figurative ]{.class_3429}"hell here on earth" and a [literal ]{.class_3429}Hell after death.

I believe one of the most tragic books I have ever read was [For Those That I Loved ]{.class_3429}by Martin Gray. Martin Gray was a full-blooded Jew who survived the Holocaust. He went through the Warsaw Ghetto, lived through a Nazi death camp, fought with the Russian army at the Oder River, and finally escaped to America. He made his fortune and returned to France where he married an actress. After building a five-million-dollar chateau and raising four children, he lost [everything]{.class_3429}---his home, his automobile, his wife, and his children---in a forest fire. [He goes through all of that with no reference to God, prayer, or the Bible. ]{.class_3429}And when he dies, he dies lost and hits Hell too. Could anything be sadder or more tragic?

So what you have in verse 1 is a picture of a lost sinner dying and going to Hell. It's also a picture of that Jew suffering at the hands of the Gentiles for his sins (Lam.1:13--14, 2:3, 4:8, 5:10). The Lord will cause it to happen again, just like He did under Nebuchadnezzar, Titus, and Hitler, one more time before He returns to set things right (Zech. 14:2).

Finally, it is a picture of the Lord Jesus Christ suffering for our sins on the cross. Christ experienced the full gambit of suffering, both physical and spiritual, when He was crucified. The Old Testament picture is [Job ]{.class_3429}on the ash heap out in the city dump---[Gehenna]{.class_3429}.

Now, here's Mordecai. He's obviously in mourning for what's about to happen to his people. So instead of sitting ["IN the king's gate"]{.class_3428} (Esth. 2:19) where he is supposed to be, he ["came\...BEFORE the king's gate" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 2). He is outside, but he is not coming in. As we saw in Nehemiah 2:1--2, no one was allowed to come into the king's court sad or depressed.

That's quite a lesson for a Christian. In Psalm 100:2, 4, the Lord says,[ "Serve the Lord with gladness: come before his presence with singing\.... Enter into his gates with thanksgiving, and into his courts with praise." ]{.class_3428}That Oriental king wouldn't let you set foot in his presence if you were "down in the mouth." It's a good thing the Lord doesn't put the same restriction on us today!

Verse 3 shows that the scene with Mordecai (vs. 1) is repeated throughout the kingdom. All the Jews of the captivity are in ["mourning"]{.class_3428} for what is about to take place, and they have added ["fasting" ]{.class_3428}to their displays of sorrow. Although it not stated, [prayer ]{.class_3429}obviously accompanies the fasting as it does elsewhere in the Scriptures (2 Sam. 12:16, Dan.9:3, Neh. 1:4). The Jews are depriving themselves of food to seek God's help for their survival.

4:4 So Esther's maids and her chamberlains came and told it her. Then was the queen exceedingly grieved; and she sent raiment to clothe Mordecai, and to take away his sackcloth from him: but he received it not.

5 Then called Esther for Hatach, one of the king's chamberlains, whom he had appointed to attend upon her, and gave him a commandment to Mordecai, to know what it was, and why it was.

6 So Hatach went forth to Mordecai unto the street of the city, which was before the king's gate.

7 And Mordecai told him of all that had happened unto him, and of the sum of the money that Haman had promised to pay to the king's treasuries for the Jews, to destroy them.

8 Also he gave him the copy of the writing of the decree that was given at Shushan to destroy them, to shew it unto Esther, and to declare it unto her, and to charge her that she should go in unto the king, to make supplication unto him, and to make request before him for her people.

9 And Hatach came and told Esther the words of Mordecai.

10 Again Esther spake unto Hatach, and gave him []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_352}commandment unto Mordecai;

11 All the king's servants, and the people of the king's provinces, do know, that whosoever, whether man or woman, shall come unto the king into the inner court, who is not called, there is one law of his to put him to death, except such to whom the king shall hold out the golden sceptre, that he may live: but I have not been called to come in unto the king these thirty days.

12 And they told to Mordecai Esther's words.

Esther has no idea of the decree passed against the Jews (vs. 5). She does not know that all the Jews throughout the kingdom are wearing sackcloth and crying and fasting. In fact, if her "ladies in waiting" had not told her, she would not have known that Mordecai was in mourning.

Verse 4 says,[ "Then was the queen exceedingly grieved." ]{.class_3428}Esther loved Mordecai and did not want to see him sad. She wanted to have communion with him, but as long as he was clothed in the garments of sorrow, he could not come ["before the court of the women's house"]{.class_3428} (Esth. 2:11) and talk to her.

She tried sending him a new set of cloths, thinking that that would take his mind off his troubles, but he turned them down and sent them back to her. Then she sent one of her attendants, Hatach, to find out what was bothering Mordecai.

Evidently the queen and all of those in her house were quite sheltered from the outside world, for not even Hatach knew what Haman had done. ["The city Shushan" ]{.class_3428}may have been ["perplexed" ]{.class_3428}when the decree was made, but it was all news to Hatach. Mordecai had to explain the entire situation to him and actually give him a copy of the law passed by Haman so that Esther could know what going on.

Mordecai ordered Esther to ["go in unto the king, to make supplication unto him, and to make request before him for her people" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 8). You will remember that ["Esther did the commandment of Mordecai, like as when she was brought up with him" ]{.class_3428}(Esth. 2:20). So Mordecai laid a task on her; he gave her a duty to perform. He wanted her to go to the king and plead for []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_353}the lives of the Jews. It was an obligation she had toward her people.

But Esther had a problem. It was not a simple thing just to walk into the king's presence. The Persians had a law that no one could see the king unless the king [summoned ]{.class_3429}him. If a person came into the king's court [unbidden]{.class_3429}, he was to be put to death unless the king held out his golden scepter and welcomed him in (vs. 11).

That is a picture of entering into God's holiness. The Apostle Paul describes the Lord Jesus as ["dwelling in the light which no man can approach unto; whom no man hath seen, nor can see" ]{.class_3428}(1 Tim. 6:16). When Moses asked to see God's glory, the Lord told him, ["Thou canst not see my face: for there shall no man see me, and live" ]{.class_3428}(Exod. 33:18--20).

That's why Jesus Christ came to earth as a man. John 1:18 says, ["No man hath seen God at any time; the only begotten Son, which is in the bosom of the Father, he hath declared him." ]{.class_3428}Jesus told the Apostle Philip, ["He that hath seen me hath seen the Father" ]{.class_3428}(John 14:9).

Jesus Christ made it possible for me to go straight into the throne room and give my petition directly to the King (Heb. 4:16). He is the ["Sceptre" ]{.class_3428}(Num. 24:17) that God uses to bid us enter into His presence. I don't need Mary, Peter, or "blessed John the Baptist." I don't need a priest, a pope, or a "saint" to go to "bats" for me. I can bypass all the "receptionists" and go straight into the head office.

Esther, though, did not have that assurance. She had not been called by the king for a whole month, and she let Mordecai know it.

4:13 Then Mordecai commanded to answer Esther, Think not with thyself that thou shalt escape in the king's house, more than all the Jews.

14 For if thou altogether holdest thy peace at this time, then shall there enlargement and deliverance arise to the Jews from another place; but thou and thy father's house shall be destroyed: and who knoweth whether thou art come to the kingdom for such a time as this?

15 Then Esther bade them return Mordecai this answer,

16 Go, gather together all the Jews that are present in Shushan, and fast ye for me, and neither eat nor drink []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_354}three days, night or day: I also and my maidens will fast likewise; and so will I go in unto the king, which is not according to the law: and if I perish, I perish.

17 So Mordecai went his way, and did according to all that Esther had commanded him.

When Mordecai receives Esther's reply, he reminds her that she is a Jew too and will not escape just because she is the queen. It is in verses 13 and 14 that the purpose of God's providence is manifested. God knows that He made Esther queen just for this occasion, but if Esther won't fulfill the [purpose ]{.class_3429}for which God has placed her in the palace, then the He will find someone else to deliver the Jews. If He has to do that, though, then He will judge Esther's house and destroy it.

I have heard many a hillbilly preacher try to preach on verse 14. Nearly every preacher's fellowship I have attended in North Carolina has somebody trying to wax eloquent on ["who knoweth whether thou art come to the kingdom for such a time as this." ]{.class_3428}I have yet to hear one that I thought exposited the text even adequately.

If you were going to apply the text to a Christian, your applications would be very general. For instance you could say that God has placed you where you are for a specific reason and purpose. He has a task that He wants you to do where you are. If you don't do it, then the Lord will get someone else. If you fail to perform the task that the Lord has set for you, then you will lose the reward God had prepared for you and be relegated to God's "second best" for your life. But you couldn't get much more specific than that.

Now, Esther makes up her mind to go before the king and take a chance, but she asks Mordecai to have the Jews in Shushan fast and pray specifically for her for three days while she and her maidens do the same (vs. 16). If nothing else works, try [fasting and prayer. ]{.class_3429}Christ recommended fasting for hard cases (Matt. 17:21). The early church fasted (Acts 14:23). The Apostle Paul fasted often (2 Cor. 11:27). If there is some answer to prayer that you need really badly from the Lord, it won't hurt you to fast for it.

Esther's sentiments in verse 16 are a good way for Christians to handle the trying circumstances of life. Esther said, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_355}["If I perish, I perish." ]{.class_3428}Esther determined to trust God and do right even if it cost her her life.

When you come against a problem in life where if you make the "wrong" decision you are liable to "get it in the neck," the [first thing]{.class_3429} you need to do is pray about it steadily for three days; fast and pray if you need to. If you believe you know what the right thing to do is after [that ]{.class_3429}then step into the situation and take your chances. If you lose your shirt, "tough apples"!

If you gave the matter [serious prayer]{.class_3429} and have shown God that you [meant business,]{.class_3429} the Lord will take care of His part. He won't just sit in Heaven and do nothing if He sees you are serious about doing His will. If He sees that you mean business, He will either honor and bless what you have done as the right step or He will work out circumstances to get you out of the mess into which you have gotten yourself. He will actually overrule [your ]{.class_3429}stupidity.

Brethren, you need to be bold and act in difficult situations, but never act before careful prayer and consideration of God's will in the matter. When you do act, realize that you are taking a chance, but put yourself in God's hands. Job said, ["Though he slay me, yet will I trust in him" ]{.class_3428}(Job 13:15).

I always did like Joab's attitude in 2 Samuel 10:12. Joab is outflanked and surrounded. He sets his brother against the Ammonites, and he takes on the Syrians. In verse 11 he says, ["If the Syrians be too strong for me, then thou shalt help me: but if the children of Ammon be too strong for thee, then I will come and help thee." ]{.class_3428}He never makes any allowance for [both ]{.class_3429}being stronger than the Israelites. But in verse 12 he says, ["Be of good courage, and let us play the men for our people, and for the cities of our God: and the LORD DO THAT WHICH SEEMETH HIM GOOD."]{.class_3428} That is, whatever He decides, THAT'S IT! And if what He decides isn't what I consider to be good, TOO BAD!

If you try to do anything for God, that's the approach you [have]{.class_3429} to take. You have to be willing to do what's right whether the Lord says yes or whether He says no. You may not know [what ]{.class_3429}you are doing, but you are [willing ]{.class_3429}to do whatever the Lord tells you to do, and you are [willing ]{.class_3429}to take whatever the consequences are for doing []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_356}it.

Those three Hebrew children in Daniel 3:16--18 told King Nebuchadnezzar, ["We are not careful to answer thee in this matter. If it be so, our God whom we serve is able to deliver us from the burning fiery furnace\...BUT IF NOT, be it known unto thee, O king, that we will not serve thy gods, nor worship the golden image which thou hast set up." ]{.class_3428}[They were prepared to do right whether God delivered them or not.]{.class_3429}

As we end our comments on chapter 4, notice one thing in verse 17. Up to this point Esther ["did the commandment of Mordecai"]{.class_3428} (Esth. 2:20). Now, ["Mordecai went his way, and did according to all that Esther had commanded him." ]{.class_3428}The little girl has grown up. She has taken on some responsibility, and she is going to risk her life to do as Mordecai asked. So Mordecai reciprocates and does as she asks him to do.

Husbands, do you know there are sometimes when your [wife ]{.class_3429}is right, and you should do what she asks you to do, regardless of how you feel? When Sarah told Abraham to get rid of Ishmael, Abraham didn't want to do it, but God said, ["In all that Sarah hath said unto thee, hearken unto her voice" ]{.class_3428}(Gen. 21:12). When Sarah said that, she wasn't usurping Abraham's authority. She saw something about what God said about her son that Abraham didn't see because he loved Ishmael. The same apostle who said, ["Wives, submit yourselves unto your own husbands, as unto the Lord" ]{.class_3428}(Eph. 5:22), said, ["submitting yourselves ONE TO ANOTHER in the fear of the Lord." ]{.class_3428}You men are to honor that wife and dwell with her ["according to knowledge" ]{.class_3428}and treat her as an heir ["together of the grace of life" ]{.class_3428}(1 Pet. 3:7).

The same thing goes for the kids. Peter said, ["Likewise, ye younger, submit yourselves unto the elder. Yea, ALL OF YOU BE SUBJECT ONE TO ANOTHER"]{.class_3428} (1 Pet. 5:5). A Christian parent's goal should be to raise [his child]{.class_3429} to the point of taking on his responsibility as a believer and serving the Lord on his own. When he does that, there will be times when you will need to subject yourself to [him ]{.class_3429}just as he did to [you ]{.class_3429}when he was growing up.

That is what happens between Mordecai and Esther in verse 17. God used Samuel in that way to speak to Eli (1 Sam.3). In the New Testament, Paul told Timothy, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2820.xhtml_page_357}["Let no man despise thy youth; but be thou an example of the believers" ]{.class_3428}(1 Tim. 4:12).

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml}

## Chapter 5 {.heading_98-0}

5:1 Now it came to pass on the third day, that Esther put on her royal apparel, and stood in the inner court of the king's house, over against the king's house: and the king sat upon his royal throne in the royal house, over against the gate of the house.

2 And it was so, when the king saw Esther the queen standing in the court, that she obtained favour in his sight: and the king held out to Esther the golden sceptre that was in his hand. So Esther drew near, and touched the top of the sceptre.

3 Then said the king unto her, What wilt thou, queen Esther? and what is thy request? it shall be even given thee to the half of the kingdom.

4 And Esther answered, If it seem good unto the king, let the king and Haman come this day unto the banquet that I have prepared for him.

5 Then the king said, Cause Haman to make haste, that he may do as Esther hath said. So the king and Haman came to the banquet that Esther had prepared.

Esther has been fasting and praying for two of the three days for which she asked Mordecai. Chapter 5 opens on the third day of that fast. Esther feels confident now that she has an answer to her prayers, so she prepares to go in to see the king.

Notice the phrase in verse 1: ["it came to pass on the third day."]{.class_3428} In the Scriptures, that third day is the third millennial day from the birth of Christ. The Apostle Peter said, ["One day is with the Lord as a thousand years, and a thousand years as one day" ]{.class_3428}(2 Pet. 3:8). In Leviticus 23, God goes 7 days and has a Sabbath day on the seventh day. He goes 7 weeks from the Feast of the Firstfruits and has the Feast of Pentecost. He goes 7 months into the Jewish year and has the Feast of Trumpets, the Day of Atonement, and the Feast of Tabernacles. That's one month with [three ]{.class_3429}of the seven observed feasts in it, and it's the [seventh month]{.class_3429}. The Lord then has the land of the Israelites rest every seventh year. Then He []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_359}runs 49 years (that's 7 x 7) and has a Year of Jubilee.

Given the pattern, the present creation will run 7,000 years (a millennial "week," with each "day" being a thousand years according to 2 Pet. 3:8). The 7,000 years are divided by the birth of Christ with 4,000 years before and 3,000 years after. The seventh 1,000 years will be the Millennial rest of Hebrews 4. That would place the Second Advent at the end of the [second ]{.class_3429}millennial day from the first advent.

This timing occurs over and over again in the Scriptures. The picture in Esther 5:1 is a Jewish bride coming in before the King and being restored ["on the third day." ]{.class_3428}Turn to Hosea 6 and look at verse 1: ["Come and let us return unto the LORD: for he hath torn, and he will heal us; he hath smitten, and he will bind us up." ]{.class_3428}In the book of Hosea, Israel is pictured as the cast off wife of God the Father that is being taken back and remarried. Hosea 6:1 is Israel repenting and returning to her "husband." But look at [when]{.class_3442} the Lord receives the nation back again. Verse 2: ["After two days will he revive us" ]{.class_3428}(Second Advent) ["in the THIRD DAY" ]{.class_3428}(Millennium) ["he will raise us up, and we shall live in his sight."]{.class_3428}

If there is any doubt that verse 2 is speaking of the Second Advent, look at verse 3: ["Then shall we know, if we follow on to know the LORD: HIS GOING FORTH IS PREPARED AS THE MORNING; AND HE SHALL COME UNTO US AS THE RAIN, AS THE LATTER AND FORMER RAIN UPON THE EARTH." ]{.class_3428}That's the ["Sun of righteousness" ]{.class_3428}arising at the Second Advent (Mal. 4:2) and the early and latter rains that follow it (Joel 2:23) right in the same verse.

Let's go to Exodus 19:10--11. ["And the LORD said unto Moses, Go unto the people, and sanctify them today and tomorrow," ]{.class_3428}(two days) ["and let them wash their clothes, And be ready against THE THIRD DAY"]{.class_3428} (that's the Millennium, in type. Look at what happens when the Millennium begins) ["for the third day THE LORD WILL COME DOWN IN THE SIGHT OF ALL THE PEOPLE UPON MOUNT SINAI."]{.class_3428} That happens ["on the third day IN THE MORNING" ]{.class_3428}(Exod.19:16). Psalm 68:8--17 marks that event as occurring at[ the Second Advent]{.class_3429} (see comments in that Commentary).

Look at the New Testament in John 1:29. []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_360}["The next day John seeth Jesus coming unto him, and saith, Behold the Lamb of God, that taketh away the sin of the world." ]{.class_3428}Now, there's no doubt about that ["day" ]{.class_3428}in John 1:29. It's the first coming of Christ to earth to die for sinners, so it is the[ first day.]{.class_3429}

Now watch the progression here. John 1:35--36, ["Again THE NEXT DAY after John stood, and two of his disciples; And looking upon Jesus as he walked, he saith, Behold the Lamb of God." ]{.class_3428}That's the second thousand years since Christ appeared. It's the time when the Gospel of Jesus Christ is preached. Notice that John dropped ["that taketh away the sin of the world."]{.class_3428} That already took place.

So you have the first day in John 1:29 and the [second day ]{.class_3429}in John 1:35. Look at John 2:1 and watch the wording carefully: ["AND THE THIRD DAY there was a MARRIAGE in Cana of Galilee."]{.class_3428} That grouping of three days occurs over and over again in the Scriptures, and every time it occurs it is either a type of the Second Advent or events immediately preceding it or succeeding it. The Scriptures clearly point to a date of A.D. 2000 for the Second Advent.

Since this Commentary has clearly been written after A.D. 2000, I can hear the "brethren" crying "heretic, date-setter, cult leader." That is because they are either hard of hearing or they can't read or they are just as crooked as a dog's hind leg. In [every ]{.class_3429}sermon where I have preached on the Rapture or the Second Advent, and in [every ]{.class_3429}book in which I have covered this material, whenever I have hazarded [a guess ]{.class_3429}as to the date of the Rapture or the Advent (and all I have ever made are guesses; [I have never set a firm date for either event]{.class_3429}), I have always been careful to add the qualifying statement: ["if]{.class_3429} our calendar is right." I think it is more than apparent at the time of this writing (2004) that our calendar [is not right.]{.class_3429}

Moreover, [God quite often skips years when counting toward a certain event. ]{.class_3429}Take Matthew 1, for example. Look at verse 17: ["So all the generations from Abraham to David are fourteen generations; and from David until the carrying away into Babylon are fourteen generations."]{.class_3428} There most certainly were [not ]{.class_3429}fourteen generations from David to Jechonias (vs.11). Matthew purposefully []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_361}[dropped three generations of kings from verse 8 ]{.class_3429}because incest was involved in that part of the Davidic line. That was a period of seventy years (see comments in the [Bible Believer's Commentary on Matthew]{.class_3429}). The Lord didn't even count [Israel's years of servitude ]{.class_3429}during the times of the judges when he reckoned the years from the Exodus to Solomon's reign (cf. 1 Kings 6:1 with Acts 13:20 and see comments under Exodus 1:8 of that commentary). Job 3:6 says, ["As for that night, let darkness seize upon it; LET IT NOT BE JOINED UNTO THE DAYS OF THE YEAR, LET IT NOT COME INTO THE NUMBER OF THE MONTHS." ]{.class_3428}There are whole periods of time that God completely ignores.

When it comes to this matter of the Second Coming, brethren, all I can tell you anymore is this: there is nothing wrong with what is [in the Bible]{.class_3429}. It is those things [outside of the Bible]{.class_3429} that pose the problems. The Bible is very clear as to [the time]{.class_3429} of the Second Coming. The problem therefore is either with [our reckoning]{.class_3429} of time or with the unrevealed will of God in these matters, or both. The trick is not to change what the Scriptures [say ]{.class_3429}when you go by the Scriptures and it looks like the Lord has left you with "egg on your face." ["Let GOD BE TRUE, but EVERY MAN A LIAR" ]{.class_3428}(Rom. 3:4).

When my guesses about the Second Coming have been wrong, I have been disappointed, but not disillusioned. You see, I wasn't looking for my guesses to be right so [I could justify myself to those that follow me]{.class_3429} (as my enemies accuse me of doing when they call me a "cult leader"). [I was looking for the Lord to come back as I was commanded ]{.class_3429}(Tit. 2:13).

So when ["Esther put on her royal apparel," ]{.class_3428}that is a picture of a Jewish bride of Jehovah being restored after the Marriage Supper of the Lamb (Esth. 1).

Notice in verse 1 that ["on the third day\...the king sat upon his royal throne in the royal house." ]{.class_3428}In the New Testament, [during the Church Age, ]{.class_3429}the Lord Jesus Christ is not seated on any throne: He is presently seated at ["the right hand of God" ]{.class_3428}the Father (Mark 16:19; Acts 2:34--35;  Rom. 8:34; Eph. 1:20; Col. 3:1; Heb. 1:3, 8:1, 10:12; 12:2; 1 Pet. 3:22) making intercession for the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_362}saints. When we get to Heaven, we shall see Him upon the Judgment Seat of Christ, but that is not a [throne]{.class_3429}. In regards to His return, Jesus told those chief priests in Matthew 26, ["Hereafter shall ye see the Son of man sitting on the right hand of power, and coming in the clouds of heaven" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 26:64). So immediately before the Second Advent, He appears seated in the clouds of Heaven prepared to judge the earth (Rev. 14:14--16), but He is still seated at God's right hand.

But in Revelation 3:21, the Lord says, ["To him that overcometh will I grant to sit with me in my throne, even as I also overcame, and AM SET DOWN WITH MY FATHER IN HIS THRONE."]{.class_3428}

Go to Matthew 25 and look at verse 31. ["When the Son of man shall come in his glory, and all the holy angels with him, THEN SHALL HE SIT UPON THE THRONE OF HIS GLORY." ]{.class_3428}That is Jesus Christ sitting on the throne of David as Gabriel told Mary back in Luke 1:32. That throne is in Jerusalem, ["the city of the great King" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 5: 35, Psa. 48:1--2).

Now turn to Jeremiah 3: the chapter is about Israel being restored as the wife of Jehovah (especially verse 14). Watch what Jeremiah says in verse 17: ["At that time" ]{.class_3428}(Israel restored to the Land under her King) ["they shall call Jerusalem the throne of the LORD" ]{.class_3428}(Jehovah---God the Father). That ["King" ]{.class_3428}in Matthew 5:35 is Jesus Christ (cf. Matt. 25:34), but in Psalm 48:1--2 the ["King" ]{.class_3428}is called Jehovah (["the LORD"]{.class_3428}) and ["our ]{.class_3428}(the Jews') [God."]{.class_3428}

When Jesus Christ comes back, He returns and reigns as Jehovah God (Zech. 12:10, 14:9). When He does, He restores Israel and Jerusalem to their place over the United Nations, and the throne of David becomes the throne of God (Zech. 12:6--8). As the Son of God, He is able to make ["us kings and priests unto God and his Father" ]{.class_3428}(Rev. 1:6). As Jehovah, He establishes a new covenant of peace with Israel forever (Isa. 54:5--10, Jer.31:31--37) based on His righteousness.

Of course, the Campbellites and the Catholics have that all "screwed up." They have Christ sitting on a throne up in Heaven now. They have Him reigning now. So the reign of God is now, and the kingdom is "spreading" with [the king on the throne. ]{.class_3429}That means []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_363}that the wine-headed bachelor over in Rome thinks he's Jesus Christ and God Almighty. The egomaniac sits on a [throne ]{.class_3429}with a [crown ]{.class_3429}on his head (although he doesn't wear it much since he has tried appealing to the Communists) claiming to be the "father" (Isa.9:6, John 17:11) of all "Christians" and the chief Bishop over the whole "Church" (1 Pet. 5:3--4).

Think for a minute, brethren. Did [Paul ]{.class_3429}sit on a throne? Did [Peter ]{.class_3429}sit on a throne? Did [Moody ]{.class_3429}or [Spurgeon ]{.class_3429}wear a crown? Of course not. The promise is that when Christ reigns all believers will be ["kings and priests,"]{.class_3428} not just a Roman Catholic spook. The reign hasn't started yet. It won't start until He returns bodily and in power.

Americans are just as bad. They go around singing "The Battle Hymn of the Republic." Don't sing "Mine eyes have seen the glory of the coming of the Lord," when they[ haven't. ]{.class_3429}Or, "He is trampling out the vintage where the grapes of wrath are stored," when they [haven't been stored yet. ]{.class_3429}Or, "He hath loosed the faithful lightning from His terrible swift sword," when He hasn't even [taken it out of its sheath]{.class_3429} yet. Or, "His truth is marching on," when He hasn't even gotten off [His seat yet.]{.class_3429}

I have been up at Beauchamp Vick's church in Detroit and John Rawlings church in Cincinnati when 4,000 people stood up and sang that song. [I sat through the whole thing and kept my mouth shut. ]{.class_3429}I was the only person to do it. I didn't let it bother me at all. What difference is it to me that 4,000 Christians are wrong?

When I tell people that, I always get someone who asks me, "Well, do you think you're right and everyone else is wrong?" In this case, ABSOLUTELY. [There's no question about it.]{.class_3429}

That song is a lie from start to finish. The Lord hasn't come in His glory yet, and "the grapes of wrath" [aren't]{.class_3429} Southern troops. When the Lord treads those "grapes," He will be stomping on the Catholic Church and the United Nations, [not white Southerners.]{.class_3429}

During the Civil War, the colored folk used to sing a song that went like this: "Oh, the master say, 'Ha Ha!' And the Darkies say, 'Ho Ho!' For it must be that the kingdom am a comin' in the year of Jubilo." That was a reference to the [Year of Jubilee]{.class_3429} in the book of Leviticus when all the slaves were set free. Well, the slaves were "set free." Did the "kingdom" come? If it [did, ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_364}then for God's sake kick the "king" off the throne; he's done a [bum job.]{.class_3429}

Verse 2: ["And it was so, when the king saw Esther the queen standing in the court, that she obtained favour in his sight." ]{.class_3428}This is an example of Proverbs 21:1 being fulfilled. The verse says, ["The king's heart is in the hands of the LORD, as the rivers of water: he turneth it whithersoever he will." ]{.class_3428}The same thing took place when Cyrus decreed that the Jews were to return to Jerusalem (Isa. 44:28--45:1).  The Lord works on the king, without his knowledge, to make him favorable to the Lord's cause.

In the New Testament, a Christian is commanded to pray ["for kings, and for all that are in authority; that we may lead a quiet and peaceable life in all godliness and honesty" ]{.class_3428}(1 Tim. 2:1--2). That is important to note. A Christian is never commanded to pray for[ world peace,]{.class_3429} but he is commanded to pray that those in charge will rule in such a way that you can live right and [serve God in peace. ]{.class_3429}That is not a prayer for all wars to cease.

When Esther found favor of the king, he ["held out to Esther the golden scepter that was in his hand." ]{.class_3428}You will remember from Esther 4:11 that the extending of the golden scepter allowed Esther to live when she approached the king unbidden. So God answered the prayers and fasting of Esther and the other Jews.

If you apply this to the New Testament believer, the writer of Hebrews says, ["But unto the Son ]{.class_3428}\[Jesus\] [he ]{.class_3428}\[God\] [saith, Thy throne, O God is for ever and ever: a scepter of RIGHTEOUSNESS is the scepter of thy kingdom" ]{.class_3428}(Heb.1:8). A Christian gets the righteousness of Christ when he accepts the Lord's sacrifice for his sins, so He always has access to the throne room of God. Hebrews 4:16, ["Let us therefore come boldly unto the throne of grace, that we may obtain mercy, and find grace to help in time of need." ]{.class_3428}What Esther had to fast and pray for, we obtain automatically when we receive Christ.

["So Esther drew near, and touched the top of the scepter." ]{.class_3428}This was a symbol that she was acknowledging and receiving the king's favor. It completed the ritual which showed that she was accepted of the king. It is a wonderful picture of a sinner receiving the righteous offered him by God and being ["accepted in the beloved" ]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_365}(Eph. 1:6).

Verse 3: ["Then said the king unto her, What wilt thou, queen Esther? And what is thy request? It shall be even given thee to the half of the kingdom." ]{.class_3428}The king's offer is a figure of speech known as [hyperbole]{.class_3429}. It is an exaggeration used for emphasis; it is not to be taken literally. If Esther had asked for half of the kingdom, he wouldn't have given her all of the country of the Medes to pacify her. If you want to see a similar situation, see what Solomon does in 1 Kings 2:13--25. He told his own mother in verse 20 of that passage that he wouldn't say [no ]{.class_3429}to any request she made---BUT HE [DID ]{.class_3429}(1 Kings 2:22--24)!

You will find numerous examples of hyperbole used in the Bible. The spies told the congregation of Israel that Canaan had ["cities\...walled up to heaven" ]{.class_3428}(Deut. 1:28). Obviously the walls of Jericho weren't built five miles up in the sky. In Numbers 13:33, the spies told the people that the giants in the Land were so big that ["we were in our own sight as grasshoppers." ]{.class_3428}Of course the giants weren't that big. Og of Bashan was only about 13 feet tall, and Goliath only came to around 10 feet. But the word picture painted by such an exaggeration was effective. The children of Israel became so scared of the giants, based on the description of the 10 spies, that they refused to enter the Land.

Now, the only other time in Scripture that the offer of Esther 5:3 is made in those exact words, outside of the book of Esther, is in Mark 6:22--23. There, [Herod ]{.class_3429}made the offer to the daughter of Herodias as a reward for titillating his lusts through a sensuous dance. But you will notice in that story that he added something. He[ swore an oath]{.class_3429} to give her whatever she wanted (Matt. 14:7 cf. Mark 6:23). That is why he complied with her request to behead John the Baptist. He would have "lost face" before all of ["his lords, high captains, and chief estates" ]{.class_3428}if he had not kept his promise.

A little girl sat in a Sunday school class where the teacher told the story of the death of John the Baptist. When the teacher finished the story, the girl asked, "Why did King Herod have to kill John the Baptist if he didn't really want to?" The teacher replied, "Honey, didn't you listen to the story? He promised the dancing girl half of his kingdom." "Well, couldn't he have told her that she could have the half that [John wasn't in?"]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_366} the little girl observed. That's a good sentiment, but it probably wouldn't have worked out too well for Herod. He feared man too much (Prov. 29:25).

The idea behind verse 3 of Esther 5 is that Esther could ask for whatever she wanted, as long as it was within reason. The same idea is behind the great prayer promises that Christ makes in John 14:13--14, 15:16, and 16:24. Paul found out the hard way that the Lord [won't]{.class_3429} just give you anything for which you ask (2 Cor.12:7--9). If you ask for something outside of the directive will of God, don't be surprised if the Lord says "no." James said, ["Ye ask, and receive not, because ye ask amiss, that ye may consume it upon your lusts" ]{.class_3428}(James 4:3). If you ask for something merely to satisfy the desires of the flesh, expect to be turned down.

Brethren, the promises of answered prayer are directed at those things that bring God glory (John 14:13) and that cause us to bear spiritual fruit in our lives (John 15:16) and that bring us joy in the things of God (John 16:20--27) and that allow us to serve the Lord better (2 Cor. 9:8). The Lord may be gracious and merciful and grant some of your requests when they don't quite meet all of those criteria. But don't go around like these stupid Charismatics trying to "name it and claim it." If the Lord gave you everything you wanted, you'd be nothing but a spoiled brat.

Back in Esther 5:4, Esther knows exactly how the king's offer is to be taken, so she prefaces her request with ["If it seem good unto the king." ]{.class_3428}That is how you want to approach God in prayer. It's not "Lord, [I]{.class_3429} want this, and [I ]{.class_3429}want that." It's "Lord, [if it be Thy will ]{.class_3429}please grant me these requests."

[That's what the Charismatics hate. ]{.class_3429}They teach that if you add a condition like that to your prayers that you're not asking ["in faith, nothing wavering" ]{.class_3428}(James 1:6). But notice that James 1:6 has nothing to do with putting any conditions on your prayers. In the context, the verse deals specifically with asking wisdom of God (James 1:5). Even if you broadened the application, the wavering (James 1:7) would be doubting God's [ability]{.class_3429} to answer prayer (Heb.1:6), not asking in the will of God.

The rest of verse 4 and verse 5 are self-explanatory.

5:6 And the king said unto Esther at the banquet of wine, What is thy petition? and it shall be granted thee: and WHAT IS THY REQUEST? even to the half of the kingdom it shall be performed.

7 Then answered Esther, and said, My petition and my request is;

8 If I have found favour in the sight of the king, and if it please the king to grant my petition, and to perform my request, let the king and Haman come to the banquet that I shall prepare for them, and I will do to morrow as the king hath said.

Instead of coming right out and asking the king for her request when the king holds out the golden scepter, Esther invites him and Haman to a private feast. The king is pleased to come, but he knows that Esther has more in mind than just throwing a party for him and his chief of state. So at the banquet the king once more asks her, ["WHAT IS THY PETITION? And it shall granted thee: and what is thy request? even to the half of the kingdom it shall be performed" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 6). 

Esther [still ]{.class_3429}does not reveal her request. Again she invites the king and Haman to another private banquet. One of the reasons she does this is because the third day of fasting was not yet complete. She had asked the Jews to fast for her three days (Esth. 4:16). In chapter 5 verse 1, Esther came to the king ["on the third day." ]{.class_3428}By delaying her request another day, she gave twelve more hours to those who were fasting and praying for her.

5:9 Then went Haman forth that day joyful and with a glad heart: but when Haman saw Mordecai in the king's gate, that he stood not up, nor moved for him, he was full of indignation against Mordecai.

10 Nevertheless Haman refrained himself: and when he came home, he sent and called for his friends, and Zeresh his wife.

11 And Haman told them of the glory of his riches, and the multitude of his children, and all the things wherein the king had promoted him, and how he had advanced him []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_368}above the princes and servants of the king.

12 Haman said moreover, Yea, Esther the queen did let no man come in with the king unto the banquet that she had prepared but myself; and to morrow am I invited unto her also with the king.

13 Yet all this availeth me nothing, so long as I see Mordecai the Jew sitting at the king's gate.

14 Then said Zeresh his wife and all his friends unto him, Let a gallows be made of fifty cubits high, and to morrow speak thou unto the king that Mordecai may be hanged thereon: then go thou in merrily with the king unto the banquet. And the thing pleased Haman; and he caused the gallows to be made.

Another reason that Esther put off her petition until the next day was to give Haman [a false sense of security. ]{.class_3429}She certainly accomplishes that. Verse 9: ["Then went Haman forth that day joyful and with a glad heart." ]{.class_3428}As far as he knows, the only thing that is happening is that, now, he has gained the favor of the queen as well as the king (vss. 11--12). He has no idea that Esther is one of the Jews whom he is seeking to destroy.

As Haman leaves the banquet "on top of the world," he runs into Mordecai at his post ["in the king's gate." ]{.class_3428}While all the other petty officials are bowing and scraping to Haman, there Mordecai sits: he doesn't make a move. He won't rise from his seat to recognize Haman, and he won't bow to reverence him. Mordecai's silence is louder than the blare of the trumpets in the palace.

As we have already noted, Haman had reached the place, in his own fancy, to where his whole day was ruined by one man slighting him. ["He was full of indignation against Mordecai." ]{.class_3428}With everything Haman had "going" for him (vss.11--12), you would think that he could have overlooked Mordecai's "cold shoulder." But in Haman's own words: ["Yet all this availeth me nothing, so long as I see Mordecai the Jew sitting at the king's gate" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 13).

Haman's problem, of course, is [pride]{.class_3429}. He thinks ["of himself more highly than he ought to think"]{.class_3428} (Rom. 12:3). You talk about a man who is stuck on himself! In verse ten, Haman calls all of []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_369}his friends and family together so they can listen to him brag about himself.

Proverbs 16:18 says, ["Pride goeth before destruction, and an haughty spirit before a fall."]{.class_3428} Haman has [God ]{.class_3429}Himself against him: ["God resisteth the proud" ]{.class_3428}(1 Pet. 5:5).

Haman is slowly cutting his own throat inch by inch. He doesn't realize that Esther's invitation is setting him up for the "kill." If that weren't bad enough, his own wife moves him to build the instrument of his own demise.

Verse 14: ["Then said Zeresh his wife and all his friends unto him, Let a gallows be made of fifty cubits high, and tomorrow speak thou unto the king THAT MORDECAI MAY BE HANGED THEREON: then go thou in merrily with the king unto the banquet."]{.class_3428}

Zeresh's attitude is reminiscent of that of Jezebel in 1 Kings 21:7. What Zeresh is basically saying to Haman is: "If you are so rich and powerful and have so much pull with the king, why don't you [do ]{.class_3429}something about Mordecai, instead of just complaining about him. Why wait until the thirteenth of Adar to kill him. Hang him in the morning; then 'party' with the king in the afternoon."

["The gallows"]{.class_3428} which Haman has built turns out to be around 75 feet high: that's seven and a half stories tall. It was probably built on top of a forty foot building. When the story is over, Haman will be hanging on a thirty-five foot "gibbet."

Now, a very common expression comes from that verse: "Give a man enough rope, and he will hang himself." The English language is filled with expressions that come from the Bible. ["He missed the boat;"]{.class_3429} that's from the story of Noah and the Ark. ["Burning the midnight oil;" ]{.class_3429}that's from the parable of The Wise and Foolish Virgins in Matthew 25.  If you what a definitive collection of these expressions get the book [Just Say the Word! ]{.class_3429}from the Bible Baptist Bookstore.

The NEA, the ACLU, and the Supreme Court judges are all trying to remove every last reference to God and the Bible from America's public life. The [King James Bible]{.class_3429} has influenced the English language so much that there's absolutely no way you can do it, so the next best thing is to make sure that the American public is completely ignorant of what the Bible [says. ]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_370}In that way, any cultural references are meaningless.

That's where America is today. No previous generation has been so Biblically illiterate as today's society, and we have the Christian universities, colleges, and seminaries to thank for it. With each new "Bible" that is put on the market, more Americans know less about the Scriptures [because no one knows what the Scriptures say. ]{.class_3429}How can they? [They don't have the Scriptures. ]{.class_3429}All they have are what the scholars call "reliable translations," paraphrases, and "contemporary versions."

At the beginning of World War II, when the British Expeditionary Force was trapped by the Germans at Dunkirk, the British commander sent a message of only three words back to England: ["And if not."]{.class_3429} Those three words were enough to stir the whole of the English people to try and rescue 350,000 besieged English troops.

["And if not"]{.class_3429}?! What in the world was in those [three words]{.class_3429} that could possibly mobilize an entire nation? Do you know? [Why don't you?]{.class_3429}

["But if not" ]{.class_3428}is from the story of the three Hebrew children in the fiery furnace; specifically it is a quotation of Daniel 3:18. Like Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, those "limeys" were willing to be rescued or die fighting. All of England not only recognized that the expression was from the Bible, they knew exactly the passage that matched it and its implication. Don't try it today; you might die of old age before anyone knew what you were talking about.

Back to verse 14: Haman ends up building the gallows on which he will be hung. The contemporary application is: "Where are the gallows on which to hang the modern 'Hamans'?" The answer is that there are not any more [Mordecai]{.class_3429}s: it takes a [Mordecai ]{.class_3429}to get a gallows built.

Now, I am not suggesting that any Christian do anything "nutty" just so he can get himself arrested. We had a fellow come through here one time who did just that. He took a bunch of our guys down to a Catholic church where they proceeded to blow out the candles and mess up the statues. Naturally they were arrested. THEY GOT WHAT THEY DESERVED. I had to get those guys out of jail, and then go down and apologize to that Catholic priest for that incident. I would []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_371}have rather have died than to have had to do that, but it had to be done.

Later on, another of our graduates was invited to go to Zaire by a national pastor to be a missionary. That pastor had gotten that guy a place to stay and a job, and he wanted him to bring his family. The only "catch" was that he was not to bring any guns or military equipment and he wasn't to carry a large amount of cash on his person. Brethren, what more could a missionary ask for when starting a work?

That jerk (and that's exactly what he was) arrived in the capitol with two military-style rifles, survival rations, and ten thousand dollars in cash. Of course they threw him in prison, and they arrested the pastor who was sponsoring him and threw him in prison too. While he was in prison, he won about four Africans to the Lord and then wrote letters back to the United States like he was the Apostle Paul suffering for his faith. He busted up an African church, and that pastor was still in jail when the American embassy got that fellow out and back to the States.

THAT'S NOT WHAT I AM REFERRING TO.

Lester Roloff was a good example of a "Mordecai." He didn't go out of his way to do anything [stupid ]{.class_3429}to get notoriety. All he did was stand up to the Health, Education, and Welfare Department (Roloff called them Hell's Evil Workers) and not let a bunch of  college-educated idiots come in and mess up his kids with TV, fornication, dope, and rock music [like they did in the State homes. ]{.class_3429}If the Lord had let him live another twenty years, you might have seen those State bureaucrats fall by their own devices.

There was a pastor in Nebraska named Sileven. He wouldn't let the State dictate to him how to run his Christian school. They arrested him, padlocked the church, and forced his deacons and their families to flee the state if they didn't want to be arrested. The State of Nebraska treated the members of that church just like the Christians were treated in Communist Russia. That pastor stuck to his position until the newspapers and the major networks finally picked the story up (after avoiding it as long as they could). That fellow didn't get any help to defend his "civil rights" from the ACLU or the NAACP or anyone else. All of this talk about "civil rights" is []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2879.xhtml_page_372}applied to blacks, women, children, faggots, fruits, fairies, lesbians, and double-breasted "finks;" anyone but a [white]{.class_3429}, straight, male, adult, Bible-believing, Protestant, [Baptist CHRISTIAN.]{.class_3429}

Nobody but a few fundamental, Bible-believing Christians stood up for that pastor or his church members. Nobody from the "civil rights" movement opened their cotton-picking mouths. Do you know why? Because that fellow was on a Bible "kick." 

Sileven had a "gallows" built for him, I guarantee you. But God turned that thing around so that now, in Nebraska, there are laws [that allow churches to operate as Sileven was operating]{.class_3429} and not have to apply for the kind of licensing that was being shoved onto Sileven and his church. But someone had to go through all of that trouble first to get the thing done.

Somewhere back in colonial America, there was a Baptist street preacher in Virginia. No one remembers his name or anything particular that he did or said. He was arrested by the British troops [for preaching on the street without a license. ]{.class_3429}Then he was publicly beaten, and that beating later on led to [his death]{.class_3429}. But a member of the Virginia House of Burgesses was passing by, and he witnessed that Baptist street preacher being beaten to death. That man was[ Patrick Henry,]{.class_3429} and that day he made his famous "Give Me Liberty or Give Me Death" speech. That speech led to popular support for the American Revolution, and because of that incident, America had religious freedom for almost 200 years. The British had no idea that when they killed that street preacher that they were beginning to destroy their own empire, but that is exactly how the Lord worked it out.

Now, brethren, the thing to remember is that if you do something for the Lord that makes someone mad enough to "hang" you, get ready to be "hung." The Lord may deliver you, but then He may [not]{.class_3429}. Your [deliverance ]{.class_3429}is not really the important thing. The important thing is for the Lord to use that thing to accomplish [His purpose. ]{.class_3429}You may end up "high and dry" like Mordecai, or you may end up on a cross like your Saviour, but God will use what you did for His glory and [His purpose.]{.class_3429}

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml}

## Chapter 6 {.heading_98-0}

6:1 On that night could not the king sleep, and he commanded to bring the book of records of the chronicles; and they were read before the king.

2 And it was found written, that Mordecai had told of Bigthana and Teresh, two of the king's chamberlains, the keepers of the door, who sought to lay hand on the king Ahasuerus.

3 And the king said, What honour and dignity hath been done to Mordecai for this? Then said the king's servants that ministered unto him, There is nothing done for him.

4 And the king said, Who is in the court? Now Haman was come into the outward court of the king's house, to speak unto the king to hang Mordecai on the gallows that he had prepared for him.

5 And the king's servants said unto him, Behold, Haman standeth in the court. And the king said, Let him come in.

Verse 1 is the night of the [third day]{.class_3429} of Esther 4:16. That night, the king couldn't sleep. The standard joke is if a married man can't sleep, it is either because his wife is having a baby or because his wife has taken the car and gone shopping.

Now, the commentators give all kinds of reasons for Ahasuerus not being able to sleep. Some say he had indigestion or an upset stomach. Others say that God providentially kept him awake. But all of these fail to "hit the nail on the head."

The king has insomnia [because someone has been praying and fasting ]{.class_3429}for three days. It is amazing how that escapes all of these "spiritual" commentators.

Usually prayer has the [opposite affect]{.class_3429} on sleep. If you have trouble getting to sleep, one of the best remedies is [to pray. ]{.class_3429}If you get up and pray, you will get sleepy quicker than by anything else you could do.

One of the hardest things that any Christian has to do is pray. If you don't believe me, try praying 15 minutes straight, by the clock.

Jesus said, ["What, could ye not watch with me one hour?"]{.class_3428} []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_374}(Matt. 26:40). I've known all kinds of brethren in my 55 years of being saved, and I don't know very many Christians that could pray straight for [one hour. ]{.class_3429}Of the ones that could, most of those were bed-ridden or in a wheel chair.

The king's solution is to have the ["records of the chronicles" ]{.class_3428}read to him. He has either made up his mind to get some work done, since he can't sleep, or he is having the most boring thing of which he can think read to him in attempt for it to put him to sleep. Regardless of the reason, it is an answer to prayer. The Lord is leading him in what he is doing. There is something in the "chronicles" that he missed.

It was a common habit in those days for a king to review the chronicles and study them to help to know what to do. That is a very intelligent practice. Every ruler should have a good set of [history books]{.class_3429} and spend most of his time reading and studying [history]{.class_3429}. That will help him see what mistakes were made before and what worked and what [didn't]{.class_3429} work.

Now, there is no disputing that everything in chapter 6 that happens is the providential working of God. When the king has the chronicles read, he just happens to get the chapter that covers the assassination attempt of Esther 2:21--23 (vs.2). That is not an accidental happenstance. The Lord guides the servant who reads the chronicles to cover the [exact portion ]{.class_3429}that will elevate Mordecai's reputation in the eyes of the king---before Haman can ask for Mordecai to be hung.

Verse 3 is a perfect example of 1 Peter 5:6. Back in Esther 2, Mordecai's loyalty went unrewarded. Instead, a wicked man like Haman was exalted (Esth. 3:1). But that is because it was not God's ["due time" ]{.class_3428}to exalt Mordecai. Now (Esth. 6), it is the right time, and we can see why.

The Lord's timing, of course, is impeccable. At the exact moment the king is seeking someone to honor Mordecai, [Haman shows up to have Mordecai hung]{.class_3429} (vs. 4). That's the providential hand of God at work, but that hand is moved by the [prayers of God's people.]{.class_3429}

There are a bunch of Jews in Shushan fasting and praying, "Lord, do something. For God's sake, Lord, help us. Do something for your glory, Lord."
