Those Jews are praying, and it doesn't seem like the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_375}Lord is doing anything. But God is keeping this guy awake, and He is guiding this other guy to pull out and read the right chronicle, and He is taking [another guy]{.class_3429} and bringing him in right [when the chronicle is being read.]{.class_3429}

The Lord cuts that thing awfully close, but He brings everything about at precisely the right moment. Haman had the gallows built. It was just a matter of seconds before he would ask the king to hang Mordecai. If Ahasuerus had been able to get a normal night's sleep, then he never would have had the chronicles read to him, and Mordecai's unrewarded act of loyalty would never have been brought to mind. If the Lord had not been working behind the scenes, things would have turned out a lot different.

Now let that be an encouragement to you to persevere in [prayer]{.class_3429}. The Lord might be doing all kinds of things that you don't [see]{.class_3429}, but are all working to answer your prayer. Unless the Lord gives you a clear [no ]{.class_3429}about a thing, just keep on praying. He hasn't forgotten that you are there. He is just waiting to bring everything together [at the right time]{.class_3429}, which isn't always [our]{.class_3429} time.

6:6 So Haman came in. And the king said unto him, What shall be done unto the man whom the king delighteth to honour? Now Haman thought in his heart, To whom would the king delight to do honour more than to myself?

7 And Haman answered the king, For the man whom the king delighteth to honour,

8 Let the royal apparel be brought which the king useth to wear, and the horse that the king rideth upon, and the crown royal which is set upon his head:

9 And let this apparel and horse be delivered to the hand of one of the king's most noble princes, that they may array the man withal whom the king delighteth to honour, and bring him on horseback through the street of the city, and proclaim before him, Thus shall it be done to the man whom the king delighteth to honour.

10 Then the king said to Haman, Make haste, and take the apparel and the horse, as thou hast said, and do even so []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_376}to Mordecai the Jew, that sitteth at the king's gate: let nothing fail of all that thou hast spoken.

11 Then took Haman the apparel and the horse, and arrayed Mordecai, and brought him on horseback through the street of the city, and proclaimed before him, Thus shall it be done unto the man whom the king delighteth to honour.

12 And Mordecai came again to the king's gate. But Haman hasted to his house mourning, and having his head covered.

Verse 6 shows you how puffed up with his own self-importance Haman really was. When Ahasuerus asked, ["What shall be done unto the man whom the king delighteth to honour," ]{.class_3428}Haman naturally figured that the king must have been talking about [him]{.class_3429}.

That streak of self-centeredness is present in all of us. When we enter a room each of us thinks, "What are these people thinking about [me]{.class_3429}?" But all of those other people are like [us; ]{.class_3429}they are all wondering what you are thinking about [them]{.class_3429}.

When the Lord made people, He made them so that they are the center of their own universe. The soul is sitting in the body receiving all of this information from the outside. [Everything is perceived as to how it relates to the individual perceiving it. ]{.class_3429}That's being [egocentric]{.class_3429}, and [everyone ]{.class_3429}is like that.

In one way it is a good thing that people are self-centered and egotistical and stuck on themselves. When they see Christ and compare themselves with Him, then they see how rotten [they ]{.class_3429}really are, and [they get saved.]{.class_3429}

But at the same time, it is a bad thing as well. You can't really appreciate anything bad that hurts you. If you could look at your troubles as calmly as you look at the troubles of others, then you would be all right. But you can't divorce yourself from [you]{.class_3429}. You're stuck inside your body; it's a prison house. [You are trapped.]{.class_3429}

Buddha saw the problem. The problem was the body. His solution was to ["get out of the frame."]{.class_3429} The Christian solution is to be put into another frame of reference that is not egocentric, and that "frame" is the Holy Spirit.

In verses 7--9, Haman is about to "set himself up" as it were. But what he doesn't know is that everything he is suggesting will be done to [Mordecai]{.class_3429}. So he is "setting himself up," but not in the way he thinks.

There used to be a "game" show on TV years ago called "Queen for a Day." Some housewife would be chosen and brought on the program. The host would bring her on stage and put a crown on her head and a robe on her shoulders and proclaim her "queen for a day." Then she got a bunch of prizes like a new washing machine and dryer or a new refrigerator and a bunch of other junk. That is kind of what Haman is suggesting here.

Haman advices the king to put the royal crown and robe on the "lucky man" and then to have ["one of the king's most noble princes" ]{.class_3428}parade the guy around on the king's horse crying, ["Thus shall it be done to the man whom the king delighteth to honour." ]{.class_3428}The man becomes an honorary "king for a day."

The situation is very similar to Joseph's back in Genesis. ["And Pharaoh said unto Joseph, See, I have set thee over all the land of Egypt. And Pharaoh took off his ring from his hand, and put it upon Joseph's hand, and arrayed him in vestures of fine linen, and put a gold chain about his neck; And he made him to ride in the second chariot which he had; and they cried before him, Bow the knee: and he made him ruler over all the land of Egypt" ]{.class_3428}(Gen. 41:41--43).

It's a picture of the exaltation of Christ in type. [Joseph is a type of Christ. ]{.class_3429}Here, the man about to be exalted is a Jew. Of course, Jesus Christ will be exalted as the King of [the Jews.]{.class_3429}

It is also a partial fulfillment of Deuteronomy 28:13, which is about that Jew: ["And the LORD shall make thee the head, and not the tail; and thou shalt be above only, and thou shalt not be beneath; if thou hearken unto the commandments of the LORD thy God, which I command thee this day, to observe and to do them." ]{.class_3428}Of course the complete fulfillment of that verse won't take place until the Millennium.

Verse 10 blows all of Haman's aspirations out of the window. ["Make haste\...and do even so to Mordecai the Jew\...let nothing fail of all that thou hast spoken." ]{.class_3428}The king thinks []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_378}Haman's idea is wonderful. The catch is Mordecai is the man whom the "king delights to honor," and Haman is the "noble prince" who will lead him around the city.

Now, that's the hand of the Lord moving where it is unmistakable. [None of the characters involved had any control over the circumstances, ]{.class_3429}but it is obvious that the circumstances were being manipulated by [Someone.]{.class_3429}

The king calls Mordecai ["the Jew." ]{.class_3428}The question comes up, then, "Didn't Ahasuerus realize that he had condemned all the Jews to death?" The commentators respond with a statement to this effect: "The king was a fickle and forgetful monarch. He had forgotten that he had given orders to destroy the Jews." But that isn't true. Ahasuerus himself never gave any order to kill the Jews. Go back and read Esther 3:8--9. Haman never told the king [who the people, that were to be destroyed, were. ]{.class_3429}Esther's own ignorance of the decree (in Esth. 4:4--8) shows clearly that Ahasuerus never even saw a copy of the decree himself. Haman kept everything carefully hidden from the king. As far as Ahasuerus knew, there was no connection between [Mordecai ]{.class_3429}and the people that [Haman wanted killed.]{.class_3429}

So Haman had to honor Mordecai in the way that he had prescribed to Ahasuerus. Can you imagine anything more horrible, more ghastly, or more awful for Haman than that? He had to take a man whom he hated with a "purple passion," dress him up in the king's royal garments, and then act as his herald in the city that had just recently been perplexed at Haman's decree against the Jews (Esth. 3:15). If Ahasuerus didn't realize the irony of what was happening, the citizens of Shushan most certainly did. That must have been a terrible ordeal for Haman. I can't see how he lived through it.

The New Testament application is this: ["If any man serve me," ]{.class_3428}Jesus said, ["him will my Father honour" ]{.class_3428}(John 12:26). It must "irk" the brethren something fierce to give credit to somebody God used, when they don't even like that fellow. That must be a terrible blow.

As a Christian, you should avoid that kind of thing. If you find your anger becoming fixated on one fellow, like Swindoll, []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_379}MacArthur, Billy Graham, Bob Jones, or Swaggart, you should draw back and not get too vehement. Don't spend all of your time on the sins and compromises of Billy Graham. Some of the brethren spend 90 percent of their time attacking Billy James Hargis or Carl McIntire or Bill Bright and Campus Crusade.

A lot of the brethren think that I am like that. From time to time I will say something about the compromises of some of my preacher brethren, but I don't get hung up on anything much except [the Book. ]{.class_3429}If they would leave[ the Book]{.class_3429} alone, I won't say much about them.

[I am for anyone God uses in any way He chooses to use him. ]{.class_3429}I wish there were more people God could use. They don't have to believe exactly as I do.

You take someone like John Calvin. That fellow never professed the New Birth a day in his life. You will look in vain for a clear-cut testimony of salvation from John Calvin. But I think the fellow was saved, and [I believe God used him. ]{.class_3429}If God is going to use him, then[ I am in favor of God using him.]{.class_3429}

I have a prayer list of a bunch of my enemies who don't care for me and won't have anything to do with me. Do you know what I pray for them? I pray that God will [use them]{.class_3429}. Bob Jones III is on that list. So are Fred Afman (Tennessee Temple) and James Price (Baptist Bible College). So are Jerry Falwell and Lee Roberson. And up until they died, I had Jack Hyles, Curtis Hutson, and John R. Rice on that list.

Beloved, when it comes to laborers in the harvest and people who will stand up for Him, the Lord is "short-handed." As far as I am concerned, [He can use all the help He can get. ]{.class_3429}If God wants to honor any of those fellows for the work they do for Him, my attitude is: ["to his own master he standeth or falleth. Yea, He shall be holden up: for God is able to make him stand" ]{.class_3428}(Rom. 14:4). It means nothing to me whatsoever.

My problem is [how can I get God to use me]{.class_3429} and [will God use me]{.class_3429}, because [I want God to use me]{.class_3429}. That might be egocentric, but in this case, it is one of the good aspects of being egocentric. In that way I can tend to my own business and leave theirs alone.

Brethren, always remember Romans 14:12. ["So then every one of us shall give account of himself to God." ]{.class_3428}If you keep []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_380}your own account in line with God, you won't have much time to mess around with someone else's account.

Notice in verse 12 the conditions of both of these men. Haman's world has just been shattered. He runs home as fast as he can, miserable, dejected, and humiliated. He covered his head, not only as a sign of mourning, but also so no one in the streets would recognize him and mock him. You see the same thing today on TV news. Some well known person gets arrested for some impropriety, and he covers his head up so that the cameras won't get a shot of his face.

Mordecai, on the other hand, simply takes his post back at ["the king's gate." ]{.class_3428}He doesn't brag to his coworkers or gloat over Haman's humiliation. He doesn't let the king's honor go to his head.

That is something that every Christian should emulate. [If you receive honor from God or man, "take it in stride." ]{.class_3429}Don't take your own "good press" seriously. Men can turn on you in a heartbeat. The same crowd that welcomed Christ into Jerusalem as a conquering king on Palm Sunday was crying for his blood three days later.

Honor from God is good, but if you become puffed up with your own self importance [because of it,]{.class_3429} the Lord will bring you down a notch or two. Some of the "big boys" in the ministry, who have been blessed by God with big churches and outreaches, think that Fundamentalism would collapse without them or their ministries. That's not true. God's always got someone who can take your place and, sometimes, even do a [better job]{.class_3429} than you.

Nobody carries revival around in his pocket---NOBODY. There is no magical little bag of tricks that Christian celebrities have that produces a spiritual work. A spiritual work is done by the Holy Spirit, [not people. ]{.class_3429}No preacher can produce the work that needs to be done in the hearts of people; only the Holy Spirit can do that.

John R. Rice put out an advertisement for a collection of his revival sermons, one time, that said, "These sermons saved 10,000 souls." Shut your blasphemous mouth, you[ lying hypocrite!]{.class_3429} No sermon ever saved [anyone's ]{.class_3429}soul. I have preached the same sermon in two different places, and in one service several people got saved, and in the other nobody even budged. The [sermon ]{.class_3429}had nothing to do with it. [It was the Spirit of God moving in the congregation, using the words of that sermon, to get men saved. ]{.class_3429}There was []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_381}[nothing ]{.class_3429}magical about the sermon.

That is the kind of attitude for which you have to watch out when you have seen some amount of success in Christian work. You begin to think that everything depends on [you]{.class_3429}, and the Lord can't do without [you]{.class_3429}. If you get that way, the Lord will either give a big "let down" to keep you humble, or (even worse) the Holy Spirit will back off and let you live off your reputation for the next 20 to 30 years. That is what has happened to a lot of these big works that are in the Monument stage of their ministries (see chapter 1 of [The History of the New Testament Church, ]{.class_3429}Volume 1).

The best way to look at these matters is this: if humiliation and ridicule come your way, just figure that you got what was coming to you and go on living for God. If you need to get right about something, get it right, but don't become mired in depression because you were shamed. If someone mocks you or humiliates you for Christ's sake, thank God you were able to suffer a little for the Lord, but don't go around bemoaning your circumstances. You haven't fared anywhere nearly as badly as your brethren did in the Middle Ages.

On the other hand, if the Lord prospers you and honors you, thank God for His mercy and blessings on a poor, saved sinner. You know you don't [deserve ]{.class_3429}what you got. Just continue to serve the Lord in humbleness of spirit.

6:13 And Haman told Zeresh his wife and all his friends every thing that had befallen him. Then said his wise men and Zeresh his wife unto him, If Mordecai be of the seed of the Jews, before whom thou hast begun to fall, thou shalt not prevail against him, but shalt surely fall before him.

14 And while they were yet talking with him, came the king's chamberlains, and hasted to bring Haman unto the banquet that Esther had prepared.

Haman goes to his wife and friends and rehearses his troubles to them just as he rehearsed his successes back in Esther 5:10--12. The man is just as self centered and egotistical in his trials and tribulations as he was in his prosperity and good fortune. The topic of conversation and the center of attention has to be [him ]{.class_3429}whether []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA2967.xhtml_page_382}[he ]{.class_3429}is doing well or poorly.

Now, Zeresh and his friends recognize something that never crosses Haman's mind because of his pride. They recognize that Someone is working on Mordecai's behalf. Haman's troubles aren't the result of [chance]{.class_3429} or everyday circumstances. [Someone ]{.class_3429}is causing Haman to fall before Mordecai, and that [Someone ]{.class_3429}is not going to stop until that fall is complete and absolute.

Verse 14 is the beginning of the end for Haman. He doesn't know it yet, but Esther's banquet will be his last meal. He is about to "get it in the neck," literally.

Chapter 6 was the beginning of the fall of Haman (vs. 13). Verse 14 introduces chapter 7 where the Lord finishes bringing Haman down.

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3039.xhtml}

## Chapter 7 {.heading_98-0}

7:1 So the king and Haman came to banquet with Esther the queen.

2 And the king said again unto Esther on the second day at the banquet of wine, What is thy petition, queen Esther? and it shall be granted thee: and what is thy request? and it shall be performed, even to the half of the kingdom.

3 Then Esther the queen answered and said, If I have found favour in thy sight, O king, and if it please the king, let my life be given me at my petition, and my people at my request:

4 For we are sold, I and my people, to be destroyed, to be slain, and to perish. But if we had been sold for bondmen and bondwomen, I had held my tongue, although the enemy could not countervail the king's damage.

5 Then the king Ahasuerus answered and said unto Esther the queen, Who is he, and where is he, that durst presume in his heart to do so?

6 And Esther said, The adversary and enemy is this wicked Haman. Then Haman was afraid before the king and the queen.

Recapping briefly, the story of Esther, in prophetic typology, is the story of Israel being restored as the wife and queen of Jehovah the King. Mordecai is a type of the saved Jewish remnant in the Tribulation. Haman, of course, is a type of Satan; verse 6 of this chapter calls him ["the adversary," ]{.class_3428}which is what the name [Satan ]{.class_3429}means (cf. 1 Pet. 5:8).

[In typology,]{.class_3442} this story fits into two New Testament scenarios, and while you can't press a type [all of the way,]{.class_3442} there are some broad applications that can be made. The first is the parable of the wedding supper in Matthew 22. The king is God the Father; the bride is the restored Jewish nation at the end of the Tribulation; and Haman is the Devil coming in to the wedding feast without a wedding garment and being bound and cast ["into outer darkness."]{.class_3428}

The next picture that you can find here is when the Church is []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3039.xhtml_page_384}caught up to be with the Lord and the Devil can no longer "play both ends against the middle." Right now, you are down here on earth while the Devil comes before the throne and accuses you to the Lord. The reverse is also true: the Devil comes to you and accuses God to you. He's trying to break up your "love affair" with Jesus Christ by telling you how mean and unkind and unloving the Lord is to let things turn out the way they do.

Of course, the Devil has a point both ways. Most of the time when he accuses us, [he's absolutely right. ]{.class_3429}And who hasn't questioned why God does things the way He does? Here's some fornicating, dope-headed rock singer or movie star whose life God cuts short in a violent car wreck or plane crash; then here is some faithful missionary or evangelist who dies in the same way. Does that seem entirely right or fair to you? Of course you have faith to believe in the Lord no matter what He does, but that is easier to [say ]{.class_3429}than [do]{.class_3429}.

The Devil is a spiritual adversary who cuts you down before God and cuts God down before you. But someday, when you are up in Heaven with the Lord and the Devil comes to present himself to the Lord as he did in Job 1, [both you and the Lord will confront the Devil about his accusations at the same time. ]{.class_3429}He won't be able to go behind either of your backs about the other any more. When that happens, out he goes, boy! The Devil is cast completely out of Heaven in Revelation 12, in the middle of the Tribulation.

Now, as chapter 7 opens, God has providentially stacked all of the circumstances against Haman. He is about to stick his head in a noose---[literally. ]{.class_3429}

Once more the king makes his offer to Esther (vs. 2). This time she tells him exactly what she wants. Verse 3: ["let MY LIFE  be given me at my petition." ]{.class_3428}That implies that she is under a death sentence. The king did not know that. She is asking to be allowed to live. ["And MY PEOPLE at my request." ]{.class_3428}She is about to be killed because her people are about to be killed.

["For we are sold, I and my people, to be destroyed, to be slain, and to perish" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 4). The Jews were sold to Haman back in Esther 3:11. Of course, the king had no idea that the Jews were the people whom he had paid Haman to kill. Haman never told him, and the king left the whole matter in Haman's hands.

["But if we had been sold for bondmen and bondwomen, I had held my tongue." ]{.class_3428}If the king had merely made them [slaves ]{.class_3429}as Pharaoh did in the book of Exodus, she wouldn't have said anything. According to Ezra 9:9, that is what they were before the decree of Cyrus for the Jews to return to the Land. It would have been a step back for the Jews, but they could have born it as they had during the seventy years of Babylonian Captivity.

The ["enemy" ]{.class_3428}of verse 4 is defined in verse 6: it is Haman. The word ["countervail" ]{.class_3428}is an archaic word that means "to balance a thing or action; to act against with equal force." Esther is saying that Haman isn't equal to the destruction of the entire Jewish race. She is telling the king what Haman has done so that Ahasuerus will have to choose between keeping [Haman ]{.class_3429}around as his prime minister or having [the queen]{.class_3429} and [her people]{.class_3429} all killed.

Now if you want a good resource for defining archaic words like ["countervail,]{.class_3428}" get the reprinted edition of Noah Webster's 1828 Dictionary (available from the Bookstore). It is a much better dictionary than modern editions. It has most of the old Bible words in it and what they mean in English.

Rather than retranslating and revising what the Bible says [to bring it down to the ignorance of modern Americans, ]{.class_3429}Christians need to do as they were commanded and [study]{.class_3429} the Scriptures. It won't hurt you to look up a word once in a while.

This overwhelming "need" to "update" the Bible is a dangerous thing to do. Once you've begun, where do you stop? If you change one word, then you'll have to change two. If you change two, then you'll have to change ten. Once you change ten, you'll see a hundred more. Pretty soon you've changed 36,000 ([NASV]{.class_3429}), and that still isn't good enough. So you change 64,000 ([NIV]{.class_3429}).

You haven't got [a Bible]{.class_3429} anymore; you've got a billion dollar mess. You have created a market for stupidity where Madison Avenue has to push a "new" Bible every TWO YEARS because "nobody understands a Bible that is 393 years old." Evidently they can't understand one translated two to four years ago either, because that was the excuse for the last 220 versions that were put on the market.

Well, if that is the case, why blow your money down a rat hole by buying the latest piece of warmed-over garbage when you can []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3039.xhtml_page_386}[study the Book God gave you? ]{.class_3429}The problem these days is that Christians have developed an appetite for [hog slop]{.class_3429} (Luke 15:16).

These faculty members from all these Christian schools (it doesn't make a difference which one you name; they are all pretty much the same in their attitudes toward the Book) are some of strangest nuts you ever saw. They all stand in the classroom and correct the [King James Bible]{.class_3429} and recommend all these new "Bibles" on the excuse that none of them affects one single doctrine of the faith. OK, why don't you leave the [AV ]{.class_3429}alone then? After all, [not one obscure word affects any fundamental of the faith!]{.class_3429}

Brethren, "what's good for the goose is good for the gander." People who would strain at the archaic words in a [King James Bible]{.class_3429} and yet swallow the additions, omissions, and outright heresies of the new versions (get the documented evidence in [The Bible Babel, The Christian's Handbook of Biblical Scholarship, Satan's Masterpiece! The New ASV, ]{.class_3429}and Gail Riplinger's [New Age Bible Versions]{.class_3429}; all available from the Bible Baptist Bookstore) are spiritual perverts. They're twisted; they're crooked.

There is no place in the Bible where any archaic word in an [AV ]{.class_3429}messes up [any ]{.class_3429}fundamental doctrine. THEN WHY DON'T THE SCHOLARS LEAVE IT THE WAY IT IS?

Now, you husbands can sympathize with Ahasuerus in verse 5. There are times that you come home and your wife begins to unload some problem on you. You haven't a clue as to what she is complaining about, but she expects you to understand her as if you already know every detail.

Ahasuerus didn't know that Haman had decreed to have the Jews killed because Haman never revealed the identity of the people to the king when he wrote the law. Moreover Ahasuerus didn't know that Esther was a Jew because she kept her nationality a secret at the command of Mordecai. You talk about a lack of communication, brother; that king had it!

Verse 6 identifies Haman as a type of the Devil (["The adversary"---]{.class_3428}1 Pet. 5:8) and the Antichrist (["enemy" ]{.class_3428}as in Pharaoh in Exod. 15 ).

Up until this point, Haman has thought that he had the queen's favor. Suddenly she is calling him her [enemy ]{.class_3429}and [wicked]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3039.xhtml_page_387}. Don't you know that was a "shocker" to Haman.

7:7 And the king arising from the banquet of wine in his wrath went into the palace garden: and Haman stood up to make request for his life to Esther the queen; for he saw that there was evil determined against him by the king.

8 Then the king returned out of the palace garden into the place of the banquet of wine; and Haman was fallen upon the bed whereon Esther was. Then said the king, Will he force the queen also before me in the house? As the word went out of the king's mouth, they covered Haman\'s face.

9 And Harbonah, one of the chamberlains, said before the king, Behold also, the gallows fifty cubits high, which Haman had made for Mordecai, who had spoken good for the king, standeth in the house of Haman. Then the king said, Hang him thereon.

10 So they hanged Haman on the gallows that he had prepared for Mordecai. Then was the king's wrath pacified.

In verse 7, the king is so angry that he has to leave the banquet and take a walk to regain control of his temper. If he stays, he is liable to "punch somebody out." Sometimes, that's the best way to handle an out-of-control temper: just get up and walk away from a volatile situation.

The only hope that Haman sees now is to make things right with Esther. As we saw back in Esther 1, when folks ate back then, they reclined on [couches]{.class_3429}. That couch is called a ["bed"]{.class_3428} in verse 8. As Haman begs for mercy, he throws himself down on the couch where Esther is lying. Undoubtedly he is grasping her hands or her feet as he pleads for clemency. At that moment the king returns to the room and takes one look at the scene. [There is Haman pawing at his wife,]{.class_3429} and Esther is probably struggling to get free of his grasp. Based on that "circumstantial evidence," Ahasuerus "puts two and two together," and figures that Haman is trying to rape the queen in her own house. Of course that is not what was happening, but the king was so mad that he couldn't "see straight."

["As the word went out of the king's mouth, they covered Haman's face." ]{.class_3428}The guards come in and put a sack over Haman's head. The idea behind that is that Haman is no longer worthy to look on the king's face.

If you picked up all the standard commentaries, they would tell you that "this was an [ancient]{.class_3429} custom [in Persia ]{.class_3429}when a prisoner was about to be executed." But the Bible is much more up-to-date than that. It is a universal custom[ in any time period]{.class_3429} to cover a person's head when he is about [to be hung]{.class_3429}. It wasn't relegated to ancient Persia. The [King James Bible]{.class_3429} "sets the pace." It tells men what to do, and they do it whether they know it or not and whether they believe it or not.

When the assassins of Abraham Lincoln were hung, [they placed a black hood over their heads. ]{.class_3429}Those Nazis that were condemned and executed at Nuremberg had a [black cape placed over their faces. ]{.class_3429}When a person is going to have his neck broken on the gallows, he has to climb thirteen steps. It would have to be thirteen; it couldn't be anything else. [The Bibles sets down thirteen as a bad number, and men follow it. The Bible is the law maker.]{.class_3429}

The ["Harbonah" ]{.class_3428}of verse 9 is one of ["the seven chamberlains that served in the presence of Ahasuerus the king" ]{.class_3428}back in Esther 1:10. In that verse the name is spelled without the [h ]{.class_3429}at the end of the name. Here in Esther 7:9, Harbonah informs the king of the gallows Haman had built to hang Mordecai.

The word ["house" ]{.class_3428}in verse 9 is not a reference to the structure in which Haman lived. The fellow didn't have an eighty-foot-high ceiling. The word is used here as it is used in Acts 16:31. It means the household of Haman. Look at Esther 8:2. ["And Esther set Mordecai over the house of Haman." ]{.class_3428}Well, Mordecai wasn't sitting on the thirty-five foot flagpole on the top of Haman's house. Obviously he was put in charge of all the people and goods that belonged to Haman.

When Ahasuerus hears about the gallows, he renders a verdict then and there: ["Hang him thereon." ]{.class_3428}Haman had no trial or jury or appeal. As we have already observed, those Oriental kings had power. They were like that queen in [Alice in Wonderland]{.class_3429}. When they cried, "Off with his head!" someone's head was coming off whether []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3039.xhtml_page_389}there was any trial or not.

Hanging is quite a means of capital punishment. The last person to be officially hung in the United States died in 1963 in a state prison in Iowa. The last public hanging was in 1936 in Owensboro, Kentucky. The media had it stopped because it was "offensive to refined sensibilities." They then proceeded to produce such wonderful cultural works like [Halloween]{.class_3429}, [Nightmare on Elm Street]{.class_3429}, [Friday the 13th]{.class_3429}, [Night of the Living Dead]{.class_3429}, [Psycho]{.class_3429}, etc., that have portrayed torture, mutilation, beheadings, cannibalism, and sex murders right in the living rooms of "civilized, refined" Americans. What a bunch of "fine, upright, honest, noble" people!

[I think hanging is good. ]{.class_3429}I think someone like Charles Manson ought to be hung [publicly]{.class_3429}. Take the sucker out where a few thousand people can see what's going on, pull the lever to the trap door, and let everyone watch him "dance on air." Then leave the body there for about[ two days]{.class_3429} with a big sign under it that says: ["The wages of sin is death."]{.class_3428}

You say, "Ruckman, how you talk!" No kidding, man, that will cut down your crime rate. Would you rather have the crime or your [unoffended sensibilities?]{.class_3429} Some punk will think twice about committing a murder after he sees that rotting carcass swinging in the breeze.

Verse 10 is a fulfillment of Psalm 9:15--16. ["The heathen are sunk down in the pit THAT THEY MADE: IN THE NET WHICH THEY HID IS THEIR OWN FOOT TAKEN. The LORD is known by the judgment which he executeth: the wicked is snared in the work of his own hands." ]{.class_3428}If you spend your time plotting to get someone and you have all these carefully laid plans for revenge, the Lord will work that thing out so that you will fall prey to your own devices. You will get caught in your own net, and you will strangle in the plans you made. You will not only reap what you sow; you will reap [more ]{.class_3429}than you sow.

You had better leave vengeance to the Lord. If He doesn't "get" them, then you were in the wrong to start with, and if He does, He will always do a better job of it than [you ]{.class_3429}could have done. The best thing you could do is to take your enemies and turn them over to the Lord and ask Him to "get" them.

Haman got hung on the very gallows he had built to get rid of Mordecai. Psalm 9:16 says that that was the judgment of God. It was brought about by a bunch of Jews praying and fasting, not by [scheming ]{.class_3429}and [conniving]{.class_3429}.

[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3091.xhtml}

## Chapter 8 {.heading_98-0}

8:1 On that day did the king Ahasuerus give the house of Haman the Jews' enemy unto Esther the queen. And Mordecai came before the king; for Esther had told what he was unto her.

2 And the king took off his ring, which he had taken from Haman, and gave it unto Mordecai. And Esther set Mordecai over the house of Haman.

Haman is now dead, and the king's anger is ["pacified"]{.class_3428} (Esth. 7:10). Ahasuerus turns everything that belonged to Haman over to Esther (vs. 1). Esther, in turn, made Mordecai the steward over Haman's household (vs. 2). At the same time, Esther tells her husband that Mordecai is her cousin and adoptive father (Esth. 2:7).

So now, the king finally promotes Mordecai as he should have back in Esther 3:1. There the king promoted Haman after Mordecai had saved the king from an assassination plot: Haman had been made the prime minister and had been given the right to make laws in the king's name (Esth. 3:10). In verse 2, Ahasuerus gives his signet ring to Mordecai. So not only is Mordecai placed in charge of everything Haman owns, he is given Haman's position in the kingdom. [Everything that Agagite had became Jewish property.]{.class_3429}

That is a picture of the Jews being restored and their "fullness" coming in. When that happens the riches of the Gentiles are turned over to the Jews. That time is described in two chapters in the Old Testament: Isaiah 65--66.

It will take place during the Millennium. During the Millennium, the Jew will have charge of all the Devil's property and people. The Jew will be on top; Jerusalem will be the capitol of the world; and the ["King of the Jews"]{.class_3428} will be the [supreme Dictator.]{.class_3442}

8:3 And Esther spake yet again before the king, and fell down at his feet, and besought him with tears to put away the mischief of Haman the Agagite, and his device that he had devised against the Jews.

4 Then the king held out the golden sceptre toward Esther. So Esther arose, and stood before the king,

5 And said, If it please the king, and if I have found favour in his sight, and the thing seem right before the king, and I be pleasing in his eyes, let it be written to reverse the letters devised by Haman the son of Hammedatha the Agagite, which he wrote to destroy the Jews which are in all the king\'s provinces:

6 For how can I endure to see the evil that shall come unto my people? or how can I endure to see the destruction of my kindred?

Esther once more comes before the king unbidden. This time she is not afraid for her own life. Her concern is only for her people (vs. 3).

Again ["the king held out the golden scepter toward Esther" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 4). He approved of her; he accepted her. She came in groveling and crying (vs. 3), but the presentation of the king's scepter allows her to stand before Ahasuerus and present her case for the Jews.

Verse 5 once again gives some wonderful pictures of approaching God in prayer.

1)[​]{.class_3445}["If it please the king." ]{.class_3428}The first thing is to ask in the will of God.

2)[​]{.class_3445}["If I have found favour in his sight." ]{.class_3428}You have to be ["accepted in the beloved" ]{.class_3428}(Eph. 1:6).

3)[​]{.class_3445}["And the thing seem right before the king." ]{.class_3428}The Lord won't answer a prayer to ["consume it upon your lusts" ]{.class_3428}(James 4:3).

4)[​]{.class_3445}["And I be pleasing in his eyes." ]{.class_3428}The New Testament application is 1 John 3:22. ["And whatsoever we ask, we receive of him, because we keep his commandments, and do those things that are pleasing in his sight."]{.class_3428}

Those are all the resources you need to get a prayer answered. You need to be [saved]{.class_3429}, ask in God's [will]{.class_3429}, ask for something that is ["right" ]{.class_3428}in God's sight, and [please God ]{.class_3429}as you ask and with what you ask.

Now, Esther's request is for the king to repeal the law that Haman passed. But as we have already seen in Esther 1:19, once a law had been sealed with the king's signet ring it could not be changed. The law Haman passed to destroy the Jews was irreversible.

8:7 Then the king Ahasuerus said unto Esther the queen and to Mordecai the Jew, Behold, I have given Esther the house of Haman, and him they have hanged upon the gallows, because he laid his hand upon the Jews.

8 Write ye also for the Jews, as it liketh you, in the king's name, and seal it with the king's ring: for the writing which is written in the king's name, and sealed with the king's ring, may no man reverse.

9 Then were the king's scribes called at that time in the third month, that is, the month Sivan, on the three and twentieth day thereof; and it was written according to all that Mordecai commanded unto the Jews, and to the lieutenants, and the deputies and rulers of the provinces which are from India unto Ethiopia, an hundred twenty and seven provinces, unto every province according to the writing thereof, and unto every people after their language, and to the Jews according to their writing, and according to their language.

10 And he wrote in the king Ahasuerus' name, and sealed it with the king\'s ring, and sent letters by posts on horseback, and riders on mules, camels, and young dromedaries:

11 Wherein the king granted the Jews which were in every city to gather themselves together, and to stand for their life, to destroy, to slay, and to cause to perish, all the power of the people and province that would assault them, both little ones and women, and to take the spoil of them for a prey,

12 Upon one day in all the provinces of king Ahasuerus, namely, upon the thirteenth day of the twelfth month, which is the month Adar.

13 The copy of the writing for a commandment to be []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3091.xhtml_page_394}given in every province was published unto all people, and that the Jews should be ready against that day to avenge themselves on their enemies.

14 So the posts that rode upon mules and camels went out, being hastened and pressed on by the king's commandment. And the decree was given at Shushan the palace.

Although ["the law of the Medes and Persians" ]{.class_3428}could not be changed or repealed, [it could be countered with another unalterable law. ]{.class_3429}The king's solution to the problem is to let Mordecai and Esther "write their own ticket" concerning the fate of the Jewish people. And although he is not going to tell them what to write, he has given them [an example ]{.class_3429}in what he did to Haman (vs. 7).

In the New Testament, the writer of Hebrews says that the counsel and oaths of God are ["immutable" ]{.class_3428}(Heb. 6:17--18); that is, they do not change. The Persian law mentioned in Ezra, Nehemiah, Esther, and Daniel is a type of these things. When God lays down a counsel as a set thing or when God swears an oath about a thing, He is not going to change it no matter how much compassion or love or regret He has in the matter.

For instance, no matter how angry the Lord may become at the Jews, [He swore an oath to Abraham to give his seed, through Isaac and Jacob, all the land of Canaan]{.class_3429} (Gen. 15:18--21, 26:2--4, 28:13--14). If He became so angry with the Jews that [He killed all of them,]{.class_3429} He would never give Palestine to any Moslem, Arab, or "Christian." [The Lord would make sure to keep at least one last Jew alive to fulfill His oath to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob]{.class_3429} (Exod. 32:10).

Spiritually speaking, God will [not ]{.class_3429}violate His counsel or oath against sin or sinners (Gen. 2:17; Ezek. 18:4, 20; Rom. 5:12,21, 6:23)---no matter how much He loves them. [Someone is going to have to die because of your sins. ]{.class_3429}If it is not you, then you need someone else, someone who has no sin of his own for which to die, to die for you.

[God won't take anybody to Heaven just because He loves them. ]{.class_3429}He may [counter]{.class_3429} His decree of death because He loves sinners, [but He will not disannul it.]{.class_3429}

["The gift of God is eternal life through Jesus Christ our Lord" ]{.class_3428}is how God offsets ["For the wages of sin is death." ]{.class_3428}You take one immutable law, or you take the other.

I'll tell you something else: once God has saved you and placed you in Christ, you are placed under an [immutable promise]{.class_3429} that God will get you home to Heaven no matter what (1 Cor. 1:8, Eph. 4:30, Phil. 1:6). After salvation, nothing about your eternal destiny depends on [you ]{.class_3429}(Rom. 8:29--39). There is no "conditional security of the believer" to it. The promise of salvation in the Church Age is so strong that nothing can countermand it once you have it.

Back in Esther 8, Mordecai counters Haman's decree by allowing the Jews to defend themselves and kill whoever attacks them (vs. 11). They are also granted the right to "spoil" those they kill. In other words, they may take the property of those that attack them to recompense them for the[ expenses of going to war.]{.class_3429}

As it turns out, the Jews leave the spoil alone. Esther 9:10, ["But on the spoil laid they not their hand." ]{.class_3428}Esther 9:15, ["But on the prey they laid not their hand." ]{.class_3428}Esther 9:16, ["But they laid not their hands on the prey." ]{.class_3428}Three times the Scriptures say that they didn't take advantage of the second part of Mordecai's decree.

Now, there is a reason for that. Haman was an [Agagite,]{.class_3429} and the Agagites were descendants of the king of the [Amalekites ]{.class_3429}during the reign of Saul in Israel. Back in 1 Samuel 15, the Lord told Saul and the Israelites to ["utterly]{.class_3428} [destroy"]{.class_3428} everything that Amalek had. They were not to take any spoil at all, but they did. [That is how the Agagites survived.]{.class_3429}

So when they get the chance to spoil a bunch of people who follow the orders of an Agagite, they refuse to take the spoil. [They are atoning for their disobedience in 1 Samuel 15.]{.class_3429}

Verse 12 is one of those rare verses that contains a good "13" in the Bible. But still you have to watch out for it even then. Originally it was a bad thirteen (Esth. 3:13) until God reversed it. And although God made it a good thirteen for the Jews, [it became a bad one for anyone who lifted a finger against them.]{.class_3429}

There is a great lesson there for a child of God. When people read or hear me speak of thirteen being bad, that's very true. In the Bible []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3091.xhtml_page_396}west to east is a bad direction. We have had plenty of missionaries, though, who have left our church to start a ministry in Europe. Well, that's west to east; what do you do with that?

Here's the thing to remember about things in the Scriptures that are characteristically bad, like [thirteen]{.class_3429}, west to east, and "words that end in [x]{.class_3429}." Those things are there for your instruction. They are not meant to guide you in [every decision of life. ]{.class_3429}They are to let you know something.

If a thirteen is involved, [be careful. ]{.class_3442}If a move from west to east is involved, [be careful. ]{.class_3442}But that kind of stuff isn't a curse on you. The Christian has a promise from God that [overrides ]{.class_3442}those things. Romans 8:28, ["And we know that ALL THINGS work together for good to them that love God, to them who are the called according to his purpose."]{.class_3428}

A thirteen can't "hex" you, but you ought to notice it and be wary of it. That happens to me all the time on flights. I am as superstitious as I can be. I notice the gate number, the flight number, the time of departure, the number on the fuselage of the plane, and the number of my seat. I have been on flights where the gate number added up to thirteen and the number on the plane added up to thirteen and the seat number was six. When I get into a situation like that, I do a lot of praying, [but I don't cancel the flight.]{.class_3429}

Now, in regard to the situation between the Jews and their enemies in the book of Esther, Psalm 76:10 says, ["Surely the wrath of man shall praise thee: the remainder of wrath shalt thou restrain." ]{.class_3428}God turned the wicked plan of Haman around so that the Jews ended up having another feast to the Lord. What was going to be the complete extermination of the Jewish race, God restrained down to nothing.

The application to the Christian is this: your enemies' anger against you and the Devil's hatred of you and the persecution you get from unsaved people and all of the Devil's attempts to shut you up and close your mouth and mess up your life may affect you. But God will take [those things]{.class_3429} and turn them to His own praise.

Before moving on to the next passage, the reader should note two more things about these verses. First, verse 9 is [the longest verse in the King James Bible. ]{.class_3429}The verse contains every letter in the English alphabet except [q]{.class_3429}, [x]{.class_3429}, and[ z]{.class_3429}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3091.xhtml_page_397}. That's one of those interesting bits of trivia about the Bible. There's not much you can do with it, but there it is.

The second thing is a little more practical and challenging. In my comments on Esther 1:22, I told you that there were [three ]{.class_3429}universal decrees in the book of Esther. Mordecai's decree here in these verses is the last of those decrees. Doctrinally, this decree is associated with the ["gospel of the kingdom" ]{.class_3428}which is universally preached in the Tribulation. But I would like to look make a devotional application for a moment to ["the gospel of the grace of God" ]{.class_3428}which is being preached now in the Church Age.

The decree of Mordecai was translated into all the languages of ["every people\...from India unto Ethiopia" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 9). In less than one year, three decrees were [translated into anywhere from 127 to 365 languages. ]{.class_3429}If a bunch of unsaved translators can do that for a heathen king, certainly a billion professing Christians can take the Gospel to the whole world after nearly 2,000 years.

No other generation of Christians has had the ability to get the Gospel to ["every kindred, and tongue, and people, and nation" ]{.class_3428}(Rev. 5:9) like we do today. [Of the world's 6,528 languages, over 2,000 have some part of the Bible. ]{.class_3429}The basic Gospel message has been translated and made available on cassette in 4,562 languages. The "Jesus" film has been translated into almost [300 languages]{.class_3429} which each have a million speakers or more and has been viewed by nearly [a half a billion people. ]{.class_3429}There are 13 large mission agencies that broadcast Gospel programming around the world by radio in [211 languages]{.class_3429} that each has over a million speakers. Enough Gospel literature is printed every year to give a tract to every person on the globe and to put a New Testament in every home.

Yet with everything that is going on we have still not reached everyone with the Gospel. [The problem is that a lot of Christians aren't going. ]{.class_3429}They aren't going with their prayers; they aren't going with their money; they aren't going where the need is the greatest.

Verse 14 says that the posts that carried Mordecai's decree were ["hastened and pressed on by the king's commandment." ]{.class_3428}Most Christians have no sense of [urgency ]{.class_3429}in regards to getting the []{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3091.xhtml_page_398}Gospel out at all. If Mordecai's decree had been treated like most Christians treat the Gospel message, the posts would not have arrived until a week after the Jews were massacred.

Brethren, at 83 years old, my philosophy isn't to retire. I might not be able to travel as much as I did, but with whatever strength, time, and ability I have left, I am going to "put the pedal to the metal" (CB jargon from the 80s) for Jesus Christ.

Of course at my age I have had to slow down quite a bit in order to accomplish what I have to do. I have now had to give up hockey and "blood ball" so that I wouldn't lose my eyesight. I have more proofreading now than I have ever had before. I have also had to cut back on my traveling. Well, if I can't go myself, I am going to do everything I can [to persuade others to go;]{.class_3429} I am going to do everything [I can]{.class_3429} to make sure those who have gone [stay on the field.]{.class_3429}

In 2004 the Bible Baptist Church increased its missionary support. Frankly I don't know where the money comes from. All we have is a bunch of "po' folks" here who struggle to pay the rent, to keep gas in the car, to take the kids to the doctor, and to stay in school. All I know is that the price of living keeps rising and the dollar keeps falling and the Lord needs someone to keep those missionaries on the field. Since our young men are often ostracized by the "dearly beloved brethren" because they are associated with me, we are going to do all we can to help them out. If we ever "bite off more than we can chew," then we may have to cut back. But until then it's forward, brother, FORWARD!

8:15 And Mordecai went out from the presence of the king in royal apparel of blue and white, and with a great crown of gold, and with a garment of fine linen and purple: and the city of Shushan rejoiced and was glad.

16 The Jews had light, and gladness, and joy, and honour.

17 And in every province, and in every city, whithersoever the king's commandment and his decree came, the Jews had joy and gladness, a feast and a good day. And many of the people of the land became Jews; for the fear of the Jews fell upon them.

Notice in verse 15 that Mordecai retains the honor the king gave him in Esther 6:8. He is arrayed for all intents and purposes as a king. That's a picture of those Jews who will be killed in the Tribulation for not bowing down and worshipping the Antichrist and his image.

Look at Revelation 20:4. ["And I saw thrones, and they sat upon them, and judgment was given unto them: and I saw the souls of them that were beheaded for the witness of Jesus, and for the word of God, and which had not worshipped the beast, neither his image, neither had received his mark upon their foreheads, or in their hands; and they lived and reigned with Christ a thousand years."]{.class_3428}

Those Jews face the Antichrist, just like Mordecai faces Haman. [They won't bow down to him, just like Mordecai won't bow to Haman. ]{.class_3442}They are dressed like the king and are given His authority after the destruction of the Antichrist, just like Mordecai[ ]{.class_3428}in Esther 8:15.

In the Millennium, there are three groups that end up reigning with Jesus Christ. There are the [twelve apostles of the Lamb. ]{.class_3429}They end up on ["twelve thrones, judging the twelve tribes of Israel" ]{.class_3428}(Matt. 19:28). They are part of a larger group of disciples in the gospels who forsook everything to follow Christ while He was here on earth. Then there are those who refuse to follow the Antichrist and are [beheaded ]{.class_3429}during the Tribulation (Rev. 20:4). And finally there are Church Age Christians who ["occupy" ]{.class_3428}this world until Christ returns (Luke 19:13) with the Gospel given to the Apostle Paul (Gal. 1:11--17; see comments on page 311 of [The Bible Believer's Commentary on 1 & 2 Corinthians]{.class_3429}, Bible Baptist Bookstore, 2002). Jesus makes those Christians who love and serve Him faithfully during their lifetimes ["kings and priests unto God and his Father"]{.class_3428} (Rev. 1:6, 5:9--10).

["And the city of Shushan rejoiced and was glad." ]{.class_3428}Proverbs 29:2 says, ["When the righteous are in authority, the people rejoice: but when the wicked beareth rule, the people mourn." ]{.class_3428}That is exactly what happened in Shushan in the book of Esther. Haman and his decree brought perplexity (Esth. 3:15) and mourning (Esth. 4:1--3). Mordecai and his decree brought rejoicing and gladness (Esth. 8:15--16).

The ["light" ]{.class_3428}[]{#I1HHcIZkQh_UMLBZXzVcAA3091.xhtml_page_400}of verse 16 is the lighting of lamps in celebration. We do the same thing with Christmas lights. The Chinese use paper lanterns. The ultimate expression would be fireworks.

["And many of the people of the land became Jews; for the fear of the Jews fell upon them" ]{.class_3428}(vs. 17). [Those are converts to Judaism. ]{.class_3429}That is a bunch of Gentiles who are honoring the Jews now that Mordecai is in charge (vs. 16). After seeing what happens to Haman, they are so scared of being on the losing side that they get circumcised and go down and join the synagogue.

The Gentiles saw that the Jews now had royal backing. A lot of the Gentiles defected over to the Jews because of that. Some of them may have recalled the decree of Darius in Daniel 6:26. ["In every dominion of my kingdom men tremble and fear before the God of Daniel: for he is the living God."]{.class_3428}

Now, these Gentiles didn't become [racial]{.class_3429} Jews. They weren't born to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. But they followed Abraham in circumcision and began to follow Jehovah as God and live under the covenant of the Law given to Israel.

In the Bible, "a Jew" can be one of three things:

1\. If a man is a [descendant ]{.class_3429}of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, he is a Jew---[racially, physically]{.class_3429}.

2\. If a man is saved and born again, he is a [spiritual]{.class_3429} Jew, but not a [physical Jew.]{.class_3429}

3\. If a Gentile joins Judaism as a [proselyte ]{.class_3429}(like Sammy Davis Jr. did), then he is counted as a Jew, but he is neither a spiritual nor a physical Jew. He's a [religious]{.class_3429} Jew.

People are always arguing whether the Jews are a religion or a race. The answer to both is [yes]{.class_3429}. A Jew can be born [physically ]{.class_3429}into the literal Jewish race, or a Jew can be a Gentile who renounces his Gentile heritage and [adopts the Jewish religion.]{.class_3429}

Besides those two ways, a Jew can also be any man, woman, or child who enters into a [spiritual relationship]{.class_3429} with Jesus Christ. [That has nothing to do with either a physical birth or a religion.]{.class_3429}
